Parsing [sent. 213 len. 21]: It was during a painful march through the desert with one of the caravans , that a favourite she-camel foaled .
Parsing [sent. 214 len. 43]: At first it was my intention to leave the young one to its fate , as my camels had already suffered much ; but , on examination , the creature showed such strength and symmetry that I resolved to bring it up .
Parsing [sent. 215 len. 30]: I therefore divided half of one of the loads between the other camels , and tied the foal upon the one which I had partly relieved for the purpose .
Parsing [sent. 216 len. 31]: We arrived safely at Cairo ; and , as the little animal grew up , I had more than ever reason to be satisfied that I had saved its life .
Parsing [sent. 217 len. 35]: All good judges considered it a prodigy of beauty and strength ; and prophesied that it would some day be selected as the holy camel to carry the Koran in the pilgrimage to Mecca .
Parsing [sent. 218 len. 28]: And so it did happen about five years afterwards , during which interval I accompanied the caravans as before ; and each year added to my wealth .
Parsing [sent. 219 len. 47]: My camel had by this time arrived to his full perfection ; he stood nearly three feet higher than any other ; and , when the caravan was preparing , I led him to the sheiks , and offered him as a candidate for the honour .
Parsing [sent. 220 len. 48]: They would have accepted him immediately , had it not been for a maribout , who , for some reason or another , desired them not to employ him , asserting that the caravan would be unlucky if my camel was the bearer of the holy Koran .

Parsing [sent. 224 len. 16]: The consequence was , that an inferior camel was selected , and I was disappointed .

Parsing [sent. 254 len. 51]: The splendid tent of the emir , which first submitted to the blast , passed close to me , flying along with the velocity of the herie , while every other was either levelled to the ground or carried up into the air , and whirled about in mad gyration .

Parsing [sent. 256 len. 77]: But the simoom had not yet poured upon us all its horrors : in a few minutes nothing was to be distinguished -- all was darkness , horrible darkness , rendered more horrible by the ravings of dying men , the screams of women , and the mad career of horses and other animals , which breaking their cords , trod down thousands in their endeavours to escape from the overwhelming fury of the desert storm .

Parsing [sent. 398 len. 16]: I am a Greek by birth ; my parents were poor people residing at Smyrna .
Parsing [sent. 399 len. 21]: I was an only son , and brought up to my father 's profession , -- that of a cooper .

Parsing [sent. 401 len. 41]: I had been for some time in the employ of a Jewish wine-merchant , and I continued there for three years after my father 's death , when a circumstance occurred which led to my subsequent prosperity and present degradation .
Parsing [sent. 402 len. 63]: At the time that I am speaking of , I had , by strict diligence and sobriety , so pleased my employer , that I had risen to be his foreman ; and although I still superintended and occasionally worked at the cooperage , I was intrusted with the drawing off and fining of the wines , to prepare them for market .
Parsing [sent. 403 len. 56]: There was an Ethiopian slave , who worked under my orders , a powerful , broad-shouldered , and most malignant wretch , whom my master found it almost impossible to manage ; the bastinado , or any other punishment , he derided , and after the application only became more sullen and discontented than before .
Parsing [sent. 404 len. 35]: The fire that flashed from his eyes , upon any fault being found by me on account of his negligence , was so threatening , that I every day expected I should be murdered .
Parsing [sent. 405 len. 51]: I repeatedly requested my master to part with him ; but the Ethiopian being a very powerful man , and able , when he chose , to move a pipe of wine without assistance , the avarice of the Jew would not permit him to accede to my repeated solicitations .
Parsing [sent. 406 len. 35]: One morning I entered the cooperage , and found the Ethiopian fast asleep by the side of a cask which I had been wanting for some time , and expected to have found ready .

Parsing [sent. 576 len. 62]: I drew some of my best -- `` This , honourable sir , '' said I , presenting the glass , `` is what I call my aga wine : the late aga was so fond of it , he used to order a whole cask at once to his house , and had it taken there in a litter . ''
Parsing [sent. 577 len. 45]: `` A good plan , '' replied the cadi , `` much better than sending a slave with a pitcher , which gives occasion for remarks : I will do the same ; but , first , let me taste all you have . ''
Parsing [sent. 578 len. 19]: He tasted several casks , but none pleased him so much as the first which I had recommended .
Parsing [sent. 579 len. 15]: At last he cast his eyes upon the three casks raised above the others .
Parsing [sent. 580 len. 7]: `` And what are those ? ''
Parsing [sent. 581 len. 3]: inquired he .
Parsing [sent. 582 len. 24]: `` Empty casks , sir , '' replied I ; but he had his stick in his hand , and he struck one .
Parsing [sent. 583 len. 38]: `` Greek , thou tellest me these casks are empty , but they do not sound so ; I suspect that thou hast better wine than I have tasted : draw me off from these immediately . ''
Parsing [sent. 584 len. 25]: I was obliged to comply -- he tasted them -- vowed that the wine was exquisite , and that he would purchase the whole .
Parsing [sent. 585 len. 32]: I stated to him that the wine in those casks was used for flavouring the rest ; and that the price was enormous , hoping that he would not pay it .
Parsing [sent. 586 len. 17]: He inquired how much -- I asked him four times the price of the other wines .
Parsing [sent. 587 len. 32]: `` Agreed , '' said the cadi ; `` it is dear -- but one can not have good wine without paying for it : -- it is a bargain . ''
Parsing [sent. 588 len. 62]: I was very much alarmed ; and stated that I could not part with those casks , as I should not be able to carry on my business with reputation , if I lost the means of flavouring my wines , but all in vain ; he said that I had asked a price and he had agreed to give it .
Parsing [sent. 589 len. 39]: Ordering his slaves to bring a litter , he would not leave the store until the whole of the casks were carried away , and thus did I lose my Ethiopian , my Jew , and my aga .
Parsing [sent. 590 len. 21]: As I knew that the secret would soon be discovered , the very next day I prepared for my departure .
Parsing [sent. 591 len. 42]: I received my money from the cadi , to whom I stated my intention to leave , as he had obliged me to sell him those wines , and I had no longer hopes of carrying on my business with success .
Parsing [sent. 592 len. 33]: I again begged him to allow me to have them back , offering him three pipes of wine as a present if he would consent , but it was of no use .
Parsing [sent. 593 len. 36]: I chartered a vessel , which I loaded with the rest of my stock ; and , taking all my money with me , made sail for Corfu , before any discovery had taken place .
Parsing [sent. 594 len. 34]: But we encountered a heavy gale of wind , which , after a fortnight -LRB- during which we attempted in vain to make head against it -RRB- , forced us back to Smyrna .
Parsing [sent. 595 len. 26]: When the weather moderated , I directed the captain to take the vessel into the outer roadstead that I might sail as soon as possible .
Parsing [sent. 596 len. 31]: We had not dropped anchor again more than five minutes when I perceived a boat pulling off from the shore in which was the cadi and the officers of justice .
Parsing [sent. 597 len. 43]: Convinced that I was discovered , I was at a loss how to proceed , when the idea occurred to me that I might conceal my own body in a cask , as I had before so well concealed those of others .
Parsing [sent. 598 len. 40]: I called the captain down into the cabin , and telling him that I had reason to suspect that the cadi would take my life , offered him a large part of the cargo if he would assist me .
Parsing [sent. 599 len. 14]: The captain who , unfortunately for me , was a Greek , consented .
Parsing [sent. 600 len. 33]: We went down into the hold , started the wine out of one of the pipes , and having taken out the head , I crawled in , and was hooped up .
Parsing [sent. 601 len. 12]: The cadi came on board immediately afterwards and inquired for me .
Parsing [sent. 602 len. 31]: The captain stated that I had fallen overboard in the gale , and that he had in consequence returned , the vessel not being consigned to any house at Corfu .
Parsing [sent. 603 len. 11]: `` Has then the accursed villain escaped my vengeance ! ''
Parsing [sent. 604 len. 34]: exclaimed the cadi ; `` the murderer , that fines his wines with the bodies of his fellow-creatures : but you may deceive me , Greek , we will examine the vessel . ''
Parsing [sent. 605 len. 16]: The officers who accompanied the cadi proceeded carefully to search every part of the ship .
Parsing [sent. 606 len. 30]: Not being able to discover me , the Greek captain was believed ; and , after a thousand imprecations upon my soul , the cadi and his people departed .
Parsing [sent. 607 len. 50]: I now breathed more freely , notwithstanding I was nearly intoxicated with the lees of the wine which impregnated the wood of the cask , and I was anxious to be set at liberty ; but the treacherous captain had no such intention , and never came near me .
Parsing [sent. 608 len. 46]: At night he cut his cable and made sail , and I overheard a conversation between two of the men , which made known to me his intentions : these were to throw me overboard on his passage , and take possession of my property .
Parsing [sent. 609 len. 18]: I cried out to them from the bung-hole : I screamed for mercy , but in vain .
Parsing [sent. 610 len. 29]: One of them answered , that , as I had murdered others , and put them into casks , I should now be treated in the same manner .
Parsing [sent. 611 len. 36]: I could not but mentally acknowledge the justice of my punishment , and resigned myself to my fate ; all that I wished was to be thrown over at once and released from my misery .
Parsing [sent. 612 len. 15]: The momentary anticipation of death appeared to be so much worse than the reality .
Parsing [sent. 613 len. 48]: But it was ordered otherwise : a gale of wind blew up with such force , that the captain and crew had enough to do to look after the vessel , and either I was forgotten , or my doom was postponed until a more seasonable opportunity .
Parsing [sent. 614 len. 29]: On the third day I heard the sailors observe that , with such a wretch as I was remaining on board , the vessel must inevitably be lost .
Parsing [sent. 615 len. 17]: The hatches were then opened ; I was hoisted up and cast into the raging sea .
Parsing [sent. 616 len. 46]: The bung of the cask was out , but by stuffing my handkerchief in , when the hole was under water , I prevented the cask from filling ; and when it was uppermost , I removed it for a moment to obtain fresh air .
Parsing [sent. 617 len. 64]: I was dreadfully bruised by the constant rolling , in a heavy sea , and completely worn out with fatigue and pain ; I had made up my mind to let the water in and be rid of my life , when I was tossed over and over with such dreadful rapidity as prevented my taking the precaution of keeping out the water .
Parsing [sent. 618 len. 28]: After three successive rolls of the same kind , I found that the cask , which had been in the surf , had struck on the beach .
Parsing [sent. 619 len. 21]: In a moment after , I heard voices , and people came up to the cask and rolled me along .
Parsing [sent. 620 len. 58]: I would not speak , lest they should be frightened and allow me to remain on the beach , where I might again be tossed about by the waves ; but as soon as they stopped , I called in a faint voice from the bung-hole , begging them for mercy 's sake to let me out .
Parsing [sent. 621 len. 52]: At first they appeared alarmed ; but , on my repeating my request , and stating that I was the owner of the ship which was off the land , and the captain and crew had mutinied and tossed me overboard , they brought some tools and set me at liberty .
Parsing [sent. 622 len. 37]: The first sight that met my eyes after I was released , was my vessel lying a wreck ; each wave that hurled her further on the beach , breaking her more and more to pieces .
Parsing [sent. 623 len. 41]: She was already divided amid-ships , and the white foaming surf was covered with pipes of wine , which , as fast as they were cast on shore , were rolled up by the same people who had released me .
Parsing [sent. 624 len. 13]: I was so worn out , that I fainted where I lay .
Parsing [sent. 625 len. 47]: When I came to , I found myself in a cave upon a bundle of capotes , and perceived a party of forty or fifty men , who were sitting by a large fire , and emptying with great rapidity one of my pipes of wine .
Parsing [sent. 626 len. 25]: As soon as they observed that I was coming to my senses , they poured some wine down my throat , which restored me .
Parsing [sent. 627 len. 19]: I was then desired by one of them , who seemed to be the chief , to approach .
Parsing [sent. 628 len. 99]: `` The men who have been saved from the wreck , '' said he , `` have told me strange stories of your enormous crimes -- now , sit down , and tell me the truth -- if I believe you , you shall have justice -- I am cadi here -- if you wish to know where you are , it is upon the island of Ischia -- if you wish to know in what company , it is in the society of those who by illiberal people are called pirates : now tell the truth . ''
Parsing [sent. 629 len. 37]: I thought that with pirates my story would be received better than with other people , and I therefore narrated my history to them , in the same words that I now have to your highness .
Parsing [sent. 630 len. 76]: When I had finished , the captain of the gang observed : -- `` Well , then , as you acknowledge to have killed a slave , to have assisted at the death of a Jew , and to have drowned an aga , you certainly deserve death ; but , on consideration of the excellence of the wine , and the secret which you have imparted to us , I shall commute your sentence .
Parsing [sent. 631 len. 57]: As for the captain and the remainder of the crew , they have been guilty of treachery and piracy on the high seas -- a most heinous offence , which deserves instant death : but as it is by their means that we have been put in possession of the wine , I shall be lenient .
Parsing [sent. 632 len. 11]: I therefore sentence you all to hard labour for life .
Parsing [sent. 633 len. 21]: You shall be sold as slaves in Cairo , and we will pocket the money and drink your wine . ''
Parsing [sent. 634 len. 23]: The pirates loudly applauded the justice of a decision by which they benefited , and all appeal on our parts was useless .
Parsing [sent. 635 len. 32]: When the weather became more settled , we were put on board one of their small xebeques , and on our arrival at this port were exposed for sale and purchased .
Parsing [sent. 636 len. 63]: Such , pacha , is the history which induced me to make use of the expressions which you wished to be explained ; and I hope you will allow that I have been more unfortunate than guilty , as on every occasion in which I took away the life of another , I had only to choose between that and my own .
Parsing [sent. 637 len. 87]: `` Well , it is rather a curious story , '' observed the pacha , `` but still , if it were not for my promise , I certainly would have your head off for drowning the aga ; I consider it excessively impertinent in an unbelieving Greek to suppose that his life is of the same value as that of an aga of janissaries , and follower of the Prophet ; but , however , my promise was given , and you may depart . ''
Parsing [sent. 638 len. 19]: `` The wisdom of your highness is brighter than the stars of the heaven , '' observed Mustapha .
Parsing [sent. 639 len. 11]: `` Shall the slave be honoured with your bounty ? ''
Parsing [sent. 640 len. 3]: `` Mashallah !
Parsing [sent. 641 len. 2]: bounty !
Parsing [sent. 642 len. 30]: I 've given him his life , and , as he considers it of more value than an aga 's , I think 't is a very handsome present .
Parsing [sent. 643 len. 7]: Drown an aga , indeed ! ''
Parsing [sent. 644 len. 16]: continued the pacha , rising , `` but it certainly was a very curious story .
Parsing [sent. 645 len. 8]: Let it be written down , Mustapha .
Parsing [sent. 646 len. 9]: We 'll hear the other man to-morrow . ''
Parsing [sent. 647 len. 6]: VOLUME ONE , CHAPTER THREE .

Parsing [sent. 673 len. 5]: STORY OF THE MONK .
Parsing [sent. 674 len. 39]: May it please your highness , I am a Spaniard by birth , and a native of Seville ; but whether my father was a grandee , or of more humble extraction , I can not positively assert .
Parsing [sent. 675 len. 80]: All that I can establish is , that when reason dawned , I found myself in the asylum instituted by government , in that city , for those unfortunate beings who are brought up upon black bread and oil , because their unnatural parents either do not choose to incur the expense of their maintenance , or having , in the first instance , allowed unlawful love to conquer shame , end by permitting shame to overcome maternal love .
Parsing [sent. 676 len. 38]: It is the custom , at a certain age , to put these children out to different trades and callings ; and those who show precocity of talent are often received into the bosom of the church .
Parsing [sent. 677 len. 32]: Gifted by nature with a very fine voice and correct ear for music , I was selected to be brought up as a chorister in a Dominican convent of great reputation .
Parsing [sent. 678 len. 20]: At the age of ten years , I was placed under the charge of the leader of the choir .
Parsing [sent. 679 len. 39]: Under his directions , I was fully occupied receiving my lessons in singing , or at other times performing the junior offices of the church , such as carrying the frankincense or large wax tapers in the processions .
Parsing [sent. 680 len. 37]: As a child my voice was much admired ; and after the service was over , I often received presents of sweetmeats from the ladies , who brought them in their pockets for the little Anselmo .
Parsing [sent. 681 len. 58]: As I grew up , I became a remarkable proficient in music ; at the age of twenty , I possessed a fine counter-tenor ; and flattered by the solicitations of the superior of the convent and other dignitaries of the church , I consented to take the vows , and became a member of the fraternity .
Parsing [sent. 682 len. 23]: Although there was no want of liberty in our convent , I was permitted even more than the rest of the monks .
Parsing [sent. 683 len. 28]: I gave lessons in music and singing , and a portion of my earnings were placed in the superior 's hands for the benefit of the fraternity .
Parsing [sent. 684 len. 34]: Independent of this , my reputation was spread all over Seville ; and hundreds used to attend the mass performed in our church , that they might hear the voice of brother Anselmo .
Parsing [sent. 685 len. 23]: I was therefore considered as a valuable property , and the convent would have suffered a great deal by my quitting it .
Parsing [sent. 686 len. 45]: Although I could not be released from my vows , still I could by application have been transferred to Madrid ; and the superior , aware of this circumstance , allowed me every indulgence , with the hopes of my being persuaded to remain .
Parsing [sent. 687 len. 28]: The money which I retained for my own exigencies enabled me to make friends with the porter , and I obtained egress or ingress at any hour .
Parsing [sent. 688 len. 54]: I was a proficient on the guitar ; and incongruous as it may appear with my monastic vows , I often hastened from the service at vespers to perform in a serenade to some fair senhora , whose _ inamorata _ required the powers of my voice to soften her to his wishes .
Parsing [sent. 689 len. 26]: My sedillas and canzonettas were much admired ; and eventually no serenade was considered as effective , without the assistance of the counter-tenor of Anselmo .
Parsing [sent. 690 len. 31]: I hardly need observe that it was very profitable ; and that I had the means of supplying myself with luxuries which the rules of our order did not admit .
Parsing [sent. 691 len. 26]: I soon became irregular and debauched ; often sitting up whole nights with the young cavaliers , drinking and singing amorous songs for their amusement .
Parsing [sent. 692 len. 22]: Still , however , my conduct was not known , or was overlooked for the reasons which I have stated before .
Parsing [sent. 693 len. 25]: When once a man indulges to excess in wine , he is assailed by , and becomes an easy prey to every other vice .
Parsing [sent. 694 len. 34]: This error soon led me into others ; and , regardless of my monastic vows , I often felt more inclined to serenade upon my own account than on that of my employers .
Parsing [sent. 695 len. 53]: I had the advantage of a very handsome face , but it was disguised by the shaven crown and the unbecoming manner of cutting the hair ; the coarse and unwieldy monastic dress belonging to our order hid the symmetry of my limbs which might have otherwise attracted notice on the Prado .
Parsing [sent. 696 len. 21]: I soon perceived that , although my singing was admired by the other sex , their admiration went no farther .
Parsing [sent. 697 len. 24]: They seemed to consider that in every other point I was , as I ought to have been , dead to the world .
Parsing [sent. 698 len. 27]: There was a young lady , Donna Sophia , whom I had for some time instructed in music , who appeared to be more favourably inclined .
Parsing [sent. 699 len. 97]: She was an excellent performer , and passionately fond of the science : and I have always observed , your highness , that between the real amateurs of harmony there is a sympathy , a description of free-masonry , which immediately puts them on a level , and on terms of extreme intimacy ; so much so , that were I a married man , and my wife extremely partial to music , I should be very careful how I introduced to her a person of a similar feeling , if I possessed it not myself .
Parsing [sent. 700 len. 40]: I was very much in the good graces of this young lady , and flattered myself with a successful issue : when one day , as we were singing a duet , a handsome young officer made his appearance .
Parsing [sent. 701 len. 28]: His hair , which was of the finest brown , curled in natural ringlets : and his clothes were remarkably well-fitted to his slender and graceful figure .
Parsing [sent. 702 len. 49]: He was a cousin , who had just returned from Carthagena ; and as he was remarkably attentive , I soon perceived that all my advances had been thrown away , and that I was more and more in the background each morning that I made my appearance .
Parsing [sent. 703 len. 74]: Annoyed at this , I ventured to speak too freely ; and during his absence calumniated him to the Donna Sophia , hoping by these means to regain my place in her affections ; but I made a sad mistake : for not only were my services dispensed with for the future , but , as I afterwards discovered , she stated to her cousin the grounds upon which I had been dismissed .
Parsing [sent. 704 len. 24]: I returned to the convent in no pleasant mood , when I was informed that my presence had been demanded by the superior .
Parsing [sent. 705 len. 36]: I repaired to the parlour , where he stated that my licentious conduct had come to his ears ; and after much upbraiding , he concluded by ordering me to submit to a severe penance .
Parsing [sent. 706 len. 42]: Aware that disobedience would only be followed up by greater severity , I bowed with humility in my mien , but indignation in my breast ; and returning to my cell , resolved upon immediately writing for my removal to Madrid .
Parsing [sent. 707 len. 15]: I had not been there many minutes when the porter brought me a note .
Parsing [sent. 708 len. 47]: It was from Donna Sophia , requesting to see me that evening , and apologising for her apparent ill-usage , which she had only assumed the better to conceal her intentions ; being afraid , at our last interview , that her mother was within hearing .
Parsing [sent. 709 len. 18]: I was in raptures when I perused the note , and hastened to comply with her request .
Parsing [sent. 710 len. 22]: Her directions were to repair to the back door , which looked out upon some fields , and give three taps .
Parsing [sent. 711 len. 30]: I arrived , and as soon as I raised my hand to give the signal , was seized by four men in masks , who gagged and bound me .
Parsing [sent. 712 len. 24]: They then stripped off my friar 's dress , and scourged me with nettles , until I was almost frantic with the pain .
Parsing [sent. 713 len. 19]: When their vengeance was satisfied , they cast me loose , removed the gag , and ran away .
Parsing [sent. 714 len. 38]: As I then suspected , and afterwards discovered to be true , I was indebted to the young officer for this treatment , in return for what I had said , and which his mistress had repeated .
Parsing [sent. 715 len. 31]: Smarting with pain , and boiling with rage , I dragged on my clothes as well as I could , and began to reflect in what manner I should act .
Parsing [sent. 716 len. 33]: Conceal my situation from the other members of the convent I could not ; and to explain it would not only be too humiliating , but subject me to more rigorous discipline .
Parsing [sent. 717 len. 33]: At last I considered that out of evil might spring good ; and gathering a large bundle of the nettles which grew under the walls , I crawled back to the convent .
Parsing [sent. 718 len. 42]: When I attained my cell , I threw off my gown , which was now unbearable from the swelling of my limbs , and commenced thrashing the walls of my cell and my bed with the nettles which I had procured .
Parsing [sent. 719 len. 45]: After a short time , I moaned piteously , and continued so to do , louder and louder , until some of the friars got up to inquire the reason ; when they found me , apparently , castigating myself in this cruel manner .
Parsing [sent. 720 len. 19]: When they opened the door , I threw myself on the bed , and cried still more vociferously .
Parsing [sent. 721 len. 23]: This certainly was the only part of my conduct which was not deceptive , for I was in the most acute agony .
Parsing [sent. 722 len. 50]: To their inquiries , I told them that I had been guilty of great enormities : that the superior had reproved me , and ordered me penance ; and that I had scourged myself with nettles ; requesting them to continue the application as my strength had failed me .
Parsing [sent. 723 len. 10]: With this injunction they were too humane to comply .
Parsing [sent. 724 len. 18]: Some went for the surgeon of the convent , while others reported the circumstance to the superior .
Parsing [sent. 725 len. 38]: The former applied remedies which assuaged the pain : the latter was so pleased at my apparent contrition , that he gave me absolution , and relieved me from the penance to which I had been subjected .
Parsing [sent. 726 len. 19]: When I recovered , I was more in favour , and was permitted the same indulgences as before .
Parsing [sent. 727 len. 21]: But I was some days confined to my bed , during which I was continually reflecting upon what had passed .
Parsing [sent. 728 len. 38]: I perceived , to my misery , the pale which I had placed between me and the world , by embracing a monastic life and how unfit I was , by temperament , to fulfil my vows .
Parsing [sent. 729 len. 18]: I cursed my father and mother , who had been the original cause of my present situation .
Parsing [sent. 730 len. 12]: I cursed the monastic dress which blazoned forth my unhappy condition .
Parsing [sent. 731 len. 14]: Then I thought of the treacherous girl , and planned schemes of revenge .
Parsing [sent. 732 len. 33]: I compared my personal qualifications with those of the young officer ; and vanity suggested , that were it not for my vile professional disguise , the advantage was on my side .
Parsing [sent. 733 len. 12]: At last I decided upon the steps that I would take .
Parsing [sent. 734 len. 26]: As I before stated , my purse was well supplied from the lessons which I gave in music , and from assisting at the serenades .
Parsing [sent. 735 len. 45]: When I was sufficiently recovered to go out , I proceeded to a barber , and on the plea of continual headache , for which it had been recommended that I should shave my head , requested him to make me a false tonsure .
Parsing [sent. 736 len. 32]: In a few days it was ready , and being very well made , no difference could be perceived between the wig and my own hair , which was then removed .
Parsing [sent. 737 len. 38]: So far I had succeeded ; but as the greatest caution was necessary in a proceeding of this nature , to avoid suspicion , I returned to the convent , where I remained quiet for several days .
Parsing [sent. 738 len. 42]: One evening I again sallied forth , and when it was quite dark repaired to the _ friperie _ shop of a Jew , where I purchased a second-hand suit of cavalier 's clothes , which I thought would fit me .
Parsing [sent. 739 len. 32]: I concealed them in my cell , and the next morning went in search of a small lodging in some obscure part , where I might not be subject to observation .
Parsing [sent. 740 len. 41]: This was difficult , but I at last succeeded in finding one to let , which opened upon a general staircase of a house , which was appropriated to a variety of lodgers , who were constantly passing and repassing .
Parsing [sent. 741 len. 33]: I paid the first month in advance , stating , it would be occupied by a brother whom I daily expected , and in the mean time took possession of the key .
Parsing [sent. 742 len. 28]: I bought a small chest , which I conveyed to my lodgings , and having removed my cavalier 's dress from the convent , locked it up .
Parsing [sent. 743 len. 25]: I then remained quiet as before , not only to avoid suspicion , but to ingratiate myself with the superior by my supposed reformation .
Parsing [sent. 744 len. 34]: After a few days I sallied forth , and leaving a note for one of the most skilful perruquiers of Seville , desired him to call at my lodgings at an hour indicated .
Parsing [sent. 745 len. 54]: Having repaired there to be ready to receive him , I took off my monk 's dress and false tonsure , which I locked up in my chest ; I tied a silk handkerchief round my head and got into bed , leaving my cavalier 's suit on the chair near to me .
Parsing [sent. 746 len. 8]: The perruquier knocked at the appointed time .
Parsing [sent. 747 len. 52]: I desired him to come in , apologised for my servant being absent on a message , and stating that I had been obliged to shave my head on account of a fever , from which I had now recovered , requested that he would provide me with a handsome wig .
Parsing [sent. 748 len. 52]: I explained at his request the colour and description of hair which I had lost ; and in so doing , represented it as much lighter than my own really was , and similar to that of the young officer , whose ringlets had been the cause of my last disaster .
Parsing [sent. 749 len. 48]: I paid him a part of the price down , and having agreed upon the exact time at which it should be delivered , he departed ; when I rose from my bed , I resumed my monastic dress and tonsure , and returned to the convent .
Parsing [sent. 750 len. 39]: During the whole of the time occupied by these transactions , I had been assiduous in laying up money , which before I had squandered as fast as I obtained it , and had realised a considerable sum .
Parsing [sent. 751 len. 14]: I could not help comparing myself to a chrysalis previous to its transformation .
Parsing [sent. 752 len. 25]: I had before been a caterpillar , I was now all ready to burst my confinement , and flit about as a gaudy butterfly .
Parsing [sent. 753 len. 51]: Another week I continued my prudent conduct , at the end of which I was admitted to my superior , in whose hands I placed a sum of money which I could very conveniently spare , and received his benediction and commendations for having weaned myself from my former excesses .
Parsing [sent. 754 len. 26]: With a quickened pulse I hastened to my lodgings , and throwing off my hateful gown and tonsure , dressed myself in my new attire .
Parsing [sent. 755 len. 5]: The transformation was complete .
Parsing [sent. 756 len. 6]: I could not recognise myself .
Parsing [sent. 757 len. 20]: I hardly could believe that the dashing young cavalier that confronted me in the mirror was the brother Anselmo .
Parsing [sent. 758 len. 23]: `` Is this a face , '' said I , communing with myself , `` to be disfigured with a vile tonsure ?
Parsing [sent. 759 len. 15]: are these limbs to be hid under the repulsive garment of a monk ? ''
Parsing [sent. 760 len. 21]: Again I surveyed myself , and it was with difficulty that I could tear myself away from contemplating my metamorphosis .
Parsing [sent. 761 len. 6]: I was indeed a butterfly .
Parsing [sent. 762 len. 8]: At last I determined upon sallying forth .
Parsing [sent. 763 len. 11]: I locked up my monastic dress and descended the staircase .
Parsing [sent. 764 len. 48]: I must acknowledge that it was with trepidation I ventured into the street , but I had soon reason to take confidence , for I was met by one of my most intimate friends , who looked in my face and passed on without the slightest recognition .
Parsing [sent. 765 len. 41]: Overjoyed at this circumstance , I took courage , and boldly proceeded to the Prado , where I was greeted with favourable glances from the women , and sneers from the men , both of which I considered equally flattering .
Parsing [sent. 766 len. 21]: In the evening I returned to my lodgings , resumed the habit of my order , and gained the convent .
Parsing [sent. 767 len. 21]: I now felt that there was no chance of discovery , and anticipated the happiness which had been denied me .
Parsing [sent. 768 len. 45]: I subsequently ordered the most fashionable and expensive clothes , hired my lodgings for six months , assumed the name of Don Pedro , made the acquaintance of many young men , and amongst others of the officer who had treated me so ill .
Parsing [sent. 769 len. 15]: He took a fancy to me , which I encouraged to further my views .
Parsing [sent. 770 len. 49]: I became his confidant , he informed me of his amour with his cousin , adding that he was tired of the business , and wished to break with her ; also , as an excellent joke , the punishment which he had inflicted upon the friar Anselmo .
Parsing [sent. 771 len. 48]: He was a great proficient with the small sword , an accomplishment which , of course , had been neglected in my education , and which I accounted for by stating , that until the death of my elder brother I had been intended for the church .
Parsing [sent. 772 len. 21]: I accepted his offer to be my instructor , and my first rudiments in the science were received from him .
Parsing [sent. 773 len. 36]: Afterwards I applied to a professor , and constantly practising , in the course of a few months I knew , from occasional trials of skill with the officer , that I was his superior .
Parsing [sent. 774 len. 13]: My revenge , which hitherto had been controlled , was now ripe .
Parsing [sent. 775 len. 27]: But in narrating my adventures abroad , it must not be supposed that I neglected every thing that prudence or caution could suggest to avoid discovery .
Parsing [sent. 776 len. 28]: On the contrary , now that I had the means of enjoying myself , I was more careful that I did not by any indiscretion excite surmises .
Parsing [sent. 777 len. 23]: I generally devoted four days out of the seven in the week to the convent and to my professional occupation as music-master .
Parsing [sent. 778 len. 26]: To increase the difficulty of identification , I became more serious in my manner , more dirty in my person , as the brother Anselmo .
Parsing [sent. 779 len. 37]: I pretended to have imbibed a fancy for snuff , with which I soiled my face and monastic attire , and seldom if ever spoke , or if I did , in a very solemn voice .
Parsing [sent. 780 len. 19]: So far from suspicion , I every day gained more and more the good will of the superior .
Parsing [sent. 781 len. 35]: My absence in the day-time was not noticed , as it was known that I gave lessons in music , and my irregularity during the night was a secret between the porter and myself .
Parsing [sent. 782 len. 48]: I hardly need observe that , as Don Pedro , I always lamented not having been gifted with a voice , and have even in the presence of my companions , sent a billet to brother Anselmo to serenade a lady whom I courted as Don Pedro .
Parsing [sent. 783 len. 35]: I do not believe until ulterior circumstances , that there was ever in the mind of any the slightest idea that , under my dissimilar habits , I was one and the same person .
Parsing [sent. 784 len. 50]: But to continue : one day the young officer , whose name was Don Lopez , informed me that he did not know how to act ; he was so pestered with the jealousy and reproaches of his mistress , and requested my advice as to how to proceed .
Parsing [sent. 785 len. 6]: I laughed at his dilemma .
Parsing [sent. 786 len. 28]: `` My dear Lopez , '' replied I , `` introduce me to her , and depend upon it that she will give you no more trouble .
Parsing [sent. 787 len. 20]: I will make love to her , and pleased with her new conquest she will soon forget you . ''
Parsing [sent. 788 len. 24]: `` My good fellow , '' replied he , `` your advice is excellent : will you come with me this afternoon ? ''
Parsing [sent. 789 len. 29]: Once more I was in the presence of her whom I had loved , but loved no more , for I now only felt and lived for revenge .
Parsing [sent. 790 len. 10]: She had not the most distant recognition of me .
Parsing [sent. 791 len. 34]: Piqued as she was with Don Lopez , and fascinated with my exertions to please , I soon gained an interest ; but she still loved him between the paroxysms of her hate .
Parsing [sent. 792 len. 33]: Trying all she could to recover him at one moment , and listening to my attentions at another , he at last accused her of perfidy and took his leave for ever .
Parsing [sent. 793 len. 24]: Then her violence broke out , and as a proof of my attachment , she demanded that I should call him to account .
Parsing [sent. 794 len. 37]: I wished no better , and pretending to be so violently attached to her that I was infatuated , I took occasion of his laughing at me to give him the lie , and demand satisfaction .
Parsing [sent. 795 len. 17]: As it was in the presence of others , there was no recal or explanation allowed .
Parsing [sent. 796 len. 45]: We met by agreement , alone , in the very field where I received my chastisement ; I brought with me my monastic habit and tonsure , which I concealed before his arrival among the very nettles which he had gathered for my chastisement .
Parsing [sent. 797 len. 19]: The conflict was not long ; after a few thrusts and parries he lay dying at my feet .
Parsing [sent. 798 len. 23]: I immediately threw over my dress that of the friar , and exchanging the wig for the tonsure , stood by him .
Parsing [sent. 799 len. 27]: He opened his eyes , which had closed from the fainting occasioned by the sudden gush from his wound , and looked at me with amazement .
Parsing [sent. 800 len. 34]: `` Yes , Don Lopez , '' said I , `` in Don Pedro behold the friar Anselmo ; he whom you scourged with nettles ; he who has revenged the insult . ''
Parsing [sent. 801 len. 48]: I then threw off the monk 's dress , and exposed to him the other beneath it , and changing my tonsure for the wig , `` Now you are convinced of the truth , '' added I , `` and now I have my revenge . ''
Parsing [sent. 802 len. 41]: `` I am , I am , '' replied he faintly ; `` but if you have slain me as Don Pedro , now that I am dying I entreat you , as brother Anselmo , to give me absolution .
Parsing [sent. 803 len. 13]: Carry not your revenge so far as to deny me this . ''
Parsing [sent. 804 len. 54]: I could not refuse , and I gave absolution in the one costume to the man who had fallen by my hand in the other : for my own part I thought it was an absurdity , but my revenge was satisfied , and I would not refuse him such a poor consolation .
Parsing [sent. 805 len. 57]: A few minutes afterwards he expired , and I hastened to my lodgings , changed my dress , and repaired to the convent , where as Don Pedro I wrote to Donna Sophia , in forming her of what had taken place , and of my having absconded until the hue and cry should be over .
Parsing [sent. 806 len. 18]: For three weeks I remained in the convent , or only appeared abroad as the father Anselmo .
Parsing [sent. 807 len. 43]: I brought a considerable sum to the superior for the use of the church , partly to satisfy the qualms of conscience which assailed me for the crime which I had committed ; partly that I might continue in his good graces .
Parsing [sent. 808 len. 40]: At the expiration of the time I sent a note to the young lady , as from Don Pedro , acquainting her with my return , and my intention to call upon her in the dusk of the evening .
Parsing [sent. 809 len. 46]: I went to my lodgings , dressed myself as Don Pedro , and tapping at her door was admitted ; but instead of being cordially greeted , as I expected , I was repulsed , loaded with abuse , and declared an object of detestation .
Parsing [sent. 810 len. 38]: It appeared that , although in her rage at the desertion of her lover , she had listened to the dictates of revenge , now that he was no more all her affection for him had revived .
Parsing [sent. 811 len. 38]: I returned her upbraiding , and quitted the room to leave the house ; but she had no intention that I should escape , and had stationed two of her relations below , ready to intercept me .
Parsing [sent. 812 len. 28]: She called to them as I descended the stairs ; when I arrived at the hall , I found them with drawn swords to dispute my passage .
Parsing [sent. 813 len. 74]: I had no resource but to fight my way ; and charging them furiously , I severely wounded one , and shortly afterwards disarmed the other , just as the enraged fair one , who perceived that I was gaining the day , had run behind me and seized my arms ; but she was too late : I threw her indignantly upon the wounded man , and walked out of the house .
Parsing [sent. 814 len. 29]: As soon as I was in the street , I took to my heels , gained my lodgings , changed my dress , and repaired to the convent .
Parsing [sent. 815 len. 6]: This adventure sobered me much .
Parsing [sent. 816 len. 27]: I now remained quiet for some months , never assuming my dress as Don Pedro , lest the officers of justice should lay hold of me .
Parsing [sent. 817 len. 17]: I became more rigid and exact in my duties , and more austere in my manner .
Parsing [sent. 818 len. 32]: The several confessional chairs in our church were usually occupied by the senior monks , although , when absent from sickness or other causes , the juniors occasionally supplied their place .
Parsing [sent. 819 len. 57]: One of the monks had been taken ill , and I knew that the mother of the young lady , who was very strict in her religious duties , confessed at that chair every Friday ; I took possession of it , with the hopes that I should find out some means of prosecuting my revenge .
Parsing [sent. 820 len. 20]: The young lady also confessed at the same chair , when she did come , which was but seldom .
Parsing [sent. 821 len. 14]: Since the death of her lover , she had never made her appearance .
Parsing [sent. 822 len. 55]: As I anticipated , the mother came , and after having run over a string of peccadilloes , for which I ordered a slight penance , I inquired , through the punctured communication on the side of the confessional chair , whether she had not children , to which she answered in the affirmative .
Parsing [sent. 823 len. 11]: I then asked , when her daughter had confessed last .
Parsing [sent. 824 len. 55]: She mentioned a long date , and I commenced a serious expostulation upon the neglect of parents , desiring that her daughter might be brought to confess , or otherwise I should be obliged to inflict a penance of some hundred Pater-Nosters and Ave-Marias upon herself , for not attending to her parental duties .
Parsing [sent. 825 len. 32]: The old lady , who had no wish to submit to her own penance , promised to bring her daughter the next day , and she was true to her word .
Parsing [sent. 826 len. 8]: Donna Sophia appeared to come very unwillingly .

Parsing [sent. 828 len. 8]: `` Have you made no reservation ? ''
Parsing [sent. 829 len. 37]: inquired I , in the low muttering tone which is used at the confessional ; for although neither party can distinguish the person of the other , I did not wish her to recognise my voice .
Parsing [sent. 830 len. 12]: `` Everything , '' replied she , in a faint whisper .
Parsing [sent. 831 len. 24]: `` My daughter , '' replied I , `` by your trembling answer , I know that you are deceiving yourself and me .
Parsing [sent. 832 len. 32]: I am an old man , and have been too many years in this chair , not to ascertain by the answers which I receive , whether the conscience is unloaded .
Parsing [sent. 833 len. 30]: Yours , I am convinced , has something pressing heavily upon it ; something for which you would fain have absolution , but which you are ashamed to reveal .
Parsing [sent. 834 len. 28]: If not a principal , you have been a party to crime ; and never shall you have absolution until you have made a full confession . ''
Parsing [sent. 835 len. 16]: Her heart swelled with emotion , she attempted to speak , and burst into tears .
Parsing [sent. 836 len. 40]: `` These are harbingers of good , '' observed I ; `` I am now convinced that my supposition was correct : pour out your soul in tribulation , and receive that comfort which I am empowered to bestow .
Parsing [sent. 837 len. 5]: Courage , my daughter !
Parsing [sent. 838 len. 10]: the best of us are but grievous sinners . ''
Parsing [sent. 839 len. 73]: As soon as she could check her sobbing , she commenced her confession ; narrating her penchant for me , her subsequent attachment to the young officer , my abuse of him , and the punishment which had ensued -- his desertion , the introduction of Don Pedro , her pique at having instigated him to kill her lover , his death , and all that I have narrated to your highness .
Parsing [sent. 840 len. 9]: `` These are serious crimes , my daughter !
Parsing [sent. 841 len. 62]: grievous indeed ; you have yielded to the tempter in your own person , caused the death of one man , you have led another astray , and have deceived him , when he claimed the reward of his iniquity ; but all these are trifles compared to the offence upon the holy monk , which is the worst of sacrilege .
Parsing [sent. 842 len. 6]: And what was his fault ?
Parsing [sent. 843 len. 24]: that he cautioned you against a person , whose subsequent conduct has proved , that the worthy man was correct in his suppositions .
Parsing [sent. 844 len. 43]: `` In every way you have offended Heaven ; a whole life will be scarce sufficient for the task of repentance , laying aside the enormous crime of sacrilege , which , in justice , ought to be referred to the inquisition .
Parsing [sent. 845 len. 11]: Excommunication is more fitting in your case than absolution . ''
Parsing [sent. 846 len. 15]: I waited some time before I again spoke , during which she sobbed bitterly .

Parsing [sent. 848 len. 41]: Send to the convent to which he belongs , and entreat him to come ; and when you have confessed your crime , offer to him the same implements of punishment , which through your instigation were so sacrilegiously applied .

Parsing [sent. 850 len. 11]: When you have done that , repair again to me .
Parsing [sent. 851 len. 12]: I shall be in this chair the day after to-morrow . ''
Parsing [sent. 852 len. 32]: The girl muffled up her face , waited a few minutes to compose herself , and then returned to her mother , who wondered what could have detained her so long .
Parsing [sent. 853 len. 20]: That evening , I received a note from Donna Sophia , requesting me to call on the ensuing day .
Parsing [sent. 854 len. 82]: I found her in her room , she had been weeping bitterly , and when I entered coloured up with shame and vexation ; but she had been too much frightened on the day before , to resist the injunctions which she had received : a large bundle of nettles lay on the chair ; and when I entered she turned the key of the door , and falling down on her knees , with many tears made a full confession .
Parsing [sent. 855 len. 35]: I expressed the utmost horror and surprise ; she embraced my knees , implored my pardon , and then , pointing to the nettles , requested I would use them if I thought proper .
Parsing [sent. 856 len. 20]: Having said this , she covered her face with her hands , and remained on her knees in silence .
Parsing [sent. 857 len. 80]: I must confess , that when I called to mind the punishment which had been inflicted on me through her means , and the manner in which she had attempted to betray me to my death , I felt very much inclined to revenge myself by scourging her severely ; but although the affection I once felt for her had passed away , I had a natural tenderness for the sex , which made me abandon this petty revenge .
Parsing [sent. 858 len. 39]: My object was to remove her , so that I might not be recognised in my worldly attire ; and she , I knew , was the only person who could prove that I had killed her lover .
Parsing [sent. 859 len. 57]: I therefore raised her up , and telling her that I was satisfied with her repentance , and , as far as I was personally concerned , forgave her ill treatment , desired her to repair to her confessor , who was the proper person to award a punishment for such a catalogue of heinous crimes .
Parsing [sent. 860 len. 56]: The next day I was in the confessional , when she narrated all that had passed : I then told her she had nothing to do , but to propitiate Heaven by dedicating her musical talents to its service ; pointing out , that her only chance of salvation was from immediately taking the veil .
Parsing [sent. 861 len. 24]: I refused to listen to any other species of penance , however severe , for which she gladly would have compromised the sentence .
Parsing [sent. 862 len. 56]: Goaded by her conscience , miserable at the desertion and death of her lover , and alarmed at the threats of excommunication , in less than a week she repaired to the Ursuline Convent ; and , after a short probation , she took the veil , and was admitted as one of the sisterhood .
Parsing [sent. 863 len. 19]: As soon as my only accuser was fairly locked up , I occasionally resumed my dress and wig .
Parsing [sent. 864 len. 71]: I say occasionally , because in the society which I chiefly delighted in , and in which I became the connoisseur of good wine , that I asserted myself to be , when your highness overheard me , I had no occasion for it , being quite as well received when I sang and played the guitar in my monkish dress , as I should have been in my other .
Parsing [sent. 865 len. 42]: Besides which , I never had to pay when in that costume , as I was obliged to do when I sported the other ; which was only put on when I wished to make myself agreeable to any fair one .
Parsing [sent. 866 len. 26]: I hardly need observe , that I took great care to avoid the society in the one dress with which I mixed in the other .
Parsing [sent. 867 len. 33]: This disguise I continued very successfully for three years , when a circumstance occurred , which ended in my discovery , and my eventually becoming a slave in your highness 's dominions .
Parsing [sent. 868 len. 22]: For some time I had taught the niece of an elderly lady , who was of noble family and very rich .
Parsing [sent. 869 len. 38]: The aunt was always present at the lessons ; and , knowing that she was very devout , I rejected all songs that were of an amorous tendency , and would only practise such as were unimpeachable .
Parsing [sent. 870 len. 17]: In my demeanour I was always sedate and respectful -- full of humility , and self-accusation .
Parsing [sent. 871 len. 45]: When I received my money from the old lady , I used to thank her in the name of our convent , for whose use it was to be appropriated , and call her donation a charity , for which Heaven would reward her .
Parsing [sent. 872 len. 15]: Her confessor died , and the old lady chose me to supply his place .
Parsing [sent. 873 len. 22]: This was what I was anxious to obtain , and I redoubled my zeal , my humility , and my flattery .
Parsing [sent. 874 len. 44]: It was not that I had originally any design upon the affections of the niece , although she was a very pretty girl , but upon the old lady 's purse , for I knew that she could not last for many years .
Parsing [sent. 875 len. 54]: On the contrary , I was anxious , if possible , to have the niece removed , as it was supposed that she would inherit the old lady 's doubloons ; but this required time and opportunity , and , in the meanwhile , I assiduously cultivated the old lady 's good graces .
Parsing [sent. 876 len. 46]: She used to confess once a week ; and I often observed that she acknowledged as a sin , thinking too much of one who had led her from her duty in former days , and for whom she still felt too much worldly passion .
Parsing [sent. 877 len. 32]: One evening when the clock had struck ten , we had laid down the cards , which we occasionally played , it being the day and her usual hour for confessing .
Parsing [sent. 878 len. 34]: Again she repeated the same offence , and I then delicately hinted , that she might be more at ease if she were to confide to me the circumstances connected with her compunctions .
Parsing [sent. 879 len. 40]: She hesitated ; but on my pointing out to her that there ought to be no reservation , and that the acknowledgment of the compunction arising from a sin was not that of the sin itself , she acquiesced .
Parsing [sent. 880 len. 40]: Her confession referred to her early days , when , attached to a young cavalier , against the wishes of her parents , under a solemn promise of marriage , she had consented to receive him into her chamber .
Parsing [sent. 881 len. 12]: The intercourse continued for some time , when it was discovered .
Parsing [sent. 882 len. 20]: Her lover had been way-laid and murdered by her relations , and she had been thrown into a convent .
Parsing [sent. 883 len. 114]: There she had been confined , and the child removed as soon as it was born : she had resisted all the force and threats employed to induce her to take the veil ; and at the death of her father had been released and came into possession of her property , of which they could not deprive her : that she made every endeavour to find out to where her child had been removed , and at last discovered that it had been sent to the Foundling Asylum ; but this information was not obtained until some years afterwards , and all the children sent there at the period had been dispersed .
Parsing [sent. 884 len. 44]: Never having married , her thoughts would revert to the scenes which had taken place with her adored Felix , although years had rolled away , and she felt that she was wrong to dwell upon what in itself had been so criminal .
Parsing [sent. 885 len. 45]: I listened to her story with great interest , for the idea occurred to me , that I might be the unfortunate offspring of their loves , and if not , that in all probability the old lady might be induced so to believe .
Parsing [sent. 886 len. 15]: I inquired whether her child had any marks by which he could be recognised .
Parsing [sent. 887 len. 56]: She answered , that she made most particular inquiries of the people who attended her , and that one of the women had stated that the child had a large wart upon the back of its neck : this however was not likely to remain , and she had abandoned all hopes of its discovery .
Parsing [sent. 888 len. 28]: I observed that warts were easily removed when contracted accidentally , but that those which appeared at the birth were no more to be removed than moles .
Parsing [sent. 889 len. 52]: I then turned the conversation , by stating , that I could not consider her conduct criminal ; it was more than could be expected from human nature , that she should not retain affection for one who had lived with her as a husband , and died for her sake .

Parsing [sent. 893 len. 12]: Might not I be the very son whom she was lamenting ?

Parsing [sent. 895 len. 8]: It was in the month of February .
Parsing [sent. 896 len. 22]: There was one other entry in the same month , same day , and nearly the same hour as my own .

Parsing [sent. 901 len. 78]: She answered that she had it in her memory too well , that it was on the 18th of February ; and that when she referred to the Asylum , they had informed her that the children brought in February had no marks ; that they had all been sent away , but where they could not tell , as the former governor had died , and he was the only person who could give the information .
Parsing [sent. 902 len. 20]: That either I or the other was her child was clear , but to prove which , was impossible .
Parsing [sent. 903 len. 24]: It however made me less scrupulous about my plan of proceeding , which was to identify myself with the child she had lost .
Parsing [sent. 904 len. 63]: It was useless to prove that I was sent in on that day as there was a competitor ; besides which , my monastic vows were at variance with my speculation : I therefore resolved to satisfy her , if I could not satisfactorily prove it to myself or to the rest of the world , and I took my measures accordingly .
Parsing [sent. 905 len. 38]: It was in my worldly disguise , that I determined to attempt my purpose ; and as it was necessary to have a wart on my neck , I resolved to obtain one as soon as possible .
Parsing [sent. 906 len. 36]: This was easily managed : a friar of the convent was troubled with these excrescences , and I jocularly proposed a trial to see whether it was true that the blood of them would inoculate .

Parsing [sent. 908 len. 65]: Within three months I had a large wart on the back of my neck , or rather a conglomeration of them , which I had produced by inoculation , assisted by constant irritation : during this period I was not so frequent in my attendance upon the old lady , excusing myself on account of the duties of the convent which devolved upon me .

Parsing [sent. 910 len. 18]: This required some reflection , as it would be but occasionally that I could make my appearance .

Parsing [sent. 912 len. 20]: Often left in her company , I took opportunities of talking of a young friend whom I highly extolled .

Parsing [sent. 923 len. 96]: When we had practised two or three songs , Donna Celia , the aunt , left the room : I then observed that I had seen the young cavalier whom I had mentioned , and that he appeared to be more infatuated than ever : that he had requested me as a favour to speak on his behalf , but that I had threatened to acquaint her aunt if he mentioned the subject ; for I considered that my duty as a confessor in the family would be very irreconcilable with carrying clandestine love messages .

Parsing [sent. 1514 len. 41]: I certainly improved very much in my profession ; for it was as much as my life was worth to draw blood , although they made no scruple of carrying on a conversation during the whole time of the operation .
Parsing [sent. 1515 len. 37]: We had taken the cargoes out of several vessels , all of which were added to the `` manifest '' by our correct captain ; when one day , we were chased by an English frigate .
Parsing [sent. 1516 len. 28]: I never met the English on shore , but I must say that , afloat , they are the most impertinent people that swim on the seas .
Parsing [sent. 1517 len. 28]: They can not be content with minding their own business , although they have plenty on their hands , but they must interfere in that of others .
Parsing [sent. 1518 len. 44]: They board you , and insist upon knowing where you come from , whither you are bound and what you have on board ; examining you with as much scrutiny as if they had been the delegated custom-house officers of the whole world .
Parsing [sent. 1519 len. 38]: Now it did not exactly suit our captain to submit to such a rigorous search ; he therefore made all sail for an island about seven miles distant , and anchored under the protection of a battery .
Parsing [sent. 1520 len. 29]: Austria -- the nation to whom the island belonged -- was not at war with England ; she was preserving what is called an `` armed neutrality . ''
Parsing [sent. 1521 len. 12]: `` Pray what is the meaning of an armed neutrality ? ''
Parsing [sent. 1522 len. 4]: demanded the pacha .

Parsing [sent. 1524 len. 62]: The frigate followed ; and being prevented by the shallowness of the water from approaching sufficiently near to us herself , sent her boats to examine us : but as there were six of them full of men , and each mounting a gun at her bow , our captain thought it advisable to refuse them permission to come on board .

Parsing [sent. 1528 len. 56]: I was on the poop when an English sailor , with a pigtail as thick as a cable , made a cut at me ; I ran back to avoid the blow , and , in so doing , came with such force against another of their men , that we both tumbled overboard together .

Parsing [sent. 1538 len. 56]: He consoled us , however , by asserting that we could never go to the bottom , as there was a lady of great sanctity passenger in the cabin , who had been sent for to assume the office of lady abbess of a convent near Marseilles , and whom the saints would indubitably preserve .

Parsing [sent. 2236 len. 13]: So far from being alarmed at my situation , I felt happy .
Parsing [sent. 2237 len. 21]: I was in a frail bark ; but I had within it all that I cared for in this world .
Parsing [sent. 2238 len. 33]: I sailed I knew not where , but Rosina was in my company ; I felt the uncertainty of our fate , but was more than compensated by the certainty of possession .
Parsing [sent. 2239 len. 63]: The wind rose , the sea ran high , and curled in threatening foam ; we darted with rapidity before it ; and steering with one arm , while Rosina was clasped in the other , I delighted in our romantic situation ; and , pleased with the excitement which it created , I was blind to the danger which we encountered .
Parsing [sent. 2240 len. 26]: For six days we ran before the wind , when an accumulation of clouds upon the southern horizon indicated that we should have a change .
Parsing [sent. 2241 len. 26]: I had no compass in the boat , but had steered by the sun during the day , and by the stars during the night .
Parsing [sent. 2242 len. 57]: I now considered myself well to the southward , and determined upon running eastward , that I might gain the African shore ; but the gale was too strong to permit me to bring the broadside of my small bark to the wind , and I was compelled to continue my course in a southerly direction .
Parsing [sent. 2243 len. 31]: For the first time , a sensation of alarm came over me : we had but two days ' more sustenance , and Rosina was worn out by constant exposure .
Parsing [sent. 2244 len. 34]: I myself felt the necessity of repose : it was with difficulty that I could keep my eyelids raised ; every minute Nature demanded her rights , and I nodded at the helm .
Parsing [sent. 2245 len. 35]: I was in a melancholy reverie , when I thought that I perceived , as the clouds on the horizon occasionally opened , something that had the appearance of the summit of a precipice .
Parsing [sent. 2246 len. 33]: They closed again ; I watched them with anxiety until they gradually rolled away , and discovered a lofty island , covered with trees and verdure down to the water 's edge .
Parsing [sent. 2247 len. 21]: I shouted with delight , and pointed it out to Rosina , who answered my exultations with a faint smile .
Parsing [sent. 2248 len. 43]: My blood curdled at the expression of her countenance : for many hours she had been in deep thought ; and I perceived that the smile was forced to please me , the intelligence I had imparted affording her but little pleasure .
Parsing [sent. 2249 len. 35]: I ascribed it to weariness and exhaustion ; and hoping soon to be able to relieve her , I steered direct for the only part of the shore which promised us a safe descent .
Parsing [sent. 2250 len. 39]: In an hour I was close to it : and , anxious to land before dark , I steered the boat , with the sail hoisted , through the surf , which was much heavier than I expected .
Parsing [sent. 2251 len. 55]: As soon as her bow struck the beach , the boat was thrown on her broadside , and it required all my exertion to save my beloved , which I did not effect without our being completely washed by the surf , which , in a few minutes , dashed the boat to pieces .
Parsing [sent. 2252 len. 51]: I bore her to a cave at a short distance from where we landed ; and , wrapping her up in a cloak which I had saved from the boat , took away her nun 's attire , and exposed it to dry in the powerful rays of the sun .
Parsing [sent. 2253 len. 31]: I went in search of food , which I soon obtained : banana and cocoa-nuts grew in profusion and in beauty , and fresh water ran down in noisy rills .
Parsing [sent. 2254 len. 32]: I bore them to her , and congratulated her that we were now beyond all pursuit , and in a spot which promised to supply us with all that we required .
Parsing [sent. 2255 len. 9]: She smiled languidly ; her thoughts were elsewhere .
Parsing [sent. 2256 len. 34]: Her clothes were dry , and I brought them to her : she shuddered at the sight of them , and seemed to muster up her resolution before she could put them on .
Parsing [sent. 2257 len. 53]: Night closed in upon us , and we remained in the cave : our bed was formed of the cloaks and the sail of the boat ; and , locked in each other 's arms , separated from all the world , and living but for each other , we fell asleep .
Parsing [sent. 2258 len. 16]: The morning broke : not a cloud was to be seen through the blue expanse .
Parsing [sent. 2259 len. 16]: We walked out , and dwelt in silent admiration upon the splendour of the scene .
Parsing [sent. 2260 len. 50]: The island was clothed in beauty ; the sun poured his genial rays upon the wild fertility of nature ; the birds were warbling forth their notes of joy ; the sea was calm and clear as a mirror , reflecting the steep hills which towered above each other .
Parsing [sent. 2261 len. 32]: `` Here then , Rosina , '' cried I , at last , with rapture , `` we have all that we require , blessed in each other 's love . ''
Parsing [sent. 2262 len. 27]: Rosina burst into tears : `` All -- all , Henrique , except an approving conscience , without which I feel that I can not live .
Parsing [sent. 2263 len. 59]: I love you -- love you dearly -- dote upon you , Henrique : you can not doubt it after all that has occurred : but now that the delirium of passion has subsided , conscience has been busy -- too busy , for it has embittered all ; and I feel that happiness is flown for ever .
Parsing [sent. 2264 len. 40]: I wedded myself to God ; I chose my Saviour as my spouse ; I vowed myself to him -- was received by him at the altar ; and I abandoned this world for that which is to come .
Parsing [sent. 2265 len. 5]: What have I done ?
Parsing [sent. 2266 len. 42]: -- I have been unfaithful to him -- left him , to indulge a worldly passion , sacrificed eternity for perishable mortality , and there is a solemn voice within that tells me I am an outcast from all heavenly joys .
Parsing [sent. 2267 len. 7]: Bear with me , dear Henrique !

Parsing [sent. 2294 len. 51]: Holy Saviour , who despised not the tears and contrition of the Magdalen , receive an unfaithful , but repentant spouse unto your bosom ; for when I made my vow , thou knowest that my heart -- '' With what agony of grief did I hang over the body !

Parsing [sent. 2306 len. 47]: Such is the history of Henrique ; and may it be a warning to those who allow their reason to be seduced by passion , and check not the first impulse towards wrong , when conscience dictates that they are straying from the paths of virtue !

Parsing [sent. 2343 len. 23]: I was so affected at the intelligence of Cerise having destroyed herself , that I found it impossible to remain on shore .
Parsing [sent. 2344 len. 42]: Having met with the captain of a whaler , who expatiated on the fortune which might be realised by embarking in the speculation , I purchased a large ship , and fitted it out for a voyage to Baffin 's Bay .
Parsing [sent. 2345 len. 30]: This consumed all the money I had left , but as I expected to return with ten times the sum , I made no scruple of parting with it .
Parsing [sent. 2346 len. 25]: My crew consisted of about thirty men , all strong fellows : ten of them Englishmen , and the remainder from my own country .
Parsing [sent. 2347 len. 46]: We stood to the northward , until we reached the ice , which floated high as mountains , and steering in between it , we at last came to a fine open water , where a large quantity of whales were blowing in every direction .
Parsing [sent. 2348 len. 28]: Our boats were soon hoisted out , and we were extremely fortunate , having twenty-three fish on board , and boiled down before the season was over .
Parsing [sent. 2349 len. 25]: I now considered my fortune made ; and the ship being full up to the beams , we made all sail to return home .
Parsing [sent. 2350 len. 35]: But a heavy gale came on from the southward , which drove all the ice together , and our ship with it , and we were in great danger of being squeezed to atoms .
Parsing [sent. 2351 len. 39]: Fortunately , we made fast in a bight , on the lee side of a great iceberg , which preserved us , and we anxiously awaited for the termination of the gale , to enable us to proceed .
Parsing [sent. 2352 len. 49]: But when the gale subsided , a hard frost came on , and we were completely frozen up , where we lay -- the ice formed round to the depth of several feet , and lifted the ship , laden as she was , out of the water .
Parsing [sent. 2353 len. 23]: The English , who were experienced fishermen , told us , that we had no chance of being released until next spring .
Parsing [sent. 2354 len. 36]: I ascended to the mast-head , and perceived that for miles , as far as the eye could scan the horizon , there was nothing but one continued succession of icebergs and floes inseparably united .
Parsing [sent. 2355 len. 26]: Despairing , therefore , of any release , until the cold weather should break up , I made all arrangements for remaining during the winter .
Parsing [sent. 2356 len. 33]: Our provisions were very short , and we were obliged to make use of the whale oil , but it soon produced such dysenteries , that it was no longer resorted to .
Parsing [sent. 2357 len. 15]: After two months , the cold became intense , and our fuel ran short .
Parsing [sent. 2358 len. 20]: At the end of three months the crew complained of scurvy , and could not move about the decks .
Parsing [sent. 2359 len. 27]: At the end of the fourth month , they had all died except the chief harpooner , a fat porpoise of an Englishman , and myself .
Parsing [sent. 2360 len. 50]: The bodies remained on the deck , for the cold was so intense that they would not have been tainted for centuries ; and , as at the end of five months , the provisions were all expended , we were again obliged to resort to the whale oil .
Parsing [sent. 2361 len. 36]: The whale oil produced a return of our complaints , and having no other resource , we were forced by imperious hunger to make our repasts from one of the bodies of our dead shipmates .
Parsing [sent. 2362 len. 73]: They were so hard , that it was with difficulty that we could separate a portion with an axe , and the flesh broke off in fragments , as if we had been splitting a piece of granite ; but it thawed before the fire , which we had contrived to keep alight , by supplying it from the bulwarks of the quarter-deck , which we cut away as we required them .
Parsing [sent. 2363 len. 56]: The old harpooner and I lived together on the best terms for a month , during which we seldom quitted the cabin of the vessel , having now drawn down the third dead body , which we cut up as we required it with less difficulty than before , from the change in the weather .
Parsing [sent. 2364 len. 30]: The ice continued breaking up , and all day and night we were startled at the loud crashing which took place , as the icebergs separated from each other .
Parsing [sent. 2365 len. 14]: But my disgust at feeding upon human flesh produced a sort of insanity .
Parsing [sent. 2366 len. 119]: I had always been partial to good eating , and was by no means an indifferent cook ; and I determined to try whether something more palatable could not be provided for our meals ; the idea haunted me day and night , and at last I imagined myself a French restaurateur ; I tied a cloth before me as an apron , put on a cotton nightcap instead of my fur cap , and was about to make a trial of my skill , when I discovered that I had no lard , no fat of any kind except train oil , which I rejected as not being suitable to the '' _ cuisine Francaise _ . ''
Parsing [sent. 2367 len. 35]: My messmates who lay dead , were examined one by one , but they had fallen away so much previous to their decease , that not a symptom of fat was to be perceived .
Parsing [sent. 2368 len. 44]: Without fat I could do nothing ; and as I thought of it in despair , my eye was caught by the rotundity of paunch which still appertained to the English harpooner , the only living being besides myself out of so many .
Parsing [sent. 2369 len. 19]: `` I must have fat , '' cried I , fiercely , as I surveyed his unwieldy carcase .
Parsing [sent. 2370 len. 38]: He started when he observed the rolling of my eyes ; and perceiving that I was advancing towards him , sharpening my knife , he did not think it prudent to trust himself longer in my company .
Parsing [sent. 2371 len. 25]: Snatching up two or three blankets , he ran on deck , and contrived to ascend to the main-top before I could follow him .

Parsing [sent. 2374 len. 38]: I was so eager in my frenzy to obtain him , that I felt neither cold nor hunger ; the weather during the day was now warm enough to be pleasant , but the nights were piercing .
Parsing [sent. 2375 len. 23]: My fat shipmate remained in the top for three days and nights , during which period I never removed from my post .

Parsing [sent. 2384 len. 41]: The first day I succeeded admirably -- I cooked my dishes ; and when they were ready I took off my night-cap and apron , passed my fingers through my hair , and fancied myself a garcon at a restaurateurs .

Parsing [sent. 2386 len. 11]: Never was any meal so delicious to my insane fancy .
Parsing [sent. 2387 len. 14]: I devoured every thing which I cooked , and drank water for champagne .
Parsing [sent. 2388 len. 21]: I meditated upon what I should have for dinner on the ensuing day , and then retired to my bed .
Parsing [sent. 2389 len. 56]: In the meantime the ice had separated , and the ship was again afloat ; but I cared not : all my ideas were concentrated in the pleasures of the table -- and the next morning I went on deck to obtain a piece of meat , when I was astonished at a terrific growl .

Parsing [sent. 2391 len. 32]: He was as large as an ox , so large that when he made a rush at me , and I slipped down the ladder , he could not follow me .
Parsing [sent. 2392 len. 14]: I again looked up , and perceived that he had finished his meal .
