Parsing [sent. 2394 len. 36]: Glad to be rid of so unpleasant a visitor , I came up , and cutting off the meat I required , again exerted my cookery , was again satisfied , and went to sleep .
Parsing [sent. 2395 len. 14]: I never felt so happy as I then did in my insane condition .
Parsing [sent. 2396 len. 45]: All I thought of , all I wished , I could command -- my happiness was concentrated in eating my fellow-creatures , cooked in a proper manner , instead of the usual method of bolting them down to satisfy the cravings of imperious hunger .
Parsing [sent. 2397 len. 48]: I woke the next morning as usual , and when I crawled on deck , was again saluted with the angry growl of the bear , who was busy making a repast upon another body -- when he had finished he plunged into the sea as before .
Parsing [sent. 2398 len. 28]: I now thought it high time to put an end to these depredations on my larder , which in a few days would have left me destitute .
Parsing [sent. 2399 len. 20]: My invention was called into action , and I hit upon a plan , which I thought would succeed .
Parsing [sent. 2400 len. 39]: I dragged all the bodies to the after part of the quarterdeck , and blocked it up before the cabin-hatch with swabs and small sails , so as to form a sort of dam about eight inches high .
Parsing [sent. 2401 len. 37]: I then went below and brought up forty or fifty buckets of train oil , which I poured upon the deck abaft , so that it was covered with oil to the height of several inches .
Parsing [sent. 2402 len. 38]: On the ensuing morning the bear came as I expected , and commenced his repast : I had stationed myself aloft , in the mizen-top , with several buckets of oil , which I poured upon him .
Parsing [sent. 2403 len. 29]: His fur was otherwise well saturated with what he had collected when he lay down on the deck to devour one of the bodies more at his ease .
Parsing [sent. 2404 len. 23]: When I had poured all my buckets of oil over him but one , I threw the empty buckets down upon him .
Parsing [sent. 2405 len. 13]: This enraged him , and he mounted the rigging to be revenged .
Parsing [sent. 2406 len. 41]: I waited until he had arrived at the futtock shrouds , when I poured my last bucket upon him , which quite blinded him , and then gained the deck by sliding down the back stays on the opposite side .
Parsing [sent. 2407 len. 27]: A bear can climb fast , but is very slow in his descent -- the consequence was that I had plenty of time for my arrangements .
Parsing [sent. 2408 len. 28]: I ran below , and lighting a torch of oakum , which I had prepared in readiness , placed it to his hinder quarters as he descended .
Parsing [sent. 2409 len. 51]: The effect was exactly what I had anticipated ; his thick fur , covered in every part with oil , was immediately in a blaze , and burnt with such rapidity , that before he could recover his feet on deck , he was like an immense ball of fire .
Parsing [sent. 2410 len. 10]: I retreated to the companion-hatch to watch his motions .
Parsing [sent. 2411 len. 47]: His first act was to return to the quarter-deck and roll himself in the oil , with an idea of quenching the flames , but this added fuel to them , and the animal roaring in his agony at last jumped into the sea and disappeared .
Parsing [sent. 2412 len. 13]: Having thus rid myself of my intruder I returned to my cooking .
Parsing [sent. 2413 len. 71]: The ship was now clear of ice , the weather was warm , the bodies of my shipmates emitted a fetid smell , but I saw and smelt nothing ; all that I observed was that the barley which had been scattered on the deck by the fowls , had sprung up about the decks , and I congratulated myself upon the variety it would give to my culinary pursuits .
Parsing [sent. 2414 len. 29]: I continued to cook , to eat , and to sleep as before , when a circumstance occurred , which put an end to all my culinary madness .
Parsing [sent. 2415 len. 35]: One night I found the water washing by the side of my standing bed-place in the cabin , and jumping out in alarm to ascertain the cause , I plunged over head and ears .
Parsing [sent. 2416 len. 27]: The fact was , that the ship , when lifted by the ice , had sprung a-leak which had gradually filled her without my perceiving it .
Parsing [sent. 2417 len. 21]: My fear of drowning was so great , that I ran into the very danger which I would have avoided .
Parsing [sent. 2418 len. 84]: I darted out of the cabin windows into the sea , whereas had I gone upon deck I should have been safe : for a little reflection might have told me that a vessel laden with oil could not have sunk -- but reflection came too late , and benumbed with the coldness of the waters , I could have struggled but a few seconds more , when I suddenly came in contact with a spar somewhat bigger than a boat 's mast .
Parsing [sent. 2419 len. 53]: I seized it to support myself , and was surprised at finding it jerked from me occasionally , as if there was somebody else who had hold of it , and who wished to force me to let it go ; but it was quite dark , and I could distinguish nothing .
Parsing [sent. 2420 len. 22]: I clung to it until daylight appeared , when what was my horror to perceive an enormous shark close to me .
Parsing [sent. 2421 len. 53]: I nearly let go my hold and sunk , so paralysed was I with fear , I anticipated every moment to feel his teeth crushing me in half , and I shut my eyes that I might not add to the horrors of my death by being a witness to the means .
Parsing [sent. 2422 len. 28]: Some minutes had elapsed , which appeared to me as so many hours , when surprised at being still alive , I ventured to open my eyes .
Parsing [sent. 2423 len. 48]: The shark was still at the same distance from me , and on examination I perceived that the boat 's mast or spar , to which I was clinging , had been passed through his nose in a transverse direction , being exactly balanced on either side .
Parsing [sent. 2424 len. 22]: The shark was of the description found in the North Seas , which is called by the sailors the blind shark .
Parsing [sent. 2425 len. 29]: I now perfectly understood that he had been caught and _ spritsail yarded _ , as the seamen term it , and then turned adrift for their diversion .
Parsing [sent. 2426 len. 30]: The buoyancy of the spar prevents the animal from sinking down under the water , and this punishment of their dreaded enemy is a very favourite amusement of sailors .
Parsing [sent. 2427 len. 50]: I summoned up all my courage , and being tired of holding on by the spar , resolved to mount upon his back , which I accomplished without difficulty , and I found the seat on his shoulders before the dorsal fin , not only secure but very comfortable .
Parsing [sent. 2428 len. 28]: The animal , unaccustomed to carry weight , made several attempts to get rid of me , but not being able to sink I retained my seat .
Parsing [sent. 2429 len. 25]: He then increased his velocity , and we went on over a smooth sea , at the rate of about three knots an hour .
Parsing [sent. 2430 len. 45]: For two days I continued my course to the southward , upon my novel conveyances during which I had nothing to eat except a few small barnacles , and some parasitical vermin , peculiar to the animal , which I discovered under his fins .
Parsing [sent. 2431 len. 44]: I also found a small _ remora _ , or sucking fish , near his tail , but when I put it to my mouth , it fixed itself so firmly on both my lips that I thought they were sealed for ever .
Parsing [sent. 2432 len. 46]: No force could detach it , and there it hung like a padlock for many hours , to my great mortification and annoyance , but at last it died from being so long out of water , and when it dropped off I devoured it .
Parsing [sent. 2433 len. 28]: On the third day I observed land at a distance ; it appeared to be an island , but I had no idea what it could be .
Parsing [sent. 2434 len. 53]: My steed continued his course straight towards it , and being blind ran his nose right upon the shore ; before he found out his mistake I slipped off his back , and climbing the steep side of the island , was once more , as I thought , on terra firma .
Parsing [sent. 2435 len. 5]: Tired with long watching .
Parsing [sent. 2436 len. 8]: I lay down and fell fast asleep .
Parsing [sent. 2437 len. 38]: I was awakened by something touching me on the shoulder , and opening my eyes , I perceived that I was surrounded by several people , whom I naturally inferred to be the natives of the island .
Parsing [sent. 2438 len. 50]: They were clad in dresses , which appeared to me to be made of black leather , consisting of a pair of trousers , and a long pea-jacket , very similar to those worn by the Esquimaux Indians , which we occasionally fell in with in the Northern Ocean .
Parsing [sent. 2439 len. 17]: They each held a long harpoon , formed entirely of bone , in their right hands .
Parsing [sent. 2440 len. 34]: I was not a little surprised at being addressed in the Patois dialect of the Basques in my own country , which is spoken about Bayonne and other parts adjacent to the Pyrenees .
Parsing [sent. 2441 len. 52]: To their questions I answered , that I was the only survivor of the crew of a whaler , which had been frozen up in the ice , during the winter ; that she had filled with water , and that I had saved myself upon the back of a shark .
Parsing [sent. 2442 len. 45]: They expressed no surprise at my unheard-of conveyance to the island ; on the contrary , they merely observed , that sharks were too vicious to ride ; and asked me to accompany them to their town , an invitation which I gladly accepted .
Parsing [sent. 2443 len. 57]: As I walked along I observed that the island was composed of white porous pumice-stone , without the least symptoms of vegetation ; not even a piece of moss could I discover -- nothing but the bare pumice-stone , with thousands of beautiful green lizards , about ten inches long , playing about in every part .
Parsing [sent. 2444 len. 21]: The road was steep , and in several parts the rock was cut into steps to enable you to ascend .
Parsing [sent. 2445 len. 31]: After an hour 's fatiguing walk , which I never should have accomplished in my weak state , without the assistance of the islanders , we arrived at the summit .
Parsing [sent. 2446 len. 9]: The view which met my eye was striking .
Parsing [sent. 2447 len. 41]: I was on the peak of a chain of hills , forming an immense amphitheatre , encircling a valley which appeared about fifteen miles in diameter , and the major part of which was occupied by a lake of water .
Parsing [sent. 2448 len. 31]: I could discern what appeared to be the habitations of men on different parts of the lake ; but there was not a tree or a shrub to be seen .
Parsing [sent. 2449 len. 30]: `` What , '' demanded I of the man who appeared to take the lead of the rest of the party , `` have you no trees here ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2450 len. 14]: `` None whatever ; and yet we can do very well without them .
Parsing [sent. 2451 len. 20]: Do you not observe that there is no mould ; that the island is composed entirely of pumice-stone ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2452 len. 29]: `` I do , '' replied I. `` Pray what is the name of your barren spot -- and in what part of the world are we ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2453 len. 63]: `` As for its name , we call it Whale Island , '' replied the man ; `` but as for where we are , we can not exactly tell ourselves , for we are a floating island , being composed entirely of pumice-stone , whose specific gravity , as you must know , is much lighter than that of water . ''
Parsing [sent. 2454 len. 20]: `` How strange , '' observed I ; `` I can not believe that you are in earnest . ''
Parsing [sent. 2455 len. 16]: `` And yet not quite so strange as you imagine , '' replied my conductor .
Parsing [sent. 2456 len. 33]: `` If you examine the structure of this island , from where you now stand , you will perceive at once , that it has been the crater of some large volcano .
Parsing [sent. 2457 len. 47]: It is easy to imagine , that after having reared its head above the surface of the sea , by some of those sudden caprices of ever-working nature , the base has again sunk down , leaving the summit of the crater floating on the ocean .
Parsing [sent. 2458 len. 28]: Such is our opinion of the formation of this island ; and I doubt whether your geologists on the continent would produce a more satisfactory theory . ''
Parsing [sent. 2459 len. 3]: `` What ?
Parsing [sent. 2460 len. 9]: you have communicated with Europe , then ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2461 len. 10]: cried I , delighted at the hopes of return .
Parsing [sent. 2462 len. 13]: `` We have had communication , but we do not communicate again .
Parsing [sent. 2463 len. 65]: In the winter time , this island , which , strange as it may appear to you , does not change its position many hundred miles in the course of centuries , is enclosed with the icebergs in the north : when the spring appears , we are disengaged , and then drift a degree or two to the southward , seldom more . ''
Parsing [sent. 2464 len. 13]: `` Are you not then affected by the winds and tides ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2465 len. 22]: `` Of course we are : but there is a universal balance throughout nature , and every thing finds its level .
Parsing [sent. 2466 len. 27]: There is order , when there appears disorder -- and no stream runs in one direction , without a counter stream , to restore the equilibrium .
Parsing [sent. 2467 len. 57]: Upon the whole , what with the under currents , and the changes which continually take place , I should say that we are very little , if at all , affected by the tides -- which may be considered as a sort of exercise , prescribed by nature to keep the ocean in good health .
Parsing [sent. 2468 len. 11]: The same may be affirmed with respect to the winds .
Parsing [sent. 2469 len. 20]: Wind is a substance , as well as water , capable of great expansion , but still a substance .
Parsing [sent. 2470 len. 23]: A certain portion has been allotted to the world for its convenience , and there is a regularity in its apparent variability .
Parsing [sent. 2471 len. 52]: It must be self-evident , when all the wind has been collected to the eastward , by the north-west gales which prevail in winter , that it must be crowded and penned up in that quarter , and , from its known expansive powers , must return and restore the equilibrium .
Parsing [sent. 2472 len. 24]: That is the reason that we have such a long continuance of easterly winds , in the months of February and March . ''
Parsing [sent. 2473 len. 11]: `` You said that you had communication with Europe ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2474 len. 29]: `` We have occasionally visits perforce , from those who are cast away in ships or boats ; but the people who come here , have never returned .
Parsing [sent. 2475 len. 32]: The difficulty of leaving the island is very great : and we flatter ourselves , that few who have remained any time with us , have ever felt the desire . ''
Parsing [sent. 2476 len. 20]: `` What -- not to leave a barren rock , without even a blade of grass upon it . ''
Parsing [sent. 2477 len. 39]: `` Happiness , '' replied my conductor , `` does not consist in the variety of your possessions , but in being contented with what you have ; '' -- and he commenced the descent of the hill .
Parsing [sent. 2478 len. 20]: I followed him in a melancholy mood , for I could imagine little comfort in such a sterile spot .
Parsing [sent. 2479 len. 49]: `` I am not a native of this island , '' observed he , as we walked along ; `` it is more than four hundred years since it was first inhabited , by the crew of a French vessel , which was lost in the Northern ocean .
Parsing [sent. 2480 len. 9]: But I do not wish to leave it .
Parsing [sent. 2481 len. 23]: I was cast on it in a whale-boat , when separated from the ship in a snow-storm , about twenty-five years ago .
Parsing [sent. 2482 len. 33]: I am now a married man , with a family , and am considered one of the wealthiest inhabitants of the island , for I possess between forty and fifty whales . ''
Parsing [sent. 2483 len. 4]: `` Whales ! ''
Parsing [sent. 2484 len. 6]: exclaimed I , with astonishment .
Parsing [sent. 2485 len. 35]: `` Yes , '' replied my conductor , `` whales , which are the staple of this island , and without them we should not be so prosperous and so happy as we are .
Parsing [sent. 2486 len. 38]: But you have much to see and learn ; you will by-and-bye acknowledge that there is nothing existing in the world , which , from necessity and by perseverance , man can not subject to his use .
Parsing [sent. 2487 len. 36]: Yon lake which covers the bottom of our valley , is our source of wealth and comfort , and yields us an increase as plentiful as the most fertile plains of Italy or France . ''
Parsing [sent. 2488 len. 23]: As we arrived close to the foot of the hills , I perceived several black substances on the shores of the lake .
Parsing [sent. 2489 len. 6]: `` Are those whales ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2490 len. 13]: inquired I. `` They were whales , but they are now houses .
Parsing [sent. 2491 len. 31]: That one by itself is mine , which I hope you will consider as yours , until you have made up your mind as to what you will do . ''
Parsing [sent. 2492 len. 29]: We descended to the beach , and his companions , wishing me good morning , left me with my conductor , who led the way to his house .
Parsing [sent. 2493 len. 23]: It was composed of the skin of one entire whale , much larger than ever I had seen in the Northern ocean .
Parsing [sent. 2494 len. 59]: The back-bone and ribs of the animal served as rafters to extend the skin , which wore the resemblance of a long tent ; it was further secured by ropes , formed of the twisted sinews which passed over the top , and were made fast to stakes of bone firmly fixed in the ground on each side .
Parsing [sent. 2495 len. 62]: When I entered , I found to my surprise that there was plenty of light , which was supplied from windows , composed of small panes of whalebone ground down very thin , and at the further end the head and skull of the animal formed a kitchen , the smoke from the fire escaping through the spiracles or breathing-holes above .
Parsing [sent. 2496 len. 50]: On each side of the room into which I was ushered were raised seats , covered with seal skins , and the other end of the house was divided off with a species of black skin , into sleeping apartments for the master of the house and his family .
Parsing [sent. 2497 len. 17]: There was not the least smell , as I anticipated before I entered this strange dwelling-place .
Parsing [sent. 2498 len. 13]: I was introduced to his wife , who welcomed me with cordiality .
Parsing [sent. 2499 len. 56]: She was dressed in the same dark skin as her husband , but of a much finer texture , and had a scarlet cap on her head , as well as scarlet trimmings to the front and bottom of her dress , which on the whole was not only comfortable but becoming in its appearance .
Parsing [sent. 2500 len. 19]: A bowl of milk was presented to me , to refresh me after my walk and long abstinence .
Parsing [sent. 2501 len. 4]: `` How ! ''
Parsing [sent. 2502 len. 12]: observed I , `` have you milk here without pasture ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2503 len. 22]: `` Yes , '' replied my host , `` drink it , and tell me if you think it palatable . ''
Parsing [sent. 2504 len. 29]: I did so , and found it very little different from the asses ' milk of my own country -- perhaps with a little more acidity of taste .
Parsing [sent. 2505 len. 34]: In the mean time several varieties of shellfish , and a large cheese , were placed upon the table , which , as well as the stools , was composed entirely of bone .
Parsing [sent. 2506 len. 7]: `` And cheese , too ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2507 len. 13]: said I. `` Yes , and you will find it not bad .
Parsing [sent. 2508 len. 22]: It is the milk of the whale which you have drank -- and the cheese is prepared from the same . ''
Parsing [sent. 2509 len. 18]: `` Friend Huckaback , '' observed the pacha , `` I think you are telling me lies .
Parsing [sent. 2510 len. 9]: Who ever heard of whale 's milk ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2511 len. 29]: `` Allah forbid that I should attempt to deceive a person of your highness 's judgment ; it could only end in mortification and defeat to myself . ''
Parsing [sent. 2512 len. 11]: `` That 's very true , '' observed the pacha .
Parsing [sent. 2513 len. 51]: `` Your highness has not called to mind , that the whale is what naturalists call a ` hot-blood animal , ' with arteries and circulation of blood similar to the human species ; and that it brings forth its young alive , and nurses it at the breast . ''
Parsing [sent. 2514 len. 9]: `` Very true , '' observed the pacha .
Parsing [sent. 2515 len. 7]: `` I had forgot that . ''
Parsing [sent. 2516 len. 22]: My conductor resumed as follows : `` As I told you before , the whale is the staple of this island .
Parsing [sent. 2517 len. 33]: You observe that his skin serves us as a house ; from his bones we form all our implements -- from his sinews , our thickest ropes down to our finest thread .
Parsing [sent. 2518 len. 41]: The dress we wear is composed of the belly-part of the skin , dressed with a sort of soap , composed of the alkali obtained from the sea-weed which abounds in the lake , and the oil of the whale .
Parsing [sent. 2519 len. 22]: His blubber serves us for fuel and candle ; his flesh for meat , and the milk is invaluable to us .
Parsing [sent. 2520 len. 50]: It is true , we have other resources ; we have our lizards , and a variety of fish and shell fish ; and when we are shut up in the winter among the icebergs , we procure the flesh and skins of the seals and the polar bear .
Parsing [sent. 2521 len. 31]: But we have no vegetable of any kind ; and although the want of bread may at first he unpleasant , a few weeks will reconcile you to the privation .
Parsing [sent. 2522 len. 30]: But it is time to repose after your fatigues -- I will report your arrival to the great harpooner , after I have shown you to your chamber . ''
Parsing [sent. 2523 len. 39]: He then conducted me to an inner room , where I found a couch , composed of the skins of the polar bears , on which I threw myself , and in a few minutes was fast asleep .
Parsing [sent. 2524 len. 10]: The next morning I was awakened by my host .
Parsing [sent. 2525 len. 35]: `` If you wish to see the whales milked , this is the hour that they are called in ; a short walk will explain more to you than many hours ' conversation . ''
Parsing [sent. 2526 len. 14]: I arose perfectly refreshed from my long nap , and followed my conductor .
Parsing [sent. 2527 len. 6]: We passed a large tank .
Parsing [sent. 2528 len. 42]: `` This is our water ; we are obliged not to waste it , although we have a sufficiency ; the tank is coated by a cement , formed of lime , obtained by the burning of the shells of fish .
Parsing [sent. 2529 len. 36]: We make all our vessels , that are submitted to the fire , of the same substance , mixed with pounded lava ; it is burnt in the fire , and glazed with sea-salt . ''
Parsing [sent. 2530 len. 47]: We arrived at the edge of the lake , where we came to a large shallow dock , cut out of the lava in the side , in which were about two dozen young whales , who followed my host as he walked round the edge .
Parsing [sent. 2531 len. 24]: `` These are my calves ; we do not admit the mothers until we have first drawn off what milk we require . ''
Parsing [sent. 2532 len. 46]: Several men now came down to the beach : one of them blew a horn , formed out of a part of the horn of a sea unicorn , and immediately a herd of whales collected at the sound , and swam towards the beach .
Parsing [sent. 2533 len. 42]: They all answered to their names ; and when the men waded in the water up to their knees , quietly grounded on their sides , so as to present one of their udders to them , clear of the water .
Parsing [sent. 2534 len. 32]: This was squeezed by four men , and the contents received into a large pail , composed of the bones of a whale , neatly hooped together by the same substance .
Parsing [sent. 2535 len. 37]: As soon as the breast of the animal was empty , with a lash of its tail it recovered the deep water , and swam round and round in small circles , near to the spot .
Parsing [sent. 2536 len. 34]: `` We always leave one breast for the calf , '' observed my host ; `` when they are all milked , I shall open the pen and let the mothers in . ''
Parsing [sent. 2537 len. 14]: `` What are those enormous whales which are playing at a distance ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2538 len. 23]: `` They are our whale oxen , '' answered my host ; `` we find that they grow to an enormous size .
Parsing [sent. 2539 len. 9]: Our houses are built of their skins . ''
Parsing [sent. 2540 len. 11]: `` Is that a dead whale on the beach ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2541 len. 37]: `` It is one of our whale boats , '' replied he , `` but formed , as you supposed , from the skin of a whale , hardened by frequent applications of oil and lime .
Parsing [sent. 2542 len. 13]: We use them to catch the whales when we want them . ''
Parsing [sent. 2543 len. 11]: `` You do not use the harpoon , then ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2544 len. 45]: `` Only when we kill ; in general we noose the tail , and fasten the rope to one of these boats , which are so buoyant , that the whale can not take it down , and soon tires with his own exertions .
Parsing [sent. 2545 len. 53]: I am now speaking of the males reserved for breeding , or strange whales , who sometimes find their way into our lake during the winter : our own are so domesticated from their infancy , that we have little trouble with them ; but it is time that we return . ''
Parsing [sent. 2546 len. 26]: `` Here , '' observed any host , as we passed a whale-house , `` is one of our manufactories ; we will step in .
Parsing [sent. 2547 len. 19]: This is the common stuff of the country , which is used for partitions in houses , etcetera .
Parsing [sent. 2548 len. 13]: This is a finer sort , such as I wear at present .
Parsing [sent. 2549 len. 18]: Here we have the skin of the whale calf , which is usually worn by the women .
Parsing [sent. 2550 len. 43]: This is the most expensive article of our manufactures ; it is the belly-part of the calf 's skin , which being white , admits of a dye from the murex -- a shell fish , very common on our shores . ''
Parsing [sent. 2551 len. 6]: `` Have you money ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2552 len. 36]: inquired I. `` None -- we exchange ; but the chief article of exchange , and which serves as money , is the whale cheese , which keeps for years , and improves in quality .
Parsing [sent. 2553 len. 18]: That fine cloth is worth eight new cheeses a square yard , which is very dear . ''
Parsing [sent. 2554 len. 20]: We arrived at the house , where we found our repast ready ; an excellent stew received my commendation .
Parsing [sent. 2555 len. 24]: `` It is one of our favourite dishes , '' replied my host ; `` it is made of lizards ' tails . ''
Parsing [sent. 2556 len. 6]: `` Lizards ' tails ! ''
Parsing [sent. 2557 len. 20]: `` Yes ; I am about to procure some for dinner , and you shall see my preserve . ''
Parsing [sent. 2558 len. 37]: In the course of the day I walked with my host a short distance up the hill , when we stopped at a large pit , covered with a net-work , made of whales ' sinews .
Parsing [sent. 2559 len. 26]: The man who accompanied us , descended , and soon returned with a pail full of lizards , confined by a similar net over them .
Parsing [sent. 2560 len. 22]: He then took them out one by one , and pulled their tails , which were immediately left in his hand .
Parsing [sent. 2561 len. 14]: He then notched the stump , and threw the animal into the pit .
Parsing [sent. 2562 len. 12]: `` Of what use is it to return the animals ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2563 len. 15]: observed I. `` Because their tails will grow again , by next year . ''
Parsing [sent. 2564 len. 15]: `` But why , then , were the stumps notched in the middle ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2565 len. 22]: `` That they might have two tails instead of one , which is invariably the case , '' replied my host .
Parsing [sent. 2566 len. 26]: But I will not tire your highness with an account of all that I saw , and which occurred during my stay on that island .
Parsing [sent. 2567 len. 75]: If I were to enter into the excellence of their government , which consisted of a great harpooner , and two councils of first and second harpoons , or of the manners and customs of the inhabitants , ceremonies at births , and marriages , and deaths -- of their amusements , and their ingenious supply of all their wants , it would afford materials for at least two volumes quarto , without margin .
Parsing [sent. 2568 len. 39]: I shall therefore confine myself to stating , that after a sojourn of six months , I became so impatient to quit the island , that I determined to encounter any risk , rather than not accomplish it .
Parsing [sent. 2569 len. 39]: My host , and all the principal inhabitants , finding that no persuasions could induce me to stay , consented at last to furnish me with the means , which I had hit upon to make my escape .
Parsing [sent. 2570 len. 36]: I omitted to mention to your highness , the whales had been rendered so docile , that they not only were used for draught on the lake , but even for carrying on their backs .
Parsing [sent. 2571 len. 61]: I never could be persuaded to mount one , I had such a horror of being seated on a fish 's back , after my travelling on the shark ; but I had often crossed the lake in one of the great whale boats towed by one or two of the animals fastened to it by loops over their tails .
Parsing [sent. 2572 len. 48]: This conveyance suggested to me the idea of my escape , which I proposed to make by means of one of these large whale boats , covered completely in , and to be towed out of the mouth of the lake by one of the draught whales .
Parsing [sent. 2573 len. 67]: At my request , a boat was prepared , and covered in with whalebone windows , to admit light ; a stock of provisions were supplied me sufficient for a long voyage ; and the whale being _ put to _ , I departed amidst the tears and lamentations of the friendly islanders , who looked upon me as a man bent upon my own destruction .
Parsing [sent. 2574 len. 25]: But I was aware that the fishery would soon commence , and had great hopes of being picked up by one of the vessels .
Parsing [sent. 2575 len. 57]: I was soon clear of the lake ; and the lad who was on the back of the draught whale , having towed me out in pursuance of his orders , until the island appeared like a cloud on the horizon , cast me loose and hastened back , that he might return home before dark .
Parsing [sent. 2576 len. 33]: For three weeks I remained in the inside of this enormous boat , or rather I may say fish tossed upon the waves , but without injury , from its extreme buoyancy .
Parsing [sent. 2577 len. 20]: One morning I was awakened from a sound sleep by a sudden blow on the outside of my vessel .
Parsing [sent. 2578 len. 32]: I imagined that I had come in contact with an iceberg , but the sound of voices convinced me , that at last I had fallen in with my fellow creatures .
Parsing [sent. 2579 len. 30]: A harpoon was now driven in , which I narrowly escaped , and a volley of execrations followed , by which I knew immediately that the people were English .
Parsing [sent. 2580 len. 30]: After a few minutes , they commenced sawing a hole in the side of my whale boat ; and a piece being removed , a head was put in .
Parsing [sent. 2581 len. 44]: Fearful of another harpoon , I had raised up my large white bear 's skin as a defence , and the man perceiving it , immediately withdrew his head , swearing that there was a white bear in the belly of the whale .
Parsing [sent. 2582 len. 34]: The boat shoved off and they commenced firing musket balls , which pierced my boat through and through , and I was obliged to lie down at the bottom to save my life .
Parsing [sent. 2583 len. 53]: After about twenty shots , the boat again came along side , and a man , putting his head in , and perceiving me at the bottom of the boat , covered over with the bear 's skin , imagined that the animal had been killed , and reported to his companions .
Parsing [sent. 2584 len. 44]: With some degree of apprehension they climbed in at the hole which they had cut , when I lifted up my bear 's skin , and made my appearance , dressed in the black skin worn by the inhabitants of Whales ' Island .
Parsing [sent. 2585 len. 40]: This frightened them still more ; one roared out that it was the devil , and they all ran to make their escape at the hole by which they entered , but in their eagerness they prevented each other .
Parsing [sent. 2586 len. 44]: It was with difficulty that I convinced them that I was harmless , which I did at last ; and having explained in a few words how I came there , they permitted me to go with them on board of the ship .
Parsing [sent. 2587 len. 36]: The captain was very sulky when he heard the story ; he had imagined it to be a dead whale , and had ordered it to be towed alongside , to cut off the blubber .
Parsing [sent. 2588 len. 37]: Disappointed in his expectations , he swore that I was a Jonas , who had come out of the whale 's belly , and there would be no luck in the ship , if I remained .
Parsing [sent. 2589 len. 52]: The sailors , whose profits in the voyage were regulated by the number of fish taken , thought this an excellent reason for throwing me overboard ; and had there not been two sail in sight , standing towards them , I certainly should have had some more adventures to narrate .
Parsing [sent. 2590 len. 17]: At last they consented to put me on board of one which had hoisted French colours .
Parsing [sent. 2591 len. 16]: She was from Havre , and having twelve fish on board , was returning home .
Parsing [sent. 2592 len. 22]: The captain consented to give me a passage , and in two months I was once more in my native country .
Parsing [sent. 2593 len. 13]: Such , your highness , were the adventures of my third voyage .
Parsing [sent. 2594 len. 27]: `` Well , the story of the island was rather too long , '' observed the Pacha , `` but , altogether , it was amusing .
Parsing [sent. 2595 len. 13]: Mustapha , I think it is worth ten pieces of gold . ''
Parsing [sent. 2596 len. 6]: VOLUME TWO , CHAPTER THREE .
Parsing [sent. 2597 len. 21]: The next day the renegade commenced his fourth voyage , in the following words : -- FOURTH VOYAGE OF HUCKABACK .

Parsing [sent. 2797 len. 5]: FIFTH VOYAGE OF HUCKABACK .
Parsing [sent. 2798 len. 31]: Your highness may be surprised , that being in the possession of wealth , rank , and my charming Cerise , I should have again ventured upon the treacherous ocean .
Parsing [sent. 2799 len. 23]: Of course your highness has heard of the revolution which took place in France , and all the horrors which attended it .
Parsing [sent. 2800 len. 3]: `` France !
Parsing [sent. 2801 len. 24]: Yes , I believe there is a country of that name ; I ca n't say that I ever heard of the revolution .
Parsing [sent. 2802 len. 3]: Holy Prophet !
Parsing [sent. 2803 len. 34]: but these people have strange ideas , '' continued the pacha to the vizier ; `` to imagine that we must know or care about what is going on in their barbarous countries .
Parsing [sent. 2804 len. 7]: You may proceed , Huckaback . ''
Parsing [sent. 2805 len. 25]: It will be necessary to say a few words upon the subject , your highness , but I will be as concise as possible .
Parsing [sent. 2806 len. 52]: One day , a party of men from my native city -LRB- Marseilles -RRB- , dressed in red caps , their shirt sleeves tucked up , and armed with various weapons , surrounded my chateau , insisting upon my immediately informing them whether I was for the summoning of the estates-general .
Parsing [sent. 2807 len. 11]: I answered , most certainly , if they wished it .
Parsing [sent. 2808 len. 8]: They cheered me , and went away .
Parsing [sent. 2809 len. 15]: Shortly afterwards , they came to ascertain if I approved of the national convention .
Parsing [sent. 2810 len. 10]: I answered , that I approved of it excessively .
Parsing [sent. 2811 len. 8]: They were satisfied , and again disappeared .
Parsing [sent. 2812 len. 21]: They came a third time , to inquire if I was a republican , to which I gave the affirmative .
Parsing [sent. 2813 len. 31]: A fourth , to know whether I sided with the Girondists ; I declared myself one of that party , and hoped that I should be asked no more questions .
Parsing [sent. 2814 len. 72]: But before two or three months had passed away , another party came to ascertain whether I was a real Jacobin , which I solemnly pronounced myself to be ; -- a second time , to know whether I thought proper to be called citizen , or have my head cut off ; I declared in favour of the former , and made them a present of my title of marquis .
Parsing [sent. 2815 len. 28]: But at last they surrounded my house with loud cries declaring that I was an aristocrat , and insisted upon carrying my head away upon a pike .
Parsing [sent. 2816 len. 8]: This I considered a subject of remonstrance .
Parsing [sent. 2817 len. 57]: I assured them that I was no aristocrat , although I had purchased the property ; and that , on the contrary , I was a citizen barber from Marseilles ; that I had relinquished the title of marquis , which I had bought with the property , and had therefore no claim whatever to aristocracy .
Parsing [sent. 2818 len. 26]: But they insisted upon proofs , and ordering my valets to bring down the materials , desired me to shave a dozen of their party .
Parsing [sent. 2819 len. 54]: I shaved for my life , and acquitted myself so much to their satisfaction that they all embraced me , and were about to depart , when one of the women demanded that my wife -LRB- whose aristocratical descent was known -RRB- should be surrendered up , as a proof of my sincerity .
Parsing [sent. 2820 len. 58]: We all have our moments of weakness ; had I had the prudence to comply with the request , things would have ended happily , but I was foolish enough , although I had been married twelve years , to demur at the prospect of the head of my charming Cerise being carried away on a pike .
Parsing [sent. 2821 len. 33]: I represented to them -LRB- as she clung to me for protection -RRB- , that although of noble descent , she had reduced herself to my level by marrying a citizen barber .
Parsing [sent. 2822 len. 15]: After a short consultation , they agreed that she was sufficiently degraded to live .
Parsing [sent. 2823 len. 19]: They contented themselves with breaking open my cellar , that they might drink my health , and departed .
Parsing [sent. 2824 len. 15]: But , your highness , I had soon cause to repent of my folly .
Parsing [sent. 2825 len. 24]: Cerise was a charming woman , and an affectionate wife in adversity , but prosperity was her ruin , as well as mine .
Parsing [sent. 2826 len. 47]: She had already had an affair with a Comte , who had lately been dismissed for a handsome young abbe but we do not mind these little _ egaremens _ in our country , and I neither had leisure nor inclination to interfere with her arrangements .
Parsing [sent. 2827 len. 53]: Satisfied with her sincere friendship for me , I could easily forgive a few trifling infidelities , and nothing had disturbed the serenity or gaiety of our establishment until this unfortunate _ expose _ which I was obliged to make , and to prove the truth of in her presence , viz .
Parsing [sent. 2828 len. 7]: that I had been a barber .
Parsing [sent. 2829 len. 42]: Her pride revolted at the idea of having formed such a connection , her feelings towards me were changed to those of the most deadly hatred ; and although I had saved her life , she ungratefully resolved to sacrifice mine .
Parsing [sent. 2830 len. 42]: The little abbe 's head had been taken off several weeks before , and she now formed a liaison with one of the jacobin associes , on condition that he would prove his attachment , by denouncing me as an aristocrat .
Parsing [sent. 2831 len. 18]: Fortunately , I had notice given to me in sufficient time to make my escape to Toulon .
Parsing [sent. 2832 len. 49]: Leaving my wife , and , what was of more consequence , the whole of my property in the hands of the jacobin , I joined the mob and vowing vengeance upon all aristocrats , became one of the most violent leaders of the _ sans culottes _ .
Parsing [sent. 2833 len. 59]: Two months afterwards , when the gates of Toulon had been opened to the army , and I was assisting at a noyade , I had the pleasure of seeing my jacobin _ locum tenens _ , who had been denounced in his turn , tied back to back to a female ; it was my adored Cerise .
Parsing [sent. 2834 len. 19]: I had no time to speak to her , for they were hurried on board of the vessel .
Parsing [sent. 2835 len. 71]: It sank with them , and some hundreds more ; and as the beautiful auburn hair of my wife was borne up from her shoulders , upon which it had been hanging loose , and floated a second or two on the wave after her head had disappeared , I sighed at the remembrance of the transitory enjoyment of competence and love which I had shared with my charming Cerise .
Parsing [sent. 2836 len. 11]: `` And is she really dead now , Huckaback ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2837 len. 4]: inquired the pacha .
Parsing [sent. 2838 len. 11]: `` Yes , your highness , she is . '' ''
Parsing [sent. 2839 len. 10]: _ Allah karim _ -- God is most merciful .
Parsing [sent. 2840 len. 18]: There is an end of that woman at last ; now the story will go on . ''
Parsing [sent. 2841 len. 60]: I have reason to believe that I should have become a person of some consequence if I had been able to remain in France , but another foolish attempt on my part to save the life of the old lawyer at Marseilles , who had assisted me in recovering part of my father 's property , rendered me suspected .
Parsing [sent. 2842 len. 39]: Aware that between suspicion and the guillotine there were but few hours of existence , I contrived to get on board of an Italian brig that had put in from stress of weather , and made my escape .
Parsing [sent. 2843 len. 30]: The vessel was bound to North America for a cargo of salt fish , to be consumed on the ensuing Lent , and had a crew of fifteen men .
Parsing [sent. 2844 len. 38]: The captain was very ill when we sailed , owing , as he said , to a cup of wine which his wife had mixed with her tears , and persuaded him to drink at their parting .
Parsing [sent. 2845 len. 45]: He gradually declined as we proceeded on our voyage , until at last he was not able to quit his bed ; and no person on board except myself having any knowledge of keeping a ship 's reckoning , that duty devolved upon me .
Parsing [sent. 2846 len. 13]: A few days before his death , the captain sent for me .
Parsing [sent. 2847 len. 31]: `` Francois , '' said he , `` my wife has poisoned me , that I might not return to interrupt a connection which she had formed during my absence .
Parsing [sent. 2848 len. 15]: I have no children , and no relations that have ever cared for me .
Parsing [sent. 2849 len. 53]: I am the owner of the cargo , as well as the captain of this vessel , and it is my intention to make it over to you ; I consider that you have the greatest claim to it , as there is nobody on board except yourself who can navigate her .
Parsing [sent. 2850 len. 51]: Understand me , it is not out of any particular regard , so much as to prevent my wife from obtaining my property , that I select you as my heir ; you have , therefore , to thank Heaven for your good fortune , more than you have me .

Parsing [sent. 2852 len. 41]: I readily made the promise which he required , and the captain drew up a will , which he read and executed before the whole of the crew , by which the vessel and cargo were made over to me .
Parsing [sent. 2853 len. 6]: Two days afterwards he expired .
Parsing [sent. 2854 len. 13]: We sewed him up in a hammock , and threw him overboard .
Parsing [sent. 2855 len. 23]: Although it was quite calm at the time , a gale sprung up immediately afterwards , which eventually increased to a hurricane .
Parsing [sent. 2856 len. 38]: We were obliged to bear up , and for several days scudded under bare poles , until I found that we were in the very centre of the Atlantic , out of the track of any vessels .
Parsing [sent. 2857 len. 17]: Gradually the weather became more settled , and we again spread our canvas to the breeze .
Parsing [sent. 2858 len. 42]: To my surprise , I observed , that although by my reckoning we were nearly one thousand miles from any land , several aquatic birds were hovering about the ship , of a description that seldom go far from the shore .
Parsing [sent. 2859 len. 20]: I watched them as the sun went down , and perceived that they took their flight to the south-east .
Parsing [sent. 2860 len. 62]: Anxious to discover any land , not hitherto described , I steered the ship in that direction during the night , and early on the next morning we found ourselves close to an island , apparently ten or fifteen miles long , very high , and of a conical shape , which I knew was not laid down upon any chart .
Parsing [sent. 2861 len. 41]: I resolved to examine it , and dropped my anchor in a small bay , at the bottom of which a few houses announced that it was inhabited ; although I could not distinguish any thing like guns or fortification .
Parsing [sent. 2862 len. 20]: We had not furled our sails , when a boat shoved off from the shore and pulled towards us .
Parsing [sent. 2863 len. 29]: She soon came alongside , and astonished us as much by the peculiarity of her structure , as by the appearance of the people who were on board .
Parsing [sent. 2864 len. 20]: She was a wide canoe , very beautifully carved and inlaid , or rather veneered , with gold ornaments .
Parsing [sent. 2865 len. 38]: She had a flag , hoisted to a staff , hanging over the stern , the field of which was white , with a representation of a fountain , worked in gold thread , in the centre .
Parsing [sent. 2866 len. 28]: The three men who were in her , particularly the one seated in the stern sheets , were very richly attired in dresses worked in gold thread .
Parsing [sent. 2867 len. 42]: But what astonished us more than all was the peculiarity of their complexions , which , although they were very well-featured men , were of a beautiful light blue -- their eyes black , and their hair of a rich auburn .
Parsing [sent. 2868 len. 25]: The personage in the stern sheets ascended the side , and addressing me in excellent Portuguese , inquired if I could speak the language .
Parsing [sent. 2869 len. 64]: I answered in the affirmative , and he then welcomed us in the name of the king , upon my arrival at the island -- asking me the number of my crew , whether I had any sick on board , and many other particulars , all of which he noted down upon tablets of gold , with a piece of red cinnabar .
Parsing [sent. 2870 len. 73]: Having replied to all his interrogations , I then obtained from him the following particulars ; viz. , That the island had been originally peopled by one of the ships belonging to Vasco de Gama 's squadron , which , returning from the East Indies laden with the produce of the east , and specimens of the various inhabitants of the newly discovered territories , had been cast away and utterly wrecked .
Parsing [sent. 2871 len. 39]: That the island , which otherwise was fertile and well-stocked , was one mine of gold , which in the absence of other metals , they were necessitated to employ for every article and utensil in common use .
Parsing [sent. 2872 len. 52]: But the greatest curiosity which the island contained , was a fountain of water at the foot of the centre peak , of a beautiful colour , and producing longevity to those who drank of it , from which it had received the name of the Isle of the Golden Fountain .
Parsing [sent. 2873 len. 77]: That when they had landed , about three hundred years ago , they consisted of various nations and colours , male and female ; but the climate and the use of the waters , had , in the course of time , produced the change in their complexions which we beheld , and all the inhabitants were now of that peculiar tint , with the exception that the females were not so dark as the men .
Parsing [sent. 2874 len. 59]: Few ships had ever touched there ; and the crews of those who had fallen in with the island , had preferred remaining , which accounted for its being so totally unknown : that the king was very partial to strangers , and always received them at his palace , which was built close to the Golden Fountain .
Parsing [sent. 2875 len. 59]: He concluded by requesting me to accompany him on shore , and pay my respects -- stating , that if I wished to quit the island , his majesty would permit me to load my vessel with as much as she could carry of the metal so precious in other countries , but so little valued in this .
Parsing [sent. 2876 len. 12]: I must acknowledge that I was quite overjoyed at his narration .
Parsing [sent. 2877 len. 44]: I considered my fortune to be made , and hastened to accompany the ambassador , who stated that the king would not be pleased if I did not permit the major part of my ship 's company to attend me to the palace .
Parsing [sent. 2878 len. 57]: As the men were very eager to go on shore after the account which they had heard , and he assured me that the wind never blew home in the bay , which was on the lee-side of the island , I consented to their wishes , and allowed all but two to quit the vessel .
Parsing [sent. 2879 len. 65]: We were much surprised when we landed at the village , to perceive that even the pig-troughs , posts , and rails , and indeed every article in which metal could be employed , were of solid gold ; but we had not time for examination , as we found several sledges , drawn by small bullocks , waiting for us near the beach .
Parsing [sent. 2880 len. 70]: We mounted , and the animals set off in a swift canter , upon a smooth and ascending road , and in less than two hours we arrived at the king 's palace , which was an extensive building , not very remarkable in its structure , excepting the unusual sight of the large columns of gold , supporting the porticos , which extended from it on every side .
Parsing [sent. 2881 len. 26]: But when we had alighted and were proceeding through the porticos , I was astonished at the wonderful finish of the statues which embellished them .
Parsing [sent. 2882 len. 36]: They were mounted on plinths of the burnished metal , and carved out of a sort of light blue chalcedony , which , joined with their masterly execution , gave them the appearance of life .
Parsing [sent. 2883 len. 28]: I was surprised at the strange attitudes which the sculptors had chosen to represent , all more or less distorted , although the human proportions were admirable .
Parsing [sent. 2884 len. 32]: Some appeared as if they had been placed on their legs when asleep , others laughing or crying , nay , one or two were represented in the act of vomiting .
Parsing [sent. 2885 len. 55]: Amongst the whole I could not perceive one image in which the human form was represented in a noble or graceful posture , and I pitied the taste of those who could have employed workmen of such extraordinary talents in representing the image of his Maker , under such a degrading variety of postures .
Parsing [sent. 2886 len. 51]: I was about to make this remark to my conductor , but I was checked by the remembrance , that I was in a king 's palace , not in a studio ; and that kings have their fancies , which they are not inclined to submit to public criticism .
Parsing [sent. 2887 len. 35]: When we arrived at the end of the portico , two lofty doors were thrown open , and we were struck dumb with the magnificence of the scene which presented itself to our eyes .
Parsing [sent. 2888 len. 78]: The king was seated on a throne of the most splendid workmanship ; the precious metal had been oxidised to every shade of colour , and was wrought in beautiful mosaic : the walls and ceiling were entirely covered with the same , in some parts burnished , to reflect as mirrors , in others elaborately carved in ornamental fretwork , as peculiar from the elegance of its design , as from the superiority of its execution .
Parsing [sent. 2889 len. 68]: On each side of the throne extending to the door at which we entered , were a row of ladies , and behind them raised on a platform about two feet higher , another row of courtiers -- all dressed in stuffs of cloth of gold , which were embroidered with flowers of variously coloured metal , so as to present the most perfect imitation of nature .
Parsing [sent. 2890 len. 96]: The women were very fair compared to the men , and their cerulean tint was far from being disagreeable , as it gave a transparency to their complexions ; but none of them could be compared to the king 's daughter , who was nearly white , and of the most perfect symmetry in feature and in form ; her auburn hair was so long , that it hung down to the bottom of her dress , and was ornamented with small chains and ornaments of polished steel , which were entwined in its tresses .
Parsing [sent. 2891 len. 46]: She sat at the foot of the throne , near to the king , and I was so astonished at her heavenly appearance , that I could not remember the compliments which I had intended to pay his majesty , but remained speechless before him .
Parsing [sent. 2892 len. 48]: The king received us very graciously , asking me many questions , and broke up the audience -LRB- after half an hour -RRB- , desiring some of the handsomest ladies to select one of my companions , and each hold herself responsible for his comfort and amusement .
Parsing [sent. 2893 len. 22]: I forgot to mention , that as every country has its peculiar customs , one here appeared to me very singular .
Parsing [sent. 2894 len. 44]: When I asked the gentleman usher what was the usual homage paid to the king of the country , he informed me that you advanced your hand before you , on a level with your face , and snapped your fingers at him .
Parsing [sent. 2895 len. 17]: That the louder you could snap them , the more accomplished and elegant you were considered .
Parsing [sent. 2896 len. 42]: But in my confusion I quite forgot his injunctions ; and it was not until the ladies all snapped their fingers in obedience to the commands of their sovereign , that I recollected the omission which I had been guilty of .
Parsing [sent. 2897 len. 41]: Before the king retired , he intimated that he expected we should take up our abodes at the palace for some days , and we should have the honour of sitting at his table , in the afternoon 's banquet .
Parsing [sent. 2898 len. 43]: The whole of the company separated ; those who had charge of my companions leading them different ways , leaving me alone with the princess , who had risen from her seat when directed by her father to take charge of me .
Parsing [sent. 2899 len. 36]: I could have fallen down and worshipped her : as it was , I involuntarily dropped on one knee , and looked up in her face as if I had been contemplating a celestial visitant .
Parsing [sent. 2900 len. 29]: She smiled , and addressed me : `` I am ordered to attend to your happiness and comfort , and I obey my father 's commands with pleasure .

Parsing [sent. 2902 len. 36]: I continued in my position at her feet , and encouraged by her urbanity , poured forth a torrent of what to the many are considered compliments , but which to her were but truths .
Parsing [sent. 2903 len. 39]: I became eloquent from excitation ; and being at this time , as I before observed to your highness , a very personable man , I perceived that she was pleased with my efforts to obtain her favour .
Parsing [sent. 2904 len. 42]: `` I have more than once had this duty allotted to me , when strangers have visited the island , '' observed she ; `` but I have always been wearied , and have called in my women to assist me .
Parsing [sent. 2905 len. 36]: I have never yet seen one like you ; you are gentle , and of a very different description from those who generally have been introduced as the captains of vessels which have arrived here .

Parsing [sent. 2909 len. 15]: O that your task might be continued for the term of my existence ! ''

Parsing [sent. 2911 len. 26]: Come , sir , permit me to obey my father 's commands , and try to beguile the hours by contributing to your amusement . ''
Parsing [sent. 2912 len. 71]: Offering me her hand , which I respectfully raised to my lips , she then conducted me over the palace , directing my attention to every object that she considered worthy of notice ; and we had passed two or three hours in conversation , and remarks upon the objects before us , when I expressed my wish to behold the curious fountain from which the island took its name .
Parsing [sent. 2913 len. 19]: `` I shall obey you , '' replied she : and again her face assumed a mournful cast .

Parsing [sent. 2915 len. 37]: The water of it , when in a body , shone with all the colours of the rainbow , and the sparkling drops which were thrown out on every side were brilliant as the purest gold .
Parsing [sent. 2916 len. 5]: `` How beautiful ! ''
Parsing [sent. 2917 len. 10]: exclaimed I , after some minutes of silent admiration .
Parsing [sent. 2918 len. 12]: `` These , then , are the waters of longevity . ''

Parsing [sent. 2922 len. 53]: I promised that I would , and we continued our walk to the porticos of the palace , where I pointed to the statues of blue chalcedony , and begged her to inform me by whom they had been executed , and why they were all in such grotesque and absurd positions .
Parsing [sent. 2923 len. 21]: `` That is a question which I can not answer , further than that they were made in the island .

Parsing [sent. 2928 len. 17]: She shook her head , as if to rebuke me , and I said no more .
Parsing [sent. 2929 len. 55]: When we had finished the banquet , his majesty ordered the water of the golden fountain to be produced , which it immediately was , by those in attendance , and extolling its virtues , desired a cup to be filled for each guest , which was handed to him by the attendant ladies .
Parsing [sent. 2930 len. 30]: As the princess presented the cup , she contrived to press one of her fingers against mine , before she removed them , to remind me of my promise .
Parsing [sent. 2931 len. 25]: I drank but sparingly , but the effects were instantaneous -- my spirits rose buoyant , and I felt a sort of intellectual intoxication .
Parsing [sent. 2932 len. 36]: At a sign made by the king , the ladies now took their seats beside us , and by their attention and caresses increased the desire for the water , which they supplied in abundance .
Parsing [sent. 2933 len. 55]: I must confess that at each sip that I took , the princess , who had taken her seat by me , appeared so much more charming in my eyes , that notwithstanding the repeated pressure of her foot to remind me of my promise , I could not resist the impulse to drink .
Parsing [sent. 2934 len. 40]: The boatswain and one of the seamen were very drunken characters , and had very soon poured down so much of the water , that they dropped off their stools on the marble pavement , without sense or motion .
Parsing [sent. 2935 len. 67]: This recalled me to my senses , which were rapidly stealing away ; I rose from my seat , and pointing out to my companions that it would ill become them to intoxicate themselves in the presence of his majesty , requested that they would drink no more , but leave the table before they were incapacitated from paying the proper attentions to their fair conductors .
Parsing [sent. 2936 len. 37]: The last argument had more weight than the first ; and notwithstanding the remonstrances of the king , who showed the greatest anxiety that we should remain , the party rose from the table and separated .
Parsing [sent. 2937 len. 26]: The two men who were intoxicated were carried away by some of the courtiers , and the king with marks of displeasure quitted the hall .
Parsing [sent. 2938 len. 55]: I was again left alone with my charming princess , and inflamed with the exhilarating draught which I had taken , I threw myself at her feet , declaring my violent passion , and my wish never to quit the island , if I could be blessed with a reciprocal feeling on her part .
Parsing [sent. 2939 len. 38]: I perceived that I had made an impression ; and following up my success , I protested and she listened , until the evening closed in and found us still seated upon the steps of the throne .
Parsing [sent. 2940 len. 42]: At last she rose and said , `` I know not whether you be sincere in what you say , but I must acknowledge that I hope you are ; and I shall be very miserable if it should prove otherwise .
Parsing [sent. 2941 len. 17]: But you are now under the effects of the intoxicating water , and may deceive yourself .
Parsing [sent. 2942 len. 28]: Come , sir , it is time that I conduct you to your chamber , where you must sleep away the exhilarating effects of the golden fountain .
Parsing [sent. 2943 len. 21]: To-morrow morning , if you are of the same opinion , I may be induced to make a discovery . ''
Parsing [sent. 2944 len. 16]: The next morning I woke without any headache from the intemperance of the previous night .
Parsing [sent. 2945 len. 13]: As soon as I quitted the apartment I met the princess outside .
Parsing [sent. 2946 len. 41]: `` I am still in the same mind , dear princess , '' said I , implanting a kiss upon her hand , `` to live for you alone , or die if I can not remain with you . ''
Parsing [sent. 2947 len. 32]: She smiled , and answered , `` Then for you will I sacrifice every thing ; for until I beheld you , I never was aware that I had a heart .
Parsing [sent. 2948 len. 12]: Rise and follow me , and you shall know all . ''
Parsing [sent. 2949 len. 36]: We passed the large hall , with which the whole of the bed-chambers communicated , and she conducted me through a dark passage to a room , in which were several golden plinths without statues .
Parsing [sent. 2950 len. 36]: At the further end of it I perceived , to my horror , that two of them were already occupied with the forms of the boatswain and sailor who had been intoxicated the night before .
Parsing [sent. 2951 len. 19]: They were now changed into the same blue chalcedony of which the statues in the porticos were composed .
Parsing [sent. 2952 len. 8]: `` Do you recognise these figures ? ''
Parsing [sent. 2953 len. 4]: inquired the princess .
Parsing [sent. 2954 len. 12]: `` I do , indeed , '' answered I with amazement .
Parsing [sent. 2955 len. 21]: `` Such are the effects , '' continued she , `` of intoxication from the water of the golden fountain .
Parsing [sent. 2956 len. 44]: They contain in solution so large a quantity of the matter which by mineralogists is denominated silex , that once allow the senses to be overpowered by repeated draughts , and in a few hours the effects which you behold will be produced .
Parsing [sent. 2957 len. 45]: It is by these means that my father has obtained the variety and number of statues which you have seen -- all of whom were once visitors to the island in different ships , not one of the crews of which have ever returned .
Parsing [sent. 2958 len. 21]: It has also the power of producing longevity , and hardening the hearts of those who use it in moderation .
