Parsing [sent. 3127 len. 9]: For some time the men seemed perfectly contented .
Parsing [sent. 3128 len. 43]: We had plenty of stores in the ship of every description : the cargo I had taken on board was chiefly manufactures , and as the island provided fresh meat , fish , and fruit , they were in want of nothing .
Parsing [sent. 3129 len. 22]: But sailors are such changeable and restless beings , that I really believe they would soon be tired of Paradise itself .
Parsing [sent. 3130 len. 34]: After a sojourn of nine months , during which they perhaps lived better than they ever had before , they began to murmur and talk of getting away in some manner or another .
Parsing [sent. 3131 len. 73]: As my cargo was valuable , I was in hopes that a vessel would visit the island , and take it on board : I therefore made every remonstrance that I could imagine to induce them to wait some time longer ; but they would not listen to me , and made preparations for building a vessel at the weather-side of the island , out of the materials that the ship afforded .
Parsing [sent. 3132 len. 48]: The reason why they chose the weather side was , that they perceived that the island only increased to leeward ; whereas to windward it was a perpendicular rock of coral , which you could not obtain bottom alongside of , with two hundred fathoms of line .
Parsing [sent. 3133 len. 46]: They had cut a slip out of the rock , and were already occupied with driving out the bolts and fastenings of the ship that was shored up in the woods , when one evening we perceived a large fleet of canoes coming towards us .
Parsing [sent. 3134 len. 64]: As I knew that I could not be far from the Sandwich Islands , I immediately pronounced them to come from that quarter , in which supposition I was correct ; for although the island was not inhabited , the islanders had for some years been aware of its existence , and came to gather the crop of cocoa-nuts which it annually produced .
Parsing [sent. 3135 len. 71]: I advised my men to keep quiet in the woods , removing the tents and every object that might create suspicion of our being on the island ; but they were of a different opinion , and as they had lately discovered the means of collecting the toddy from the cocoa-nut trees , and distilling arrack , they had been constantly drunk , mutinous , and regardless of my authority .
Parsing [sent. 3136 len. 45]: They thought it would be much easier to take the large canoes from the islanders , and appropriate them to their own use , than to build a vessel , and notwithstanding my entreaties , they persisted in their resolution to make the attempt .
Parsing [sent. 3137 len. 39]: As the canoes approached , we counted fourteen , all of a very large size , and with my glass I could distinguish that they had fifty or sixty persons on board of each , including the women .
Parsing [sent. 3138 len. 51]: I pointed this out to the sailors , stating that I did not believe there were more than ten women in each canoe , so that the men must amount to seven hundred , a force much too large to give them any chance of success in their rash intentions .
Parsing [sent. 3139 len. 46]: But I did more harm than good ; the mention of the women seemed to inspire them with fresh ardour , and they vowed that they would kill all the men , and then would be content to remain on the island with the women .
Parsing [sent. 3140 len. 28]: They armed themselves with muskets , and retired among the trees as the canoes approached , fearful that the islanders would not land if they were discovered .
Parsing [sent. 3141 len. 42]: The canoes ran between the reefs , and in a few minutes the whole of the islanders disembarked ; not conceiving it necessary to leave any but the women in the canoes , the water being as smooth as a fish-pond .
Parsing [sent. 3142 len. 77]: The arrangements of my men were certainly very good : they allowed the islanders to go up to the tents , which were now more than a mile from the beach , and then walking down under cover of the trees , rushed to the canoes , and putting one man in each with their muskets and ammunition , shoved them off and made them fast to the coral rocks , about two hundred yards distant .
Parsing [sent. 3143 len. 26]: The screams of the women , and the shoving off of the canoes , alarmed the men , who hastened down to ascertain the cause .
Parsing [sent. 3144 len. 37]: As soon as they came within half musket shot , the sailors who were on shore , amounting to twenty-five , fired a volley out of the wood , which killed and wounded a great number .
Parsing [sent. 3145 len. 14]: The islanders retreated in confusion , then gave a loud shout and advanced .
Parsing [sent. 3146 len. 17]: Another volley was fired , and they again retreated , bearing off their killed and wounded .
Parsing [sent. 3147 len. 38]: They now held a consultation , which ended in their dividing into two bodies , one of which separated from the other , so that they might attack the party in the wood from two different points .
Parsing [sent. 3148 len. 49]: In the meantime several of the women leaped overboard and swam on shore , and the men in the boats were so busy in preventing the others from following , that they could give no assistance to the party in the wood , although they were within musket-shot .
Parsing [sent. 3149 len. 37]: The conduct of the islanders puzzled our men ; and although I had taken no part in this murderous attack , yet as I considered my life at stake , I thought that I must assist .
Parsing [sent. 3150 len. 30]: I therefore advised them to retreat to the ship , which , if they once gained possession of , they would be enabled to keep the islanders at bay .
Parsing [sent. 3151 len. 44]: My advice was followed , and creeping through the thick we reached the ship in safety , having climbed up by rope-ladders , which were hanging from her , to enable us to go on board , to fetch any articles we required .
Parsing [sent. 3152 len. 12]: We hauled them up after us , and waited the issue .
Parsing [sent. 3153 len. 35]: In a few minutes , one of the parties of the islanders came up , and seeing the ship with us on board , gave a loud yell , and let fly their spears .
Parsing [sent. 3154 len. 29]: We returned a volley which killed many , but they were very brave , and continued the attack although we fired twenty or thirty rounds with great execution .
Parsing [sent. 3155 len. 54]: The other party now came up , and the conflict continued ; they made every attempt to climb the stern and sides of the vessel , but were repulsed ; and as the evening closed in , they retired taking away their killed and wounded , which we estimated at two hundred men .
Parsing [sent. 3156 len. 35]: When they retreated , we fired some of our large guns in that direction , as much to frighten the islanders , as to let our comrades in the canoes know where we were .
Parsing [sent. 3157 len. 16]: We kept a sharp look out till dark , but saw no more of them .
Parsing [sent. 3158 len. 44]: I proposed that we should attempt to communicate with the men in the canoes , and desire them to permit some of them to drift on shore after taking out the women , as the islanders would then in all probability go away .
Parsing [sent. 3159 len. 49]: But as the men very justly remarked , nobody in the first place would venture on such a dangerous service , and in the next , if the islanders obtained some of their canoes , they would attack the others and overpower the sailors that were in them .
Parsing [sent. 3160 len. 7]: This plan was therefore justly overruled .
Parsing [sent. 3161 len. 55]: I then proposed that one man should steal down to the beach , swim off , and desire the fourteen men to take all the women into one canoe , and pull round to the north side of the island during the night , leaving the remainder for the islanders to go away in .
Parsing [sent. 3162 len. 48]: This was considered a good scheme , but no one would volunteer ; and , as I had proposed it , I thought that I was in honour bound to go , as otherwise the men would , in future , have had no opinion of me .
Parsing [sent. 3163 len. 20]: I therefore stated my intention , and taking my musket and ammunition , I slipped down by a rope .
Parsing [sent. 3164 len. 21]: As soon as I was on my legs , I perceived something crawling out of the wood towards the ship .
Parsing [sent. 3165 len. 31]: I could not exactly decipher what it was , so I crept under the counter of the vessel , where it was so dark that I could not be distinguished .
Parsing [sent. 3166 len. 41]: As it approached , I made it out to be one of the islanders with a faggot of wood on his back ; he placed it close to the side of the vessel , and then crawled back as before .
Parsing [sent. 3167 len. 48]: I now perceived that there were hundreds of these faggots about the ship , which the islanders had contrived to carry there during the night ; for although the moon was up , yet the vessel was so inclosed with trees that the light did not penetrate .
Parsing [sent. 3168 len. 53]: I immediately comprehended that it was their intention to set fire to the vessel , and I was thinking of communicating the information to my companions on board , when two more crawled from the woods , and deposited their bundles so close to me , that we were nearly in contact .
Parsing [sent. 3169 len. 38]: I therefore was obliged to leave those who were on board to make the best of it , and imitating the islanders , I crawled from the vessel into the brushwood , trailing the gun after me .
Parsing [sent. 3170 len. 59]: It was fortunate that I took this precaution , for in the very part of the wood where I crept to , there were dozens of them making up faggots , but it was too thick with underwood , and too dark to distinguish any thing , although I heard them close to me breaking off the branches .
Parsing [sent. 3171 len. 33]: I did the same as I went on , to avoid discovery , until I had passed by them , when I continued my route to where the canoes had been left .
Parsing [sent. 3172 len. 60]: I arrived in safety at the outskirts of the wood close to the beach , and perceived the canoes still lying at the rocks , to which they had been taken ; but the moon shone bright , and I hesitated to walk out in the light , until I ascertained whether there were any islanders on the beach .
Parsing [sent. 3173 len. 45]: As I waited a short time in the dark shade of the trees , close to one of the springs of fresh water , I heard a moan close to me , and looking in that direction I perceived a body on the ground .
Parsing [sent. 3174 len. 23]: I went towards it , and could distinguish very plainly that it was one of the women who had swam on shore .
Parsing [sent. 3175 len. 36]: She was nearly lifeless , and feeling , as every man must have done , compassion at her unfortunate condition , I knelt down by her to see if I could afford her any assistance .
Parsing [sent. 3176 len. 41]: As she had very little clothes round her body , I discovered , by passing my hand over her , that she was wounded with a musket-ball above the knee , and was exhausted from pain and loss of blood .
Parsing [sent. 3177 len. 40]: I tore my neck-cloth and shirt into bandages , and bound up her leg ; I then fetched some water from the spring in my hat , which I poured into her mouth , and threw over her face .
Parsing [sent. 3178 len. 63]: She appeared to recover and I felt happy that I had been of some use , and not being able to descry any of the islanders , was proceeding to the beach , that I might swim off to the canoes , when just as I walked out of the shade , two or three muskets were fired by those on board .
Parsing [sent. 3179 len. 26]: These were followed by others , and loud yells from the islanders , who had swum off in hundreds , and were attacking our people .
Parsing [sent. 3180 len. 45]: The conflict was very short , for the men , not being able to load their muskets quickly enough , were overpowered by the islanders , who climbed into the canoes ; and in a few minutes they were all paddled to the beach .
Parsing [sent. 3181 len. 47]: I now thought that it was all over with my men on board of the ship , and so it proved ; for an hour before daylight the islanders lighted the faggots , and , at the same time , attacked the vessel with great fury .
Parsing [sent. 3182 len. 87]: The fire continued to blaze higher and higher , the muskets were constantly discharging , and the shouts and yells continued for about an hour , when I heard no more reports from the muskets , and took it for granted that my men were overcome , which was the case , as I afterwards found out ; many were killed by the spears when on board , others when they leaped from the vessel to avoid the flames , and the remainder had been suffocated .
Parsing [sent. 3183 len. 37]: As the sun rose above the horizon , a loud explosion took place , by which I knew that the flames had communicated with the magazine , and that the ship had been blown to atoms .
Parsing [sent. 3184 len. 17]: I determined to hide myself in the bushes , with the hope of not being discovered .
Parsing [sent. 3185 len. 21]: Before I went , I made a hasty visit to the poor wounded woman , to see how she was .
Parsing [sent. 3186 len. 27]: It was broad daylight , and I found that I had afforded succour to a very beautiful young girl , about sixteen or seventeen years old .
Parsing [sent. 3187 len. 29]: As she still appeared faint , I brought her some more water , and when I gave it to her , she expressed her gratitude with her eyes .
Parsing [sent. 3188 len. 27]: Examining the bandages , which had slipped a little on one side , I replaced them , and then darted into the thickest of the underwood .
Parsing [sent. 3189 len. 65]: As I pressed on , bent half double , my head suddenly came in contact with something hard ; I looked up , and found that it was the head of one of the islanders , who was also forcing his way through the bushes , an immense , powerful man , who immediately sprung upon me , and pinned me to the ground .
Parsing [sent. 3190 len. 18]: He was followed by several others who came to his assistance , and all resistance was useless .
Parsing [sent. 3191 len. 39]: They pulled some of the creeping withies , that grow in those countries , and bound me hand and foot ; then selecting a large pole , they made me fast to it , and carried me away .
Parsing [sent. 3192 len. 21]: When they arrived at the beach , I was laid down on my back , exposed to the burning sun .
Parsing [sent. 3193 len. 40]: Left to my own reflections , and calling to mind all that I could recollect from the voyages and travels which I had read , I concluded that I was to be made a sacrifice of to their gods .
Parsing [sent. 3194 len. 18]: I prayed to Heaven for mercy , and resigned myself to my fate , which appeared inevitable .
Parsing [sent. 3195 len. 14]: The islanders had all assembled on the beach close to where I lay .
Parsing [sent. 3196 len. 24]: The dead bodies of their companions , who had fallen in the conflict , and the wounded , were carried into the canoes .
Parsing [sent. 3197 len. 22]: They formed a circle round the fire , which they had kindled , made several speeches , and danced a war-dance .
Parsing [sent. 3198 len. 29]: I turned round on my side , and perceived to my horror , that they had collected all the bodies of my companions , and were devouring them .
Parsing [sent. 3199 len. 21]: What they did not feel inclined to eat , they packed up in baskets , and put into the canoes .
Parsing [sent. 3200 len. 41]: I anticipated that such would be my own fate -- not at present , as they had more than they could consume -- but that I should be reserved for a festival , after their arrival in their own country .
Parsing [sent. 3201 len. 40]: Nor was I incorrect in my supposition ; they collected together all the bones , which they carried with them , and putting me on board , hoisted their mat sails , and steered away for their own islands .
Parsing [sent. 3202 len. 23]: On the third day we arrived , when I was carried on shore and confined in what I believe was a burying-ground .
Parsing [sent. 3203 len. 35]: They stuffed me every day with pork and other victuals to keep me alive , and in good condition , but they never cast me loose from the pole to which I was bound .
Parsing [sent. 3204 len. 30]: I heard processions , shouts , and lamentations for the dead ; but I could see nothing , for I was now too weak to turn on my side .
Parsing [sent. 3205 len. 82]: When I had been a week in this confined state , the agony arising from the swelling of my limbs , and from the increased tightness of the ligatures was so great , that I called for death to relieve me from my sufferings ; and when I once more found myself raised upon the shoulders of men , I was as impatient for my approaching fate , as I should have been , under other circumstances , for my release .
Parsing [sent. 3206 len. 22]: My senses were gradually overpowered by the pain , which was so much increased by the renewed suspension of my body .
Parsing [sent. 3207 len. 32]: I have a distinct recollection of being placed on the ground in a large circle -- of the screams of a woman , and of a confused uproar , which followed .
Parsing [sent. 3208 len. 68]: When I came to my senses , I found myself in a hut , unbound , and lying upon soft mats , with fomentations applied to my limbs and when my eyes opened , I beheld , hanging over me with an air of the tenderest solicitude , the beautiful savage , whom I had found wounded , and had succoured on the night of the affray .
Parsing [sent. 3209 len. 67]: I subsequently learnt , that when I had been brought into the circle , she had recognised me as the person who had assisted her ; that she claimed my life , pointing to her wound , and producing the bandages with which I had bound it up , and which were identified with the remainder , as part of the dress which I still wore .
Parsing [sent. 3210 len. 74]: A council was held ; and as it appeared that I could not have been with the party in the ship , for I had been taken prisoner in the woods , near to where the girl lay , after many speeches pro and con , it was decided that my life should be spared , and that I should be married to the girl who had been the means of preserving it .
Parsing [sent. 3211 len. 22]: She had carried me away to her hut , and was now returning the debt of gratitude which she had incurred .
Parsing [sent. 3212 len. 44]: Owing to her unwearied kindness and attention , I soon recovered , and before I was aware that I was to be her husband I courted her by signs , and all the little attentions that could be suggested by gratitude and love .
Parsing [sent. 3213 len. 29]: As soon as I was supposed to be sufficiently recovered I was led into a large circle of the islanders , to be formally admitted into their society .
Parsing [sent. 3214 len. 58]: A venerable old man made a speech , which I presume was not a very good one from its extreme length , and then several men laid hold of me , and throwing me on the ground , face downwards , sat astride on me , and commenced running needles into the upper part of my thighs .
Parsing [sent. 3215 len. 34]: The pain was excessive ; but as all the islanders were tattooed about the loins , I presumed it was an operation that I must submit to , and bore it with fortitude .
Parsing [sent. 3216 len. 9]: `` And pray what is that tattooing ? ''
Parsing [sent. 3217 len. 30]: `` Tattooing , may it please your highness , is puncturing the skin with needles or sharp points -- and then rubbing Indian ink or gunpowder into the wounds .
Parsing [sent. 3218 len. 11]: This leaves an indelible mark of a deep blue tint .
Parsing [sent. 3219 len. 22]: All the islanders in those seas practise it , and very often the figures that are drawn are very beautiful . ''
Parsing [sent. 3220 len. 3]: `` Mashallah !
Parsing [sent. 3221 len. 5]: How wonderful is God !
Parsing [sent. 3222 len. 12]: I should like to see it , '' rejoined the pacha .
Parsing [sent. 3223 len. 20]: `` Allah forbid , '' replied the renegade , `` that I should expose my person to your highness .
Parsing [sent. 3224 len. 7]: I know my duty better . ''
Parsing [sent. 3225 len. 16]: `` Yes , but I must see it , yaha bibi , my friend ! ''
Parsing [sent. 3226 len. 12]: continued the pacha , impatiently ; `` never mind your person .
Parsing [sent. 3227 len. 7]: Come -- obey my orders . ''
Parsing [sent. 3228 len. 21]: The renegade was a little at a nonplus , as he never had undergone the operation which he had described .
Parsing [sent. 3229 len. 39]: Fortunately for the support of his veracity , it happened that during one of his piratical excursions , in an idle fit , he had permitted one of his companions to tattoo a small mermaid on his arm .
Parsing [sent. 3230 len. 4]: `` Min Allah !
Parsing [sent. 3231 len. 80]: God forbid , '' rejoined the renegade ; `` my life is at the disposal of your highness , and I had sooner that you should take it , than I would affront your august eyes with the exposure in question ; fortunately I can gratify your highness 's curiosity without offending decency -- as , after they had finished the operation I was describing , they made the figure of their most respected deity upon my arm . ''
Parsing [sent. 3232 len. 33]: The renegade then pulled up his sleeve , and showed the figure of a mermaid , with a curling tail , a looking-glass in one hand and a comb in the other .
Parsing [sent. 3233 len. 12]: `` Here your highness will perceive a specimen of their art .
Parsing [sent. 3234 len. 10]: This is a representation of their goddess , Bo-gee .
Parsing [sent. 3235 len. 36]: In one hand she holds an iron rake , with which she tattoos those who are good , and the mark serves as a passport when they apply for admittance into the regions of bliss .
Parsing [sent. 3236 len. 27]: In the other , she brandishes a hot iron plate , with which she brands those who are sentenced to be punished for their sins . ''
Parsing [sent. 3237 len. 8]: `` Allah karim -- God is merciful !
Parsing [sent. 3238 len. 10]: And why has she a fish 's tail ? ''
Parsing [sent. 3239 len. 4]: inquired the pacha .
Parsing [sent. 3240 len. 35]: `` The people I am describing , inhabit a cluster of islands , and it is to enable her to swim from one to the other , as her presence may be required . ''
Parsing [sent. 3241 len. 20]: `` Very true , '' observed the pacha -- `` now you may go on with your story . ''
Parsing [sent. 3242 len. 28]: As I mentioned to your highness , they tattooed me without mercy ; the operation lasted an hour , when they put me on my feet again .
Parsing [sent. 3243 len. 30]: Another speech was made , which I understood as little of as the former ; they left me with my wife , and the ceremony was at an end .
Parsing [sent. 3244 len. 19]: I must say I wished that I had not been naturalised and married both on the same day .
Parsing [sent. 3245 len. 32]: I was so swelled and so stiff with the tattooing , that it was with difficulty I could , with the assistance of my wife , walk back to my hut .
Parsing [sent. 3246 len. 22]: However , by the remedies which she constantly applied , in the course of three days I felt no further inconvenience .
Parsing [sent. 3247 len. 12]: I now considered myself settled for the remainder of my life .
Parsing [sent. 3248 len. 51]: I was passionately attached to Naka-poop , for such was the name of my young wife , and notwithstanding my French education , could not but acknowledge that her natural and unsophisticated manners were more graceful and more fascinating , than is all the studied address of my own countrywomen .
Parsing [sent. 3249 len. 32]: She was of high rank in her own country , being nearly allied to the king ; and for two years my life slipped away , in uninterrupted happiness and peace .
Parsing [sent. 3250 len. 4]: But , alas !
Parsing [sent. 3251 len. 9]: -- and the renegade covered up his face .
Parsing [sent. 3252 len. 27]: `` Come , Huckaback , you surely have been too much accustomed to lose your wives by this time , to make a fuss about it .

Parsing [sent. 3254 len. 19]: `` Your highness must excuse me ; I shall not offend again , for I never married afterwards .
Parsing [sent. 3255 len. 23]: My charming Naka-poop died in child-bed , and the island became so hateful to me , that I determined to quit it .
Parsing [sent. 3256 len. 15]: An opportunity occurred by an American vessel , which arrived with some missionaries . ''
Parsing [sent. 3257 len. 6]: `` What are missionaries ? ''
Parsing [sent. 3258 len. 4]: inquired the pacha .
Parsing [sent. 3259 len. 27]: `` People who came to inform the islanders , that Bo-gee was not a goddess , and to persuade them to embrace the true faith . ''
Parsing [sent. 3260 len. 22]: `` Very right , '' replied the pacha , `` there is but one God , and Mahomet is his prophet .
Parsing [sent. 3261 len. 42]: Well -- '' As I understood both languages , I was employed as an interpreter , but it was impossible to explain what the missionaries intended to convey , as the language of the islanders had not words that were analogous .
Parsing [sent. 3262 len. 36]: A council was held ; and the answer which the missionaries received was as follows : -- `` You tell us that your God rewards the good and punishes the wicked -- so does Bo-gee .
Parsing [sent. 3263 len. 9]: We speak one language , you speak another .
Parsing [sent. 3264 len. 11]: Perhaps the name of your God means Bo-gee in ours .
Parsing [sent. 3265 len. 12]: Then we both worship the same God , under different names .
Parsing [sent. 3266 len. 19]: No use to talk any more ; take plenty of pigs and yams , and go home . ''
Parsing [sent. 3267 len. 19]: The missionaries took their advice , their pigs and their yams , and I went home with them .
Parsing [sent. 3268 len. 36]: We arrived at New York , where I claimed and received from the Bible Society my pay as interpreter to the missionaries from the time that they landed up to the day of our return .
Parsing [sent. 3269 len. 29]: I never should have thought of claiming it , had it not been for the advice of one of the missionaries , who took a fancy to me .
Parsing [sent. 3270 len. 30]: With the money that I received I paid my passage in a vessel bound to Genoa , where I arrived in safety , but without the means of subsistence .
Parsing [sent. 3271 len. 34]: But what doth the poet say , `` Necessity is a strong rider with sharp stirrups , who maketh the sorry jade do that which the strong horse sometimes will not do . ''
Parsing [sent. 3272 len. 17]: Having no other resource , I determined once more to try my fortune upon the ocean .
Parsing [sent. 3273 len. 9]: `` Allah wakbar -- God is every where !

Parsing [sent. 3275 len. 32]: `` It was his kismet -- his fate , your sublime highness , '' rejoined Mustapha , `` that he should go through those perils to amuse your leisure hours . ''
Parsing [sent. 3276 len. 10]: `` Wallah thaib -- well said , by Allah !
Parsing [sent. 3277 len. 8]: Let the slave rejoice in our bounty .

Parsing [sent. 3280 len. 23]: `` May your sublime shadow never be less , '' replied Huckaback , as he salaamed out of the pacha 's presence .
Parsing [sent. 3281 len. 6]: VOLUME TWO , CHAPTER SIX .
Parsing [sent. 3282 len. 6]: THE LAST VOYAGE OF HUCKABACK .
Parsing [sent. 3283 len. 56]: Your highness will be surprised at the unheard-of adventures that occurred to me in my last voyage , and I think I can boldly assert that no man , either before or since , has explored so much , or has been in the peculiarly dangerous situations in which I have been placed by destiny .
Parsing [sent. 3284 len. 66]: Notwithstanding the danger which I incurred from my former expedition to the Northern Ocean , I was persuaded to take the command of a whaler about to proceed to those latitudes : we sailed from Marseilles early in the year that we might arrive at the northward in good time , and be able to quit the Frozen Ocean before the winter had set in .
Parsing [sent. 3285 len. 21]: We were very fortunate on our arrival at Baffin 's Bay , and very soon had eighteen fish on board .
Parsing [sent. 3286 len. 43]: The autumn was hardly commenced before I proposed to return , and we were steering in a southerly direction , when we encountered two or three large icebergs , upon the edges of which the walruses or sea-horses were lying in herds .
Parsing [sent. 3287 len. 32]: As we had some casks still empty , I determined to fill them with the oil to be obtained from these animals , and hoisted out my boats to attack them .
Parsing [sent. 3288 len. 45]: We killed a large number , which we sent on board , and continued our fishery with great success , having only lost one boat , the bottom plank of which had been bitten out by the tusks of one of these unwieldy animals .
Parsing [sent. 3289 len. 31]: Of a sudden the wind changed to the southward , and the small icebergs which were then to windward rapidly closed with the large one upon which we were fishing .
Parsing [sent. 3290 len. 30]: The harpooners observed it , and recommended me to return to the ship , but I was so amused with the sport that I did not heed their advice .
Parsing [sent. 3291 len. 33]: A sea-horse was lying in a small cave accidentally formed on the upright edge of the iceberg , and wishing to attack him , I directed my boat to pull towards it .
Parsing [sent. 3292 len. 30]: At this time there was not more than twenty yards of water between the two icebergs , and a sudden squall coming on , they closed with great rapidity .
Parsing [sent. 3293 len. 80]: The men in the other boats immediately pulled away , and , as I afterwards learnt , when I arrived at Marseilles , they escaped , and returned home in the ship ; but those in mine , who were intent upon watching me , as I stood in the bow of the boat with the harpoon to strike the animal , did not perceive the danger until the stern of the boat was touched by the other iceberg .
Parsing [sent. 3294 len. 35]: The two now coming within the attraction of cohesion of floating bodies , were dashed like lightning one against the other , jamming the men , as well as the boat , into atoms .
Parsing [sent. 3295 len. 73]: Being in the bow of the boat , and hearing the crash , I had just time , in a moment of desperation , to throw myself into the cave upon the back of the sea-horse , when the two enormous bodies of ice came in contact -- the noise I have no doubt was tremendous , but I did not hear it , as I was immediately enclosed in the ice .
Parsing [sent. 3296 len. 52]: Although at first there were interstices , yet , as the southerly gale blew the icebergs before it into the northern region , all was quickly cemented together by the frost , and I found myself pent up in an apartment not eight feet square , in company with a sea-horse .
Parsing [sent. 3297 len. 38]: I shall not detain your highness by describing my sensations : my ideas were , that I was to exist a certain time , and then die for want of fresh air ; but they were incorrect .
Parsing [sent. 3298 len. 25]: At first , indeed , the cave was intolerably hot from the accumulation of breath , and I thought I should soon be suffocated .
Parsing [sent. 3299 len. 58]: I recollected all my past sins , I implored for mercy , and lay down to die ; but I found that the ice melted away with the heat , and that , in so doing , a considerable portion of the air was liberated , so that in a few minutes my respiration became more free .
Parsing [sent. 3300 len. 44]: The animal in the meantime , apparently frightened at his unusual situation , was perfectly quiet ; and , as the slightest straw will be caught at by the drowning man , so did the idea of my preservation come into my head .
Parsing [sent. 3301 len. 29]: I considered how much air so enormous an animal must consume , and determined upon despatching him , that I might have more for my own immediate wants .
Parsing [sent. 3302 len. 31]: I took out my knife , and inserting it between the vertebral bones that joined his head to his neck , divided the spinal marrow , and he immediately expired .
Parsing [sent. 3303 len. 58]: When I found that he was quite dead , I crawled from his shoulders , and took up a more convenient berth in that part of the cave which was before his head , to which I had been afraid to venture while the animal was alive , lest he should attack me with his enormous tusks .
Parsing [sent. 3304 len. 12]: The air soon became more pure , and I breathed freely .
Parsing [sent. 3305 len. 47]: Your highness may be surprised at the assertion ; but , whether I obtained air from the ice itself , or whether the ice was sufficiently porous to admit of it , I know not ; but from that time I had no difficulty of respiration .
Parsing [sent. 3306 len. 46]: In our country we have had instances of women and children , who have been buried in the snow for two months , and yet have been taken out alive , and have recovered , although they had little or no nourishment during their inhumation .
Parsing [sent. 3307 len. 45]: I recollected this , and aware that the carcase of the animal would supply me for years , I began to indulge a hope that I might yet be saved , if driven sufficiently to the southward to admit of my being thawed out .
Parsing [sent. 3308 len. 32]: I was convinced that the ice about me could not be more than six or eight feet thick , as I had sufficient light to distinguish the day from the night .
Parsing [sent. 3309 len. 27]: Afterwards my eye-sight became so much more acute , that I could see very well to every corner of the cave in which I was embedded .
Parsing [sent. 3310 len. 65]: During the first month the calls of hunger obliged me to make frequent attacks upon the carcase of the sea-horse ; after that , my appetite decreased , until at length I would not touch a mouthful of food in a week , -- I presume from the want of fresh air and exercise , neither of which I could be said to enjoy .
Parsing [sent. 3311 len. 49]: I had been about two months in this hole , when a violent shock like that of an earthquake took place , and I fell from the top of the cave to the bottom , and for a minute was knocked about like a pea in a rattle .
Parsing [sent. 3312 len. 26]: I had almost lost my senses before it was over , and I found myself lying upon what was before the top of the cave .
Parsing [sent. 3313 len. 55]: From these circumstances I inferred that the iceberg in which I was inclosed had come in contact with another , and that I had been broken off from it , and was floating on the sea with other pieces , which , when collected in large quantities , are termed a floe of ice .
Parsing [sent. 3314 len. 21]: Whether my situation was changed for the better I knew not , but the change inspired me with fresh hopes .
Parsing [sent. 3315 len. 31]: I now calculated that five months had elapsed , and that it was the depth of winter , therefore I had no chance of being released until the ensuing spring .
Parsing [sent. 3316 len. 10]: `` Allah wakbar , God is every where ! ''
Parsing [sent. 3317 len. 4]: interrupted the pacha .
Parsing [sent. 3318 len. 24]: `` But I wish to know , Huckaback , how you were so exactly aware of the time which had passed away . ''
Parsing [sent. 3319 len. 10]: `` Min bashi , and head of thousands ! ''
Parsing [sent. 3320 len. 11]: replied Huckaback , `` I will explain to your highness .
Parsing [sent. 3321 len. 16]: I once jammed my nail at the bottom , and I expected to lose it .
Parsing [sent. 3322 len. 32]: It did not however come off but grew up as before , and I had the curiosity to know how often people changed their nails in the course of a year .
Parsing [sent. 3323 len. 14]: It was exactly two months , and from this I grounded my calculations .
Parsing [sent. 3324 len. 20]: I observed specks on my nails , and as they grew up , so did I calculate time . ''
Parsing [sent. 3325 len. 8]: `` Mashallah , how wonderful is God !
Parsing [sent. 3326 len. 3]: Wallah thaib !
Parsing [sent. 3327 len. 6]: Well said , by Allah !
Parsing [sent. 3328 len. 13]: I never should have thought of that , '' observed the pacha .
Parsing [sent. 3329 len. 7]: `` Proceed with your story . ''
Parsing [sent. 3330 len. 51]: The five months had elapsed , according to my calculations , when one morning I heard a grating noise close to me ; soon afterwards I perceived the teeth of a saw entering my domicile , and I correctly judged that some ship was cutting her way through the ice .
Parsing [sent. 3331 len. 16]: Although I could not make myself heard , I waited in anxious expectation of deliverance .
Parsing [sent. 3332 len. 43]: The saw approached very near to where I was sitting , and I was afraid that I should be wounded , if not cut in halves ; but just as it was within two inches of my nose , it was withdrawn .
Parsing [sent. 3333 len. 36]: The fact was , that I was under the main floe , which had been frozen together , and the firm ice above having been removed and pushed away , I rose to the surface .

''
Parsing [sent. 3341 len. 4]: But , alas !
Parsing [sent. 3342 len. 61]: my hopes soon vanished : the voices became more faint , I felt that I was plunged under the floe to make room for the passage of the ship , and when I rose , the water which had filled the incision made by the saw , froze hard , and I was again closed in -- perhaps for ever .
Parsing [sent. 3343 len. 35]: I now became quite frantic with despair , I tore my clothes , and dashed my head against the corners of the cave , and tried to put an end to my hated existence .
Parsing [sent. 3344 len. 20]: At last , I sank down exhausted with my own violent efforts , and continued sullen for several days .
Parsing [sent. 3345 len. 19]: But there is a buoyant spirit in our composition which raises our heads above the waters of despair .
Parsing [sent. 3346 len. 11]: Hope never deserts us , not even in an iceberg .
Parsing [sent. 3347 len. 45]: She attends us and supports us to the last ; and although we reject her kind offices in our fury , she still watches by us , ready to assist and console us , when we are inclined to hearken to her encouraging whispers .
Parsing [sent. 3348 len. 27]: I once more listened to her suggestions , and for six months fed upon them , aided by occasional variations of the flesh of the sea-horse .
Parsing [sent. 3349 len. 22]: It was now late in the summer , and the ice in which I was bound up had evidently melted away .
Parsing [sent. 3350 len. 25]: One morning I was astonished by perceiving that the light of the sun seemed to change its position regularly every quarter of an hour .
Parsing [sent. 3351 len. 43]: Had it done so occasionally during the day , and at no stated intervals , I should have imagined that the ice that I was enclosed in , altered its position with the winds and currents ; but the regularity astonished me .
Parsing [sent. 3352 len. 32]: I watched it , and I found that the same phenomenon occurred , but at shorter intervals , and it continued until the light shifted from side to side every minute .
Parsing [sent. 3353 len. 71]: After some reflection , the horrid idea occurred to me that I must have been drifted to the coast of Norway , and was in the influence of the dreadful whirlpool , called the Maelstroom , and that , in a few minutes , I should be engulfed for ever ; and , whilst I was thinking that such might be the case , the light revolved each fifteen seconds .
Parsing [sent. 3354 len. 6]: `` Then it is ! ''
Parsing [sent. 3355 len. 34]: cried I in despair ; and , as I uttered the words , it became quite dark , and I knew that I had sunk in the vortex , and all was over .
Parsing [sent. 3356 len. 42]: It may appear strange to your highness , that after the first pang , occasioned by the prospect of perdition , had passed away , that so far from feeling a horror at my situation , I mocked and derided it .
Parsing [sent. 3357 len. 15]: I could feel no more , and I waited the result with perfect indifference .
Parsing [sent. 3358 len. 24]: From the marks in my nails , I afterwards found out that I was nearly six months in the interior of the earth .
Parsing [sent. 3359 len. 32]: At last , one day I was nearly blinded by the powerful light that poured through my tenement , and I knew that I was once more floating on the water .
Parsing [sent. 3360 len. 4]: `` Allah kebir !
Parsing [sent. 3361 len. 6]: God is most powerful ! ''
Parsing [sent. 3362 len. 4]: exclaimed the pacha .
Parsing [sent. 3363 len. 14]: `` Holy Prophet , where was it that you came up again ? ''
Parsing [sent. 3364 len. 9]: `` In the harbour of Port-Royal in Jamaica .
Parsing [sent. 3365 len. 16]: Your highness will hardly credit it , but on my honour it is true . ''
Parsing [sent. 3366 len. 50]: The heat of the sun was so great , that in a very short time the ice that surrounded me was thawed , and I found myself at liberty ; but I still floated upon the body of the sea-horse , and the ice which was under the water .
Parsing [sent. 3367 len. 114]: The latter soon vanished , and striding the back of the dead animal , although nearly blind by the rays of the sun , and suffocated with the sudden change of climate , I waited patiently to gain the shore , which was not one mile distant ; but , before I could arrive there , for the sea breeze had not yet set in , an enormous shark , well known among the English by the name of Port-Royal Tom , who had daily rations from government , that by remaining in the harbour he might prevent the sailors from swimming on shore to desert , ranged up along side of me .
Parsing [sent. 3368 len. 29]: I thought it hard that I should have to undergo such new dangers , after having been down the Maelstroom , but there was no help for it .

Parsing [sent. 3371 len. 53]: Again he attacked it , and continued to take piece after piece off my steed , until I was afraid that he would come to the rider at last , when fortunately a boat full of black people , who were catching flying fish , perceived me and pulled to my assistance .
Parsing [sent. 3372 len. 36]: They took me on shore , and carried me to the governor , to whom I gave a history of my adventures ; but Englishmen suppose that nobody can meet with wondrous adventures except themselves .
Parsing [sent. 3373 len. 86]: He called me a liar , and put me in the Clink , and a pirate schooner havimg been lately taken and the crew executed , I was declared to have been one of them ; but , as it was clearly proved that the vessel only contained thirty men , and they had already hung forty-seven , I was permitted to quit the island , which I did in a small vessel bound to America , on condition that I would work my passage .
Parsing [sent. 3374 len. 37]: We had gained to the northward of the Bahama Isles , and were standing to the westward before a light breeze , when early one morning several waterspouts were observed to be forming in various directions .
Parsing [sent. 3375 len. 29]: It was my watch below , but as I had never seen one of these curious phenomena of nature , I went on deck to indulge my curiosity .

Parsing [sent. 3377 len. 13]: inquired the pacha ; `` I never heard of one before . ''
Parsing [sent. 3378 len. 50]: `` A waterspout , your highness , is the ascent of a large body of water into the clouds -- one of those gigantic operations by which nature , apparently without effort , accomplishes her will , pointing out to man the insignificance of his most vaunted undertakings . ''
Parsing [sent. 3379 len. 3]: `` Humph !
Parsing [sent. 3380 len. 9]: that 's a waterspout , is it ? ''
Parsing [sent. 3381 len. 14]: replied the pacha ; `` I 'm about as wise as before . ''

Parsing [sent. 3383 len. 20]: A black cloud was over our heads , and we perceived that for some time it was rapidly descending .

Parsing [sent. 3385 len. 30]: From the end of this bag a thin , wiry , black tongue of vapour continued to descend until it had arrived half-way between the cloud and the sea .
Parsing [sent. 3386 len. 34]: The water beneath , then ruffled on its surface , increasing its agitation more and more until it boiled and bubbled like a large cauldron , throwing its foam aside in every direction .
Parsing [sent. 3387 len. 30]: In a few minutes a small spiral thread of water was perceived to rise into the air , and meet the tongue which had wooed it from the cloud .
Parsing [sent. 3388 len. 46]: When the union had taken place , the thread increased each moment in size , until it was swelled into a column of water several feet in diameter , which continued to supply the thirsty cloud until it was satiated and could drink no more .
Parsing [sent. 3389 len. 39]: It then broke , the sea became smooth as before , and the messenger of heaven flew away upon the wings of the wind , to dispense its burden over the parched earth in refreshing and fertilising showers .
Parsing [sent. 3390 len. 35]: While I was standing at the taffrail in admiration of this wonderful resource of nature , the main boom gybed and struck me with such force , that I was thrown into the sea .
Parsing [sent. 3391 len. 51]: Another waterspout forming close to the vessel , the captain and crew were alarmed and made all sail to escape , without regarding me ; for they were aware that if it should happen to break over them , they would be sent to the bottom with its enormous weight .

Parsing [sent. 3393 len. 39]: Thus was I left to my fate , and convinced that I could not swim for many minutes , I swallowed the salt water as fast as I could , that my struggles might the sooner be over .
Parsing [sent. 3394 len. 58]: But as the sea boiled up , I found myself gradually drawn more to the centre , and when exactly in it , I was raised in a sitting posture upon the spiral thread of water , which , as I explained to your highness , forced itself upwards to join the tongue protruded by the cloud .
Parsing [sent. 3395 len. 42]: There I sat , each second rising higher and higher , balanced like the gilt ball of pith , which is borne up by the vertical stream of the fountain which plays in the inner court of your highness 's palace .

Parsing [sent. 3584 len. 13]: The dispute ran high , and the beautiful Princess Babe-bi-bobu remained unmarried .
Parsing [sent. 3585 len. 124]: This great question was at last very properly referred to the mufti ; these sages handled it , and turned it , and twisted it , added to it , multiplied it , subtracted from it , and divided it , debated it fasting , debated it on a full stomach , nodded over it , dreamt on it , slept on it , woke up with it , analysed it , criticised it , and wrote forty-eight folio volumes , of which twenty-four were advocates of , and twenty-four opponents to the question ; the only conclusion which they could come to at last was , that _ moles _ were _ moles _ : and the beautiful Princess Babe-bi-bobu remained unmarried .
Parsing [sent. 3586 len. 108]: The question was then taken up by the dervishes and fakirs of the country in a religious point of view ; they split into two parties , tried the question by a dispute under a banyan tree , which lasted eighteen months , and still not half of the holy men had given their sentiments upon the question ; tired of talking , they proceeded to blows , and then to anathematisation and excommunication of each other ; lastly , they had recourse to impalement to convince each other ; more than a thousand perished on each side ; and still the beautiful Princess Babe-bi-bobu remained unmarried .
Parsing [sent. 3587 len. 51]: The colleges and schools of the kingdom took up the question , and argued it metaphysically , and after having irrecoverably lost , between the two sides , twenty-two millions of threads of arguments , the question was as fresh as ever , and the beautiful princess Babe-bi-bobu remained unmarried .
Parsing [sent. 3588 len. 72]: But this was not all ; for at last the whole nation joined in the quarrel , splitting into violent and angry factions , which divided town against town , inhabitants against inhabitants , house against house , family against family , husband against wife , father against son , brother against sister ; and in some cases , where he had doubts on both sides , a man against himself .
Parsing [sent. 3589 len. 41]: The whole nation flew to arms , distinguishing themselves as Molists and Anti-molists ; four hundred insurrections , and four civil wars , were the consequence ; and what was a worse consequence , the beautiful Princess Babe-bi-bobu remained unmarried .

Parsing [sent. 3600 len. 143]: The espionage at that time was so strict , that even a whisper was to be heard at the distance of miles , and this observation was reported ; it certainly was new because it was neutral , when neutrality was not permitted or thought of ; it was buzzed about ; the remark was declared wonderful , it ran like wildfire through the suburbs , it roared through the city , it shook the very gates of the palace ; at last it reached the holy in divan , who pronounced it to be inspiration from the Deity , and immediately there was issued a solemn edict , in which it was laid down as a most positive and important article of Souffrarian faith , that moles were not scars , and only blemishes when they were considered so to be .
Parsing [sent. 3601 len. 68]: Every one praised the wisdom of this edict ; it was read and subscribed to as an article of faith ; towns greeted towns , house congratulated house , and relations shook hands ; what was still stranger was , husbands and wives were reconciled -- and what was even more delightful , there was now some chance of the beautiful Princess Babe-bi-bobu no longer remaining unmarried .
Parsing [sent. 3602 len. 69]: This fortunate edict , by which it was clear that those who believed a mole to be a blemish were quite safe , and who did not believe it , were in no manner of danger , set every thing to rights ; the metropolis was again filled with aspirants , the air tortured with the music of the mandolins , and impregnated with the attar of roses .

Parsing [sent. 3618 len. 19]: Who was there in the whole kingdom of Souffra who could so sweetly touch the mandolin as Acota ?
Parsing [sent. 3619 len. 134]: Yet , who was there , not only in Souffra , but in all the adjacent countries , who struck such occasional discordant notes as Acota , and that in the ear of the beautiful princess Babe-bi-bobu , who , far from being displeased , appeared to approve of his occasional violence , which not only threatened to crack the strings of the instrument , but the tympanums of those who were near , who longed to escape , and leave the princess to enjoy the dissonance alone , little thinking that the discord was raised that their souls ' harmony might be undisturbed by the presence of others , and that the jarring of the strings was more than repaid to the princess , by the subsequent music of Acota 's voice .
Parsing [sent. 3620 len. 62]: Acota seated himself , at a signal from the princess , and commenced his playing , if such it could be called , thrumming violently , and jarring every chord of his instrument to a tone of such dissonance , that the attendant girls put their fingers into their ears , and pitied the beautiful Babe-bi-bobu 's bad taste in music .

Parsing [sent. 3630 len. 77]: In the mean time , a rumour was spread abroad that at sunset a public examination of all the candidates was to take place on the bank of the rapid-flowing river , which ran through a spacious meadow near to the city , in order to reject those candidates who might prove , by any _ scar _ or _ blemish _ , not to come expressly within the meaning of the old king 's will .

Parsing [sent. 3632 len. 44]: It was supposed , as this was a religious ceremony , that all the females of Souffra , who were remarkable for their piety , would not fail to attend -- and all the world were eager for the commencement of the examination .
Parsing [sent. 3633 len. 66]: O then it was pleasant to see the running , and mounting , and racing , among the young Souffrarian rayahs , who were expected to be examined ; and a stranger would have thought that a sudden pestilence had entered the city , from the thousands upon thousands who poured out from it , hastening to the river side , to behold the ceremony .
Parsing [sent. 3634 len. 175]: But to the astonishment of the people , almost all the rayahs , as soon as they were mounted , left the city in an opposite direction , some declaring , that they were most surely without _ scar _ or _ blemish _ , but still they could not consent to expose their persons to the gaze of so many thousands ; others declared that they left on account of _ scars and honourable wounds _ received in battle ; and until that afternoon , the Souffrarians were not aware of how much modesty and how much courage they had to boast in their favoured land ; and many regretted , as they viewed the interminable line of gallant young men depart , that the will of the late king should have made scars received in battle to be a bar to advancement ; but they were checked by the brahmins , who told them that there was a holy and hidden mystery contained in the injunction of the old king 's will .

Parsing [sent. 3832 len. 66]: Most sublime pacha , allow me first to observe , that , although I have latterly adhered to my own opinions , I am not so intolerant as not to permit the same licence to others : I do not mean to say that there are not such things as facts in this world , nor to find fault with those who believe in them .
Parsing [sent. 3833 len. 120]: I am told that there are also such things as flying dragons , griffins , and other wondrous animals , but surely it is quite sufficient for me , or any one else , to believe that these animals exist , when it may have been our fortune to see them ; in the same manner , I am willing to believe in a fact , when it is cleared from the mists of doubt ; but up to the present , I can safely say , that I seldom have fallen in with a fact , unaccompanied by _ doubts _ , and every year adds to my belief , that there are few genuine facts in existence .

Parsing [sent. 4173 len. 6]: TALE OF THE ENGLISH SAILOR .
Parsing [sent. 4174 len. 38]: I was born at Shields , and bred to the sea , served my time out of that port , and got a berth on board a small vessel fitted out from Liverpool for the slave trade .
Parsing [sent. 4175 len. 63]: We made the coast , unstowed our beads , spirits , and gunpowder , and very soon had a cargo on board ; but the day after we sailed for the Havannah , the dysentery broke out among the niggers -- no wonder , seeing how they were stowed , poor devils , head and tail , like pilchards in a cask .

Parsing [sent. 5010 len. 18]: A yellow-skinned , meagre , and wrinkled old Chinaman was brought in between two of the guards .

Parsing [sent. 5031 len. 6]: THE WONDROUS TALE OF HAN .
Parsing [sent. 5032 len. 39]: Who was more impassioned in his nature , who was more formed for love , than the great Han Koong Shew , known in the celestial archives as the sublime Youantee , brother of the sun and moon ?
Parsing [sent. 5033 len. 62]: -- whose court was so superb -- whose armies were so innumerable -- whose territories were so vast -- bounded as they were by the four seas , which bounded the whole universe ; yet was he bound by destiny to be unhappy , and thus do I commence the wondrous tale of Han -- the sorrows of the magnificent Youantee .
Parsing [sent. 5034 len. 15]: Ti-tum , tilly-lilly -- Yes , he felt that some one thing was wanting .
Parsing [sent. 5035 len. 17]: All his power , his wealth , his dignity , filled not his soul with pleasure .
Parsing [sent. 5036 len. 15]: He turned from the writings of the great Fo -- he closed the book .
Parsing [sent. 5037 len. 2]: Alas !
Parsing [sent. 5038 len. 20]: he sighed for a second self to whom he might point out -- `` All this is mine . ''
Parsing [sent. 5039 len. 20]: His heart yearned for a fair damsel -- a maid of beauty -- to whose beauty he might bow .
Parsing [sent. 5040 len. 24]: He , to whom the world was prostrate , the universe were slaves , longed for an amorous captivity and sighed for chains .
Parsing [sent. 5041 len. 28]: But where was the maiden to be found worthy to place fetters upon the brother of the sun and moon -- the magnificent master of the universe ?
Parsing [sent. 5042 len. 7]: Where was she to be found ?
Parsing [sent. 5043 len. 8]: Ti-tum , tilly-lilly , ti-tum , ti .
Parsing [sent. 5044 len. 55]: Yes , there was one , and but one , worthy to be his mate , worthy to be the queen of a land of eternal spring , filled with trees whose stems were of gold , branches of silver , leaves of emerald , and whose fruits were the fragrant apples of immortality .
Parsing [sent. 5045 len. 12]: And where was this moon , fit bride unto the sun ?
Parsing [sent. 5046 len. 23]: Was she not plunged in grief -- hidden in a well of her own tears -- even in the gardens of joy ?
Parsing [sent. 5047 len. 17]: Those eyes which should have sunned a court of princes , were dimmed with eternal sorrow .
Parsing [sent. 5048 len. 21]: And who was the cause of this eclipse , but the miscreant gold-loving minister , _ Suchong Pollyhong Ka-te-tow _ .
Parsing [sent. 5049 len. 4]: Ti-tum , tilly-lilly .

Parsing [sent. 5051 len. 19]: `` Hear me , ye first chop mandarins , peers , lords , and princes of the empire .

Parsing [sent. 5056 len. 23]: Am I then so unfortunately great , or so greatly unfortunate , that I may not be permitted to descend to love ?
Parsing [sent. 5057 len. 20]: Even the brother of the sun and moon can not , during his career on earth , exist alone .

Parsing [sent. 5076 len. 59]: But before they could be permitted to shoot up the rays of love through the mist of glory which surrounded the imperial throne -- before their charms were to make the attempt upon the heart of magnanimity , it was necessary that all their portraits should be submitted to the great Youantee , in the hail of delight .
Parsing [sent. 5077 len. 53]: That is to say , out of the twenty thousand virgins whose images were to be impressed upon the ivory , one hundred only , selected by a committee of taste , composed of the first class mandarins and princes , were to be honoured with the beam of the celestial eye .
Parsing [sent. 5078 len. 65]: The avaricious , gold-seeking , Suchong Pollyhong Kate-tow , had performed his task -- wealth poured into his coffers from the ambitious parents , who longed to boast of an alliance with the brother of the sun and moon , and many were the ill-favoured whose portraits were dismissed by the committee of taste , with surprise at the minister 's ideas of beauty .
Parsing [sent. 5079 len. 42]: Now there was a certain mandarin , whose daughter had long been extolled through the province of Kartou as a miracle of beauty , and her father , Whanghang , brought her in a litter to the minister Suchong Pollyhong Ka-te-tow .

Parsing [sent. 5081 len. 34]: Refuse to send her portrait he dare not , it was therefore ordered to be taken as well as the others , and Whanghang considered himself as the father-in-law of the celestial Youantee .
Parsing [sent. 5082 len. 33]: The young painter who was employed finished his task , then laid down his pencil , and died with grief and love of such perfection which he never could hope to obtain .
Parsing [sent. 5083 len. 38]: The picture was sent to the vile minister , who reserved it for himself , and wrote the name of this pearl beyond price under that of another , unworthy to unloose her zone as her handmaiden .
Parsing [sent. 5084 len. 55]: The committee of taste did , however , select that picture among the hundred to be placed in the hall of delight , not because the picture was beautiful , but because the fame of her beauty had reached the court , and they thought it right that the emperor should see the picture .
Parsing [sent. 5085 len. 70]: The virgins , whose pictures were thus selected , were all ordered to repair to the imperial palace , and the magnificent Youantee entered the hall of delight , which was illumined with ten thousand lanterns , and cast his eyes over the portraits of the hundred beauties , but not one feature touched his heart , he turned away in disgust at the degenerate countenances of the age .

Parsing [sent. 5172 len. 6]: Another of the robber chiefs .
Parsing [sent. 5173 len. 28]: This man , although a follower of the court , and sunned in the celestial presence , had dared to utter vile falsehoods against the celestial dynasty .

Parsing [sent. 5175 len. 94]: The most important of all the criminals next appeared , who being great in favour at court , and appointed to the high office of physician to the celestial conscience , had been discovered in the base attempt of drugging it with opium ; he had also committed several other enormities , such as being intoxicated in his mandarin robes , and throwing mud at the first chief mandarin ; also of throwing aside his robes , mingling with the lower classes , and associating with mountebanks , jugglers , and tight-rope dancers .

Parsing [sent. 5443 len. 6]: STORY OF THE OLD WOMAN .
Parsing [sent. 5444 len. 83]: I was born in Georgia , where , as your highness knows , the women are reckoned to be more beautiful than in any other country , except indeed Circassia ; but , in my opinion , the Circassian women are much too tall , and on too large a scale , to compete with us ; and I may safely venture my opinion , as I have had an opportunity of comparing many hundreds of the finest specimens of both countries .
Parsing [sent. 5445 len. 50]: My father and mother , although not rich , were in easy circumstances ; my father had been a janissary in the sultan 's immediate employ , and after he had collected some property , he returned to his own country , where he purchased some land and married .
Parsing [sent. 5446 len. 24]: I had but one brother , who was three years older than myself , and one of the handsomest youths in the country .
Parsing [sent. 5447 len. 34]: He was disfigured a little by a scarlet stain on his neck , somewhat in shape resembling a bunch of grapes , and which our national dress would not permit him to conceal .
Parsing [sent. 5448 len. 23]: My father , intending that he should serve the sultan , brought him up to a perfect knowledge of every martial exercise .
Parsing [sent. 5449 len. 31]: Even at fourteen years old , few could compete with him in the use of the bow , and throwing the djireed , and as a horseman he was perfect .
Parsing [sent. 5450 len. 29]: As for me , I was , I am certain , intended for the sultan 's seraglio , for as a child I was beautiful as a houri .
Parsing [sent. 5451 len. 23]: My father was a man who would not scruple to part with his children for gold , provided he obtained his price .
Parsing [sent. 5452 len. 41]: I was considered , and I believe that I was , the most beautiful girl in the country , and every care was taken that I should not injure my appearance or hurt my complexion by domestic labour or exposure .
Parsing [sent. 5453 len. 22]: I was not permitted to assist my mother , who , induced by my father 's orders , waited upon me .
Parsing [sent. 5454 len. 20]: I was indulged in every whim , and I grew up as selfish and capricious as I was beautiful .
Parsing [sent. 5455 len. 9]: Smile not , pacha -- time has been .
Parsing [sent. 5456 len. 41]: One day , when I was about fourteen years old , I was sitting at the porch , when a large body of Turkish cavalry suddenly made their appearance from a wood close to the house , and surrounded it .
Parsing [sent. 5457 len. 31]: They evidently came for me , for they demanded me by name , threatening to burn the house down to the ground , if I was not immediately delivered up .
Parsing [sent. 5458 len. 35]: Our house , which was situated near the confines of the country , had been constructed for defence ; and my father expecting assistance from his neighbours , refused to acquiesce to their terms .
Parsing [sent. 5459 len. 33]: The assault was made , my father and mother , with all their household , were murdered , my brother severely wounded , the house plundered and burnt to the outside walls .
Parsing [sent. 5460 len. 12]: I was of course a prisoner as well as my brother .
Parsing [sent. 5461 len. 30]: He was tied , wounded as he was , upon one horse , and I upon another , and in a few hours the party had regained the frontiers .
Parsing [sent. 5462 len. 31]: A young man , handsome as an angel , was the leader of the band , and I soon perceived that all his thoughts and attentions were directed to me .
Parsing [sent. 5463 len. 24]: He watched me with the greatest solicitude when we halted , procured me every comfort , and was always hovering about my presence .
Parsing [sent. 5464 len. 21]: From the discourse of the soldiers I discovered that he was the only son of the grand vizier at Stamboul .
Parsing [sent. 5465 len. 46]: He had heard of my beauty , had seen me , and offered a large sum to my father , who had refused , as his ambition was that I should belong to the sultan -- in consequence I had been carried off by force .
Parsing [sent. 5466 len. 51]: I could have loved the beautiful youth , although he had murdered my father and mother , but it was the taking me by force which steeled my heart , and I vowed that I never would listen to his addresses , although I was so completely in his power .
Parsing [sent. 5467 len. 31]: During the time that I had been in his possession I had never spoken one word , and it came into my head that I would pretend to be dumb .
Parsing [sent. 5468 len. 8]: In three weeks we arrived at Constantinople .
Parsing [sent. 5469 len. 44]: Since I had quitted the country I had never seen my brother ; his wound was too severe to allow him to travel with the same rapidity , and it was not until years afterwards that I knew what had become of him .
Parsing [sent. 5470 len. 59]: I was taken to Osman Ali 's house , and allowed a few days repose from the fatigue of the journey ; after which , as I was still but a child , I was ordered to be instructed in music , dancing , singing , and every other accomplishment considered necessary for the ladies of a harem .
Parsing [sent. 5471 len. 75]: But I adhered to my resolution ; every method to induce me to speak was tried in vain ; even blows , torture from pinching , and other means were resorted to , but would not induce me to swerve from my resolution ; at last they concluded that I was either born dumb , or had become so from fright at the time that the attack and slaughter of my family took place .
Parsing [sent. 5472 len. 17]: I was eighteen months in the harem of Osman Ali , and never spoke one word .
Parsing [sent. 5473 len. 3]: `` Mashallah !
Parsing [sent. 5474 len. 6]: but this is wonderful ! ''
Parsing [sent. 5475 len. 14]: exclaimed the pacha -- `` a woman hold her tongue for eighteen months !
Parsing [sent. 5476 len. 7]: Who is to believe this ? ''
Parsing [sent. 5477 len. 24]: `` Not at all wonderful , '' replied the old woman , `` when you recollect that she was required to speak . ''
Parsing [sent. 5478 len. 14]: Once , and once only , did I nearly break through my resolution .
Parsing [sent. 5479 len. 11]: Two of the principal favourites were conversing in my presence .
Parsing [sent. 5480 len. 26]: `` I can not imagine , '' said one , `` what Ali can see in this little minx to be so infatuated with her .
Parsing [sent. 5481 len. 29]: She is very ugly -- her mouth is large -- her teeth are yellow -- and her eyes not only have no expression , but look different ways .
Parsing [sent. 5482 len. 35]: She has one shoulder higher than the other , and worse than all , being dumb , can not be taught any thing but dancing , which only shows her ugly broad feet . ''
Parsing [sent. 5483 len. 11]: `` That is all true , '' replied the other .
Parsing [sent. 5484 len. 36]: `` If I was Ali , I should employ her as a common slave ; she is fit for nothing but to roll up and beat carpets , boil rice , and prepare our coffee .
Parsing [sent. 5485 len. 17]: A little of the slipper on her mouth would soon bring her to her senses . ''
Parsing [sent. 5486 len. 66]: I must own that I was near breaking through my resolution that I might have indulged my revenge , and had not the door suddenly opened , I should have proved to them , that I could have spoken to some purpose , for never would I have ceased , until they had both been sewn up in sacks , and cast into the Bosphorus .
Parsing [sent. 5487 len. 25]: But I restrained myself , although my cheeks burned with rage , and I more than once put my hand to my jewelled dagger .
Parsing [sent. 5488 len. 33]: I was often visited by Osman Ali , who in vain attempted to make me speak ; a harsh guttural sound was all which I would utter to express pain or pleasure .
Parsing [sent. 5489 len. 22]: At last , being convinced that I was dumb , he exchanged me with a slave-merchant for a beautiful Circassian girl .
Parsing [sent. 5490 len. 31]: He did not state my supposed infirmity , but gave it as his reason for parting with me , that I was too young , and required to be taught .
Parsing [sent. 5491 len. 51]: As soon as the bargain was struck , and the merchant had received the money which had been given by Ali to effect the exchange , I was despoiled of my dress and ornaments , and put in a litter , to be conveyed to the house of the slave-merchant .
Parsing [sent. 5492 len. 40]: As your highness may imagine , not a little tired of holding my tongue for a year and a half -- `` By the beard of the Prophet , we can believe you on that point , good woman .
Parsing [sent. 5493 len. 5]: You may proceed . ''
Parsing [sent. 5494 len. 9]: `` Yes , yes , I may proceed .

Parsing [sent. 5496 len. 9]: Be it so -- time has been . ''
Parsing [sent. 5497 len. 54]: I was no sooner in the litter than I let loose my tongue , and called out to the women who were appointed to conduct me to the door of the harem , `` Tell Osman Ali , that now I am no longer his slave , I have found my tongue . ''
Parsing [sent. 5498 len. 10]: Then closing the curtains , I was carried away .
Parsing [sent. 5499 len. 25]: As soon as I arrived , I told the merchant all that had passed , and the reason why Ali had parted with me .
Parsing [sent. 5500 len. 20]: The merchant , who was astonished at having made so good a bargain , laughed heartily at my narrative .
Parsing [sent. 5501 len. 41]: He told me that he intended me for the seraglio of the sultan -- flattered me by declaring that I should be certainly the favourite , and advised me to profit all I could by the masters he would provide .
Parsing [sent. 5502 len. 78]: In the mean time , Osman Ali having heard from the women the message I had sent , was very wroth , and came to the slave-merchant to procure me again ; but the slave-merchant informed him that the kislar aga of the sultan had seen me , and ordered me to be reserved for the imperial seraglio ; by this falsehood screening himself , not only from Ali 's importunities , but also from his vengeance .
Parsing [sent. 5503 len. 49]: I took the advice of my master , and in a little more than a year became a proficient in music and most other accomplishments ; I also learnt to write and read , and to repeat most of the verses of Hafiz , and other celebrated poets .
Parsing [sent. 5504 len. 17]: At seventeen I was offered to the kislar aga as a prodigy of beauty and talent .
Parsing [sent. 5505 len. 41]: The kislar aga came to see me , and was astonished ; he saw at once that I should immediately become first favourite ; and having heard me sing and play , he demanded my price , which was enormous .
Parsing [sent. 5506 len. 31]: He reported me to the sultan , stating that he had never beheld such perfection , and at the same time informing him of the exorbitant demand of the slave-merchant .
Parsing [sent. 5507 len. 41]: The sultan , who had lately felt little interest in the inmates of his harem , and was anxious for novelty , ordered the sum to be paid , and I was conducted to the seraglio in a royal litter .
Parsing [sent. 5508 len. 44]: That I was anxious to be purchased by the sultan I confess : my pride rebelled at the idea of being a slave , and if I was to be so , at least I wished to be the slave of the sultan .
Parsing [sent. 5509 len. 41]: I indulged the idea that I should soon bring him to subjection , and that the slave would lord it over her master , and that master the dispenser of life and death , honour and disgrace , to millions .
Parsing [sent. 5510 len. 22]: I had made up my mind how to behave ; the poets I had read had taught me but too well .
Parsing [sent. 5511 len. 36]: Convinced that a little wilfulness would , from its novelty , be most likely to captivate one who had been accustomed to dull and passive obedience , I allowed my natural temper to be unchecked .
Parsing [sent. 5512 len. 32]: The second day after my arrival , the kislar aga informed me that the sultan intended to honour me with a visit , and that the baths and dresses were prepared .
Parsing [sent. 5513 len. 49]: I replied that I had bathed that morning , and did not intend to bathe again -- as for the dresses and jewels , I did not require them , and that I was ready to receive my lord , the sultan , if he pleased to come .
Parsing [sent. 5514 len. 44]: The kislar aga opened his eyes with astonishment at my presumption ; but not venturing to use force to one who , in his opinion , would become the favourite , he returned to the sultan , reporting to him what had passed .
Parsing [sent. 5515 len. 21]: The sultan , as I expected , was more amused at the novelty than affronted at the want of respect .
Parsing [sent. 5516 len. 23]: `` Be it so , '' replied he , `` this Georgian must have a good opinion of her own charms . ''
Parsing [sent. 5517 len. 29]: In the evening the sultan made his appearance , and I prostrated myself at his feet , for I did not wish to proceed too far at once .
Parsing [sent. 5518 len. 9]: He raised me up , and appeared delighted .

''
Parsing [sent. 5522 len. 16]: The sultan was delighted at my apology , and I certainly was pleased with him .
Parsing [sent. 5523 len. 45]: He was then about forty years of age , very handsome and well made ; but I was still more gratified to find that my conversation amused him so much that he remained with me for many hours after his usual time for retiring .
Parsing [sent. 5524 len. 12]: This gave promise of an ascendancy which might survive personal charms .
Parsing [sent. 5525 len. 21]: But not to detain your highness , I will at once state , the sultan soon thought but of me .
Parsing [sent. 5526 len. 56]: Not only my personal attractions , but my infinite variety , which appeared natural , but was generally planned and sketched out previous to his visits , won so entirely upon him , that so far from being tired , his passion , I may say his love , for me was every day increased .
Parsing [sent. 5527 len. 26]: `` Well , it _ may be _ all true , '' observed the pacha , looking at the wrinkled and hideous object before him .
Parsing [sent. 5528 len. 9]: `` What do you say , Mustapha ? ''

Parsing [sent. 5536 len. 68]: Once sure of the sultan 's affections , I indulged myself in greater liberties -- not with him , but with others ; for I knew that he would laugh at the tricks I might play upon his dependants , but not be equally pleased with a want of respect towards himself ; and other people of the harem were the objects of my caprice and amusement .
Parsing [sent. 5537 len. 38]: So far from preventing him from noticing the other women in the harem , I would recommend them , and often have them in my apartments when he would visit me , and wish to be alone .
Parsing [sent. 5538 len. 19]: I generally contrived to manage a little quarrel about once a month , as it renewed his passion .
Parsing [sent. 5539 len. 33]: In short , the sultan became , as I intended , so infatuated , that he was my slave , and at the same time I felt an ardent attachment to him .
Parsing [sent. 5540 len. 6]: My power was well known .

Parsing [sent. 5542 len. 17]: This indifference on my part to what women are usually too fond of increased his regard .

Parsing [sent. 5545 len. 8]: I speak not of the present . ''

Parsing [sent. 5547 len. 26]: The queen mother , and the kislar aga , both of whom I had affronted , were indefatigable in their attempts to undermine my power .

Parsing [sent. 5557 len. 11]: Men will be fickle , and I expected no otherwise .

Parsing [sent. 5708 len. 72]: A Georgian slave who had been the favourite previous to my arrival , and who had never forgiven my supplanting her , had been sent to him by the sultan as a compliment ; and this rare distinction had been conferred upon him on the day when I requested leave to remain behind the screen in the hall of the divan , that I might behold this celebrated and distinguished person .

Parsing [sent. 5721 len. 21]: My brother had so often led the troops to victory , that he had acquired an unbounded sway over them .

Parsing [sent. 5723 len. 46]: To his new wife , the Georgian , he had entrusted his plans , and she resolved to regain the favour of the sultan and accomplish my ruin by making me a party , and then communicating to him the treason which was in agitation .
Parsing [sent. 5724 len. 52]: She proposed to my brother that he should inform me of his intentions , alleging , that in all probability I would assist him , as I cared little for the sultan ; and at all events if I did not join , my interest might save him from his wrath .

Parsing [sent. 5726 len. 21]: My brother had been allowed to visit me , and he took it opportunity of stating to me his schemes .
