Parsing [sent. 5810 len. 20]: One evening I felt sufficiently recovered to speak , and I demanded of my attendants what had taken place .
Parsing [sent. 5811 len. 91]: They informed me that the mutes , who had mistaken the signal , had been impaled , and that the janissaries had risen and demanded my brother , whose execution had been deferred by the sultan ; but that on the commotion taking place , by order of the grand vizier , my brother had been executed , and his head thrown out to the rebellious troops , who had then dispersed , and had since been brought to subjection , and some hundreds of their ringleaders had been executed .
Parsing [sent. 5812 len. 16]: I turned away at this intelligence , for I loved my noble but misguided brother .
Parsing [sent. 5813 len. 20]: The movement occasioned excruciating pain , which arose from the deep wound made by the bowstring in my neck .
Parsing [sent. 5814 len. 28]: The next morning I rose , that I might contemplate my person in the mirror , and I at once perceived the alteration which had taken place .
Parsing [sent. 5815 len. 17]: There was a certain degree of distortion of features which I thought would never be removed .
Parsing [sent. 5816 len. 24]: I felt , that although the sultan might respect me , I could not expect the same influence and undivided attention as before .
Parsing [sent. 5817 len. 17]: With a heavy heart I threw myself on the couch , and planned for the future .
Parsing [sent. 5818 len. 22]: I reflected upon the uncertain tenure by which the affections of a despot are held -- and I resolved to part .
Parsing [sent. 5819 len. 20]: Still I loved him , loved him in spite of all his cruelty ; but my resolution was made .
Parsing [sent. 5820 len. 22]: For six weeks I refused to see the sultan , although he inquired every day , and sent me magnificent presents .
Parsing [sent. 5821 len. 48]: At the end of that period I had recovered , and all that remained from the effects of the bowstring , was a slight wrinkling of the skin from distension , and the deep blue mark round my neck which I have just shown to your highness .
Parsing [sent. 5822 len. 12]: When I first admitted the sultan , he was much affected .
Parsing [sent. 5823 len. 25]: `` Zara , '' said he mournfully , `` I swear by the holy Prophet that I meant not to give the signal . ''
Parsing [sent. 5824 len. 13]: `` I believe you , my lord , '' replied I calmly .
Parsing [sent. 5825 len. 11]: `` Neither did I intend that your brother should suffer .
Parsing [sent. 5826 len. 12]: I meant to have gained your favour by his pardon . ''
Parsing [sent. 5827 len. 18]: `` He was a traitor , my lord , an ungrateful traitor , and deserved his death .
Parsing [sent. 5828 len. 8]: So may all like him perish . ''
Parsing [sent. 5829 len. 14]: `` And now , Zara , may I hope for your forgiveness ? ''
Parsing [sent. 5830 len. 18]: `` On one condition , sultan , and swear that you will grant what I require . ''
Parsing [sent. 5831 len. 8]: `` I do , by Allah ! ''
Parsing [sent. 5832 len. 15]: `` It is , that you send me back to my own country . ''
Parsing [sent. 5833 len. 40]: Not to detain your highness by dwelling too long upon what passed , it will suffice to say , that notwithstanding the intreaties of the sultan , and the pleadings of my own heart , my resolution was immovable .
Parsing [sent. 5834 len. 27]: Every arrangement was made for my departure , and during the preparations , the sultan was continually with me , persuading me to abandon the idea .
Parsing [sent. 5835 len. 38]: The magnificence and liberality which he showed in the costly presents bestowed upon me , that I might return with honour and wealth to my own country , more than once made me waver in my resolution .
Parsing [sent. 5836 len. 15]: The evening before my departure he made a last attempt , but in vain .
Parsing [sent. 5837 len. 37]: My refusal was at least softened by the tears which I shed , for now that the time of departure was so near , I felt how truly , how devotedly I was attached to him .
Parsing [sent. 5838 len. 27]: We parted ; I threw myself on the couch , and wept till the dawn of day , when I was summoned to commence my journey .
Parsing [sent. 5839 len. 31]: As your highness may be aware is the custom , when my brother was executed , all his property was seized by the sultan , and distributed among the favourites .
Parsing [sent. 5840 len. 21]: The new capitan pacha who succeeded my brother was called Abdallah , and was said to be an excellent soldier .
Parsing [sent. 5841 len. 37]: Part of my brother 's property was made over to him , and among the rest the Georgian slave , who had been the ruin of my brother , and had so fatally destroyed my happiness .
Parsing [sent. 5842 len. 30]: To show me every attention and respect , the sultan had ordered Abdallah in person to escort me to my own country , with a picked body of cavalry .
Parsing [sent. 5843 len. 44]: The cavalcade was magnificent -- treasure had been heaped on treasure -- present upon present ; twenty women of my own country , and numerous slaves had been permitted to attend upon me , and the procession wore the appearance of a pageant .
Parsing [sent. 5844 len. 24]: I ascended my litter with an aching heart ; and , journeying by easy stages , arrived at the land of my nativity .
Parsing [sent. 5845 len. 31]: The borders were passed , and Abdallah requested me to write an acknowledgment that he had done his duty , which the sultan would require of him upon his return .
Parsing [sent. 5846 len. 44]: I gave him the paper ; and , professing many wishes for my future happiness , he assembled his troops , and the escort turned the heads of their neighing steeds towards the city , where my heart had truly been left behind .
Parsing [sent. 5847 len. 32]: It will now be necessary to revert to the Georgian slave , who had been presented to my brother by the sultan , and had afterwards been made over to Abdallah .
Parsing [sent. 5848 len. 24]: When she heard that I was about to depart for my own country , loaded with presents , her rage was without bounds .
Parsing [sent. 5849 len. 46]: Already had her beauty and talents made great impression upon Abdallah , and she soon won him over to a plot which would be advantageous to him , at the same time that it would throw me , whom he distrusted , into her power .
Parsing [sent. 5850 len. 64]: She proposed to Abdallah that , after having escorted me to the frontiers , and received from me the acknowledgment required by the sultan , he should follow my small escort of slaves , cut them to pieces , take possession of me and all my treasure , and return with it to Constantinople , where I might be immured in his harem .
Parsing [sent. 5851 len. 36]: The avarice of Abdallah was not able to withstand the temptation ; and , aware that there was no chance of the nefarious transaction being discovered by the sultan , he agreed to the proposal .
Parsing [sent. 5852 len. 32]: On the second night after we had parted with Abdallah , a body of horsemen galloped down upon us , and all my attendants , male and female , were massacred .
Parsing [sent. 5853 len. 33]: I was seized , put into a sack , and thrown across a horse ; and as soon as the treasure could be collected , they set off at a rapid pace .
Parsing [sent. 5854 len. 21]: I was nearly dead when they halted , and when I was removed from my painful situation I fainted away .
Parsing [sent. 5855 len. 40]: Abdallah had never seen my face ; the soldiers reported me dead , and he was glad when he heard of it , for it was only to please his wife that he had promised to bring me back .
Parsing [sent. 5856 len. 22]: He walked up to where I lay , and was , even in my miserable situation , enamoured with my beauty .
Parsing [sent. 5857 len. 14]: His heart acknowledged that I was the most valuable of all his plunder .
Parsing [sent. 5858 len. 36]: Every care and attention was bestowed upon me ; and after several hours ' halt , to allow me to refresh myself , I was placed in a small litter , and our journey recommenced .
Parsing [sent. 5859 len. 53]: He was studious to obtain my favour : at first I spurned him , but when he told me that the Georgian slave had instigated him to the deed , and had insisted that he should bring me back , I well knew for what purpose , and thought only of revenge .
Parsing [sent. 5860 len. 27]: I feigned to be less averse to him , and before our journey was over , had used all my powers of fascination with triumphant success .
Parsing [sent. 5861 len. 49]: At last our wearied horses arrived at Stamboul , and after waiting in the suburbs till the evening closed in , that the cavalcade might not attract attention , it proceeded to the house of Abdallah , and I was once more in the precincts of a harem .
Parsing [sent. 5862 len. 41]: The Georgian slave hastened to meet me , when she was informed of our arrival , and taking off her slipper , she struck me contemptuously on the mouth , with such force as to cause the blood to flow .
Parsing [sent. 5863 len. 21]: `` Now sultana , '' cried she , `` the day is mine ; again shall you receive the bastinado .
Parsing [sent. 5864 len. 21]: Ay , and again shall the bowstring be applied to your proud neck -- and more effectually than before . ''
Parsing [sent. 5865 len. 16]: She then ordered her slaves to strip me , and put on the meanest attire .
Parsing [sent. 5866 len. 36]: When that was done , she spat in my face , and left me without speaking ; but the flashing of her eyes gave evidence of the fiery passions which were raging in her bosom .
Parsing [sent. 5867 len. 36]: In the mean time Abdallah had proceeded to the palace , to present to the sultan the document proving my safe arrival , and having so done , he hastened back to his own house .

Parsing [sent. 5870 len. 20]: He entered , and found me clothed in a slave 's dress , with my face covered with blood .
Parsing [sent. 5871 len. 27]: When I stated the treatment I had received , and the further threat of the bastinado and the bowstring , his rage was beyond all bounds .

Parsing [sent. 5873 len. 28]: My desire for revenge induced me to grant his request , and he quitted the harem to look after the treasure of which I had been robbed .

Parsing [sent. 5876 len. 32]: He was admitted , and again expressed his indignation at the conduct of my rival , offering , as a proof of his attachment , to abandon her to my resentment .

Parsing [sent. 5881 len. 8]: She has sealed her own doom . ''

Parsing [sent. 5883 len. 25]: My revenge was more than satiated , and I covered up my eyes that I might not be a witness to the dreadful spectacle .
Parsing [sent. 5884 len. 25]: When I removed my hands , I found Abdallah only in the apartment , and my rival lying a blackened corpse upon the floor .
Parsing [sent. 5885 len. 23]: For three years I remained in the harem of Abdallah ; and , if not happy , was resigned to my fate .
Parsing [sent. 5886 len. 23]: He was devotedly attached to me , and , if I could not return his love , was not deficient in gratitude .
Parsing [sent. 5887 len. 40]: At last a second war broke out between the Turks and Russians , and Abdallah was ordered to put himself at the head of his troops , and drive the invaders back to their regions of frost and snow .
Parsing [sent. 5888 len. 58]: As was the custom with Turkish commanders , all his harem accompanied him , and after travelling about from one territory to another , sometimes in pursuit of , and at others retreating before the enemy 's forces , we were shut up in the fortress of Ismael , with orders to defend it to the last .
Parsing [sent. 5889 len. 13]: I shall not weary your highness with a detail of what occurred .
Parsing [sent. 5890 len. 44]: I shall only say , that after the town had been nearly reduced to ashes , by the shells and shot , which had set fire to it at least one hundred times , it was taken by storm , with immense slaughter .
Parsing [sent. 5891 len. 56]: We sat in our apartments , listening with terror to the alternate shouting and shrieking -- the noise of the bursting of the shells , the whizzing of the balls , the cries of the wounded , and the terrific roaring of the flames , which were now consuming the whole town in their fury .
Parsing [sent. 5892 len. 13]: At last our doors were burst open , and the enemy entered .
Parsing [sent. 5893 len. 12]: We screamed , and would have fled , but in vain .
Parsing [sent. 5894 len. 35]: What became of the rest I know not , but I was dragged over the dead and the dying , through smoke and through flame , until I fainted away with terror and exhaustion .
Parsing [sent. 5895 len. 31]: When I recovered , I found myself in a hut , lying on a small bed , and attended by two bearded monsters , whom I afterwards discovered were Cossacks .

Parsing [sent. 5898 len. 30]: I discovered that evening that I had , by the fortune of war , become the property of a Russian general , who had no time for making love .
Parsing [sent. 5899 len. 14]: With him it was all ready made , as a matter of course .
Parsing [sent. 5900 len. 39]: Still he was a handsome man , and when not tipsy , was good-humoured and generous ; but the bivouacs , even of a general , were very different from the luxuries to which I had been accustomed .
Parsing [sent. 5901 len. 9]: I lived badly , and was housed worse .
Parsing [sent. 5902 len. 46]: It so unfortunately happened , that my protector was a great gambler , as indeed are all Russians ; and one morning to my surprise , a handsome young officer came into the tent , and the general very unceremoniously handed me over to him .
Parsing [sent. 5903 len. 36]: My beauty had been made known in the camp , and the Russian general , having the night before lost all his money , had staked me for one thousand sequins , and had lost .
Parsing [sent. 5904 len. 54]: My new master was a careless , handsome youth , a colonel in the army ; I could have loved him , but I had not time ; for I had not been in his tent more than three weeks , before I was again gambled away , and lost to a major .
Parsing [sent. 5905 len. 21]: I had hardly time to make myself comfortable in my new abode , when I was staked and lost again .
Parsing [sent. 5906 len. 84]: In short , your highness , in that campaign I was the property of between forty and fifty Russian officers ; and what with the fatigue of marching , the badness of provisions , and my constant unsettled state of mind and body , I lost much of my good looks -- so much , indeed , that I found out that instead of being taken as a stake of one thousand sequins , I was not valued at more than two hundred .
Parsing [sent. 5907 len. 40]: I can assure your highness that it is no joke to go through a Russian camp in that way -- to be handed about like a purse of money , out of one man 's pocket into another 's .
Parsing [sent. 5908 len. 42]: I assure you , that before the campaign was over , I had had quite enough of the Russians , and only wished that the Turkish army might rout them , and I could find myself once more in a harem .
Parsing [sent. 5909 len. 18]: It was then that I first lamented over my hard fate , and that of the sultan .
Parsing [sent. 5910 len. 31]: It was then that I first used the expression , when I thought of my condition , and that I said to myself , `` The time has been . ''
Parsing [sent. 5911 len. 66]: At last the army was ordered to march back , and being then the property of a Cossack , he put me on a pony , and made me keep up with the squadron , driving me before him with his long spear , sometimes sticking the point into the rear of the pony , and sometimes into me , by way of a joke .
Parsing [sent. 5912 len. 70]: But I had not been more than ten days on the retreat , before he sold me , pony , bridle , saddle , altogether , as a bargain , to an infantry officer , who , as soon as he had taken possession , made me dismount , while he got in the saddle , desiring me to lay hold of the pony 's tail and follow him .
Parsing [sent. 5913 len. 18]: When they halted he made me wait upon him , and do every thing which he required .
Parsing [sent. 5914 len. 18]: In the morning he mounted again , and I had to walk after him , as before .
Parsing [sent. 5915 len. 15]: This was hard service for one who had been the favourite of the sultan .
Parsing [sent. 5916 len. 20]: For a week I contrived to hobble after him , but it was impossible to go on any longer .
Parsing [sent. 5917 len. 39]: We passed through a town , and as soon as we were clear of the gates and he did not watch me , I let go the tail of the pony , and escaped without his perceiving it .
Parsing [sent. 5918 len. 21]: I regained the town , and faint with hunger and fatigue , sat at the steps of a large house .
Parsing [sent. 5919 len. 31]: A lady , dressed in rich furs and sables , came out , and perceiving that my dress was foreign , stopped , and inquired of me who I was .

Parsing [sent. 5921 len. 18]: A few days afterwards she sent for me , and I then narrated to her my history .
Parsing [sent. 5922 len. 27]: She was kind and generous , and I became her head attendant ; I was contented and happy , and hoped to die in her service .
Parsing [sent. 5923 len. 8]: But my misfortunes were not half over .
Parsing [sent. 5924 len. 12]: My mistress was a lady of rank , and much esteemed .
Parsing [sent. 5925 len. 18]: Her house was always full of company : she was rich , and gave most splendid entertainments .
Parsing [sent. 5926 len. 20]: Her husband had been dead about two years , but she was still very young , and exceedingly beautiful .

Parsing [sent. 5935 len. 8]: God knows how it may end . ''
Parsing [sent. 5936 len. 37]: I immediately consented -- packed up what we required , and without disturbing those who were enjoying themselves we gained the court-yard , and took our seats in a britska , in company with the officer .
Parsing [sent. 5937 len. 20]: In four days we arrived at Petersburgh , and my mistress was separated from me and thrown into prison .

Parsing [sent. 5939 len. 9]: For three weeks my mistress remained in prison .

Parsing [sent. 5942 len. 24]: `` Ekaterina , '' said she , at last , `` I have heard my sentence , and am to be punished to-morrow .

Parsing [sent. 5945 len. 10]: We raised her , and she recovered a little .

Parsing [sent. 5947 len. 5]: -- worse than death .
Parsing [sent. 5948 len. 16]: The knout -- the knout -- and that attended with public exposure in the market-place .
Parsing [sent. 5949 len. 9]: May God forgive the emperor his cruelty ! ''
Parsing [sent. 5950 len. 17]: I had heard of this dreadful punishment , but little thought that women suffered by it .
Parsing [sent. 5951 len. 5]: It was too barbarous .

Parsing [sent. 5956 len. 25]: My dear mistress begged me , as a favour , that I would attend her to the place of execution , and I consented .
Parsing [sent. 5957 len. 3]: Poor creature !
Parsing [sent. 5958 len. 19]: she , as well as I , had but an imperfect idea of what she was to endure .

Parsing [sent. 5960 len. 28]: She appeared on the raised platform upon which she was to suffer , in a genteel undress , which contributed still more to heighten her extreme beauty .
Parsing [sent. 5961 len. 28]: The sweetness of her countenance obtained for her the commiseration of those who were ordered and accustomed to execute the will of the despotic and cruel emperor .
Parsing [sent. 5962 len. 57]: Young , lively , and admired , sought for , and caressed by every body , high in rank , and rich in , worldly wealth , she stood , no longer surrounded by the attentions and homage due to her talents , her beauty , and her wit , but surrounded only by stern executioners .

Parsing [sent. 5966 len. 74]: One of the executioners then seized her by both hands , and turning half round , threw her on his back , bending forwards , so as to raise her feet a few inches from the ground , and the other executioner , with his rough hands , and without symptoms of remorse , adjusted her on the back of his companion in a posture most convenient for her to receive her punishment .
Parsing [sent. 5967 len. 45]: Sometimes he pressed his large hands brutally upon her head , in order to make her keep it down ; at others , like a butcher handling a lamb , he appeared to soothe her until he had fixed her in a favourable attitude .
Parsing [sent. 5968 len. 122]: He then took the knout , a whip made of a long strip of leather , prepared for the purpose ; he retreated a few steps , measuring the requisite distance with a steady eye , and looking backwards , gave a stroke with the end of the whip , so as to carry away a slip of skin from the neck to the bottom of the back ; then striking his feet against the ground , he took his aim for a second blow , parallel to the former , so that in a few moments all the skin of her back was cut away in small slips , most of which remained hanging to her shift and dress below .
Parsing [sent. 5969 len. 11]: I fainted with horror long before the punishment was over .
Parsing [sent. 5970 len. 5]: `` Good heavens ! ''
Parsing [sent. 5971 len. 21]: thought I , `` I have suffered the bastinado and the bowstring , but both were merciful compared to this .
Parsing [sent. 5972 len. 13]: Is there no God in heaven to punish such despotic cruelty ? ''
Parsing [sent. 5973 len. 42]: My mistress was not dead , and the surgeons were ordered to pay her every attention , that she might recover ; and I thought this attention on the part of the emperor in some measure made amends for his barbarity .
Parsing [sent. 5974 len. 6]: But , God in heaven !
Parsing [sent. 5975 len. 38]: she was restored to life that she might be more cruelly punished ; for no sooner was she able to bear this infliction , than they cut out her tongue , and then banished her to Siberia .
Parsing [sent. 5976 len. 5]: Thus , O pacha !
Parsing [sent. 5977 len. 15]: was my beautiful mistress treated upon mere suspicion , for guilty she never was .
Parsing [sent. 5978 len. 79]: I had been permitted to see her previous to her latter punishment , and she fancied , poor thing , that the emperor 's wrath had been appeased , and that she would have been permitted to return home , but her tongue was cut out without her receiving any warning of the second punishment which awaited her , and after that I was refused admittance , and I never saw my beautiful and ill-treated mistress any more .
Parsing [sent. 5979 len. 34]: It was from the officer who had the charge of her that I learnt this cruel intelligence , and I went back to my lodgings with a heart bursting with grief and indignation .
Parsing [sent. 5980 len. 31]: I was resolved that , if possible , I would escape from a country where women 's tongues were cut out ; but how to manage it I knew not .
Parsing [sent. 5981 len. 45]: I had still some money and valuables , which had been left in my possession by my unfortunate mistress , and I made inquiry about the means of proceeding to Constantinople , where , at least , I should be in a civilised country .
Parsing [sent. 5982 len. 42]: At last a Jew , who heard that I wished to go to the southward , offered to take me with him as soon as the snow was on the ground , for which I bargained to pay five hundred roubles .
Parsing [sent. 5983 len. 20]: In a fortnight the winter had set in , and we got into a drotski , and went away .
Parsing [sent. 5984 len. 14]: We arrived at Moscow , and from thence we at last gained Constantinople .
Parsing [sent. 5985 len. 41]: On my arrival I selected my luggage , that I might pay the sum agreed ; but it was snatched from me by the old rascal , who saluted me with a kick in the body which half killed me .
Parsing [sent. 5986 len. 37]: I was locked up in a room , and in half an hour a slave merchant came , and I was sold for a low sum and taken away , remonstrating in vain against the injustice .
Parsing [sent. 5987 len. 21]: My beauty was now gone , I was more than thirty years old , and hardship had done the rest .
Parsing [sent. 5988 len. 14]: My subsequent life has been nothing but a series of changes and disasters .
Parsing [sent. 5989 len. 15]: I was sold to a pastry-cook , and broiled by standing over the oven .
Parsing [sent. 5990 len. 16]: I grew obstinate and was punished by blows , but for those I cared not .
Parsing [sent. 5991 len. 58]: The pastry was burnt , and I was resold to a barber , whose wife was a shrew , and half killed me ; fortunately the barber was accused of shaving a criminal , who had escaped from prison , and one morning was stretched out before his own door , with his head under his arm .
Parsing [sent. 5992 len. 11]: His wife and I were both sold again as slaves .
Parsing [sent. 5993 len. 36]: Thus did I go down hill each year , fetching less and less , and receiving worse treatment , until I was embarked with several others by an Armenian , who was bound to Smyrna .
Parsing [sent. 5994 len. 24]: The vessel was captured by an Algerine pirate , and for a long while I was kept on board to cook their victuals .
Parsing [sent. 5995 len. 23]: At last she was wrecked on this coast ; how I escaped I know not , for I was weary of life .
Parsing [sent. 5996 len. 33]: But I was thrown up , and made my way to this place -- where I have for many years lived in company with an old wretch like myself , supplicating alms .
Parsing [sent. 5997 len. 16]: He died about a year ago , and left me in the hovel by myself .
Parsing [sent. 5998 len. 37]: I still beg for my subsistence ; and now , pacha , you have my story , and I think you will acknowledge that I may well say that '' _ Time has been _ . ''
